1568 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with configuration capability (all profiles).

1569 NOTE: For boot managers deployed in critical systems or environments with elevated security requirements,
1570 manufacturers may consider requiring a combination of independent authentication mechanisms (e.g.
1571 physical presence combined with cryptographic credential verification) for trust anchor modifications.
1572 This defence-in-depth approach mitigates risks from compromise of a single authentication factor.

1573 5.6.2 [REQ-BM-AC-002]

1574 Requirement: The boot manager shall allow protection of configuration settings related to the boot process against
1575 unauthorised modification if configured.

1576 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with configuration capability (all profiles).

1577 NOTE 1: In embedded system scenarios, replacing or revoking trusted keys or certificates is often performed via
1578 authenticated software updates, without requiring physical presence.

1579 NOTE 2: Examples of configuration settings related to the boot process include:

1580 a) boot order;

1581 b) boot parameters;

1582 c) selection of boot targets or modes.

1583 5.6.3 [REQ-BM-AC-003]

1584 Requirement: The boot manager shall require explicit authentication before any modification of security-critical
1585 configuration settings.

1586 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with configuration capability (all profiles).

1587 NOTE: Examples of such actions include:

1588 a) weakening or disabling secure default settings;

1589 b) downgrading security-related configuration parameters;

1590 c) modifying security-critical options such as verification policies or trust anchors.

1591 5.6.4 [REQ-BM-AC-004]

1592 Requirement: When passwords are used for authentication, the boot manager shall throttle authentication attempts, for
1593 instance, by limiting attempts, increasing delays, or using cryptographic methods designed to be slow key derivation
1594 functions that are deliberately slow.

1595 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with configuration capability using password authentication (all security
1596 profiles).

1597 5.6.5 [REQ-BM-AC-005]

1598 Requirement: Where security configuration policies are provided as separate signed artefacts, the boot manager shall
1599 verify their authenticity and integrity before importing or enforcing them.

1600 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with verified or measured boot and configuration capability (MEDIUM or
1601 HIGH security profile).

1602 5.6.6 [REQ-BM-AC-006]

1603 Requirement: The boot manager shall indicate when running with non-default security-critical configuration through
1604 persistent visual indication or, where logging capability is supported, through logged events.


1605 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with configuration capability (all profiles).

1606 NOTE 1: The indication may be visual (when a user interface is available) or may consist of recorded events in
1607 secure logs.

1608 NOTE 2: Examples of indications include: a) a persistent on-screen message or icon; b) a status LED or display
1609 element; c) a logged event recorded in a secure audit log.

1610 5.6.7 [REQ-BM-AC-007]

1611 Requirement: The boot manager shall protect trusted certificate stores from unauthorised modification.

1612 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with verified or measured boot (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

1613 5.6.8 [REQ-BM-AC-008]

1614 Requirement: The boot manager shall be accompanied with documentation declaring its code execution authority
1615 model, including the mechanisms and entities that constitute it, their scope and relationships, the default state as placed
1616 on the market, any external dependencies of the mechanisms, and the processes by which the model can be changed
1617 where any aspect is mutable.

1618 Applicability: Applies to all boot managers (all security profiles).

1619 NOTE: Where no entity or mechanism has authority to decide which code can be executed, this is itself a
1620 declaration of the model and satisfies the requirement provided the documentation states it explicitly.

1621 5.6.9 [REQ-BM-AC-009]

1622 Requirement: For each authority transfer mechanism provided by the boot manager, the boot manager shall be
1623 accompanied with documentation declaring the entities that can initiate or approve the transfer, the components
1624 covered, and the permanence of the transfer.

1625 Applicability: Applies to boot managers that provide one or more authority transfer mechanisms.

1626 5.6.10 [REQ-BM-AC-010]

1627 Requirement: The boot manager shall be accompanied with documentation declaring how the integrator or a
1628 downstream party can verify whether a given piece of software is authorised to run on the boot manager, including the
1629 tools, public keys, or mechanisms required for that verification.

1630 Applicability: Applies to all boot managers (all security profiles).

1631 5.6.11 [REQ-BM-AC-011]

1632 Requirement: Any authority transfer initiated through a mechanism provided by the boot manager shall require explicit
1633 authorisation by the entity declared in the authority model as competent to authorise the transfer and shall not be
1634 performed as part of an automatic update or as a condition for continued operation.

1635 Applicability: Applies to boot managers that provide one or more authority transfer mechanisms.

1636 5.7 Confidentiality protection

1637 5.7.0 Introduction to confidentiality protection requirements

1638 This clause addresses the requirements in the CRA [i.1], Annex I, Part I, point (2)(e). Boot managers shall protect
1639 cryptographic key material, credentials, and security policies in resource-constrained environments against persistent
1640 physical access threats.


1641 5.7.1 [REQ-BM-CP-001]

1642 Requirement: The boot manager shall restrict access to cryptographic key material to authorised boot components as
1643 defined by the boot manager's security policy.

1644 Applicability: Applies to boot managers using cryptographic keys (all security profiles).

1645 5.7.2 [REQ-BM-CP-002]

1646 Requirement: Device-specific keys shall be used for symmetric verified boot operations. The use of global secret keys
1647 for verified boot purposes is explicitly forbidden.

1648 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with verified boot (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

1649 NOTE: Use of symmetric device-unique keys mitigates the risk of large-scale attacks resulting from compromise
1650 of a single global key.

1651 5.7.3 [REQ-BM-CP-003]

1652 Requirement: The boot manager shall prevent key material from being used for cryptographic purposes other than
1653 those for which it was designated.

1654 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with verified or measured boot (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

1655 5.7.4 [REQ-BM-CP-004]

1656 Requirement: The boot manager shall not place sensitive data in crash dumps or log.

1657 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with logging capability (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

1658 NOTE: Examples of sensitive data include:

1659 a) cryptographic key material;

1660 b) authentication credentials;

1661 c) security-critical configuration parameters;

1662 d) personal or otherwise confidential information managed during the boot process.

1663 5.7.5 [REQ-BM-CP-005]

1664 Requirement: The boot manager shall protect stored credentials using approved mechanisms that prevent recovery of
1665 the credential values. This does not include tokenised values or credentials.

1666 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with configuration and recovery capability (all security profiles).

1667 NOTE 1: Examples of protected credential types include user passwords, recovery keys, and other authentication
1668 secrets.

1669 NOTE 2: Examples of protection mechanisms include:

1670 a) key-derivation functions (e.g. salted password hashing);

1671 b) hardware-bound storage or sealed storage;

1672 c) encryption using keys not accessible to unauthorised entities;

1673 d) key-wrapping or secret-derivation schemes.


1674 5.7.6 [REQ-BM-CP-006]

1675 Requirement: The boot manager shall protect network boot parameters containing authentication information using
1676 approved mechanisms that prevent unauthorised disclosure.

1677 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with configuration capability and network boot (MEDIUM or HIGH security
1678 profile).

1679 5.7.7 [REQ-BM-CP-007]

1680 Requirement: The boot manager shall cryptographically erase all data possessed by boot manager and clear all
1681 security-critical configuration during secure disposal, where technically feasible (see note).

1682 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with verified or measured boot and configuration capability that implement
1683 secure disposal (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

1684 NOTE: When cryptographic material or sensitive data are stored in immutable components such as e-fuses or
1685 ROM, complete erasure may not be possible.

1686 5.7.8 [REQ-BM-CP-008]

1687 Requirement: When secure disposal is supported, the boot manager shall provide a secure response upon successful
1688 completion of the sanitisation process.

1689 Applicability: Applies to boot managers that implement secure disposal (all security profiles).

1690 5.7.9 [REQ-BM-CP-009]

1691 Requirement: The boot manager shall support protecting the confidentiality and integrity of boot configuration data
1692 transmitted over the network using secure methods or secure alternatives.

1693 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with network boot (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

1694 5.7.10 [REQ-BM-CP-010]

1695 Requirement: The boot manager shall clear confidential or unprotected sensitive data after use, clear from memory
1696 credentials and temporary data structures containing such before boot target handoff and not persist authentication
1697 credentials or confidential cryptographic material beyond the operating system handoff. The measurements and
1698 credentials used for attestation shall persist.

1699 Applicability: Applies to all boot managers (all security profiles).

1700 NOTE 1: Examples of unprotected sensitive data include authentication credentials, unsalted passwords,
1701 cryptographic key material, and temporary data structures created during the boot process.

1702 NOTE 2: Examples of mechanisms for removing sensitive data include: a) overwriting sensitive data after use; b)
1703 clearing temporary data structures and credentials before handing off control to the boot target; c)
1704 avoiding persistence of authentication credentials or cryptographic material beyond the operating system
1705 handoff.

1706 5.8 Integrity protection

1707 5.8.0 Introduction to integrity protection requirements

1708 This clause addresses the requirements in the CRA [i.1], Annex I, Part I, point (2)(f). Boot managers establish trust
1709 chains through cryptographic verification, measurement, and protection mechanisms that resist component substitution,
1710 rollback, and TOCTOU attacks.


1711 5.8.1 [REQ-BM-INT-001]

1712 Requirement: The boot manager shall enforce privilege boundaries so that code executed in one boot stage cannot
1713 obtain privileges assigned to another boot stage or cross established trust boundaries.

1714 Applicability: Applies to all boot managers (all security profiles).

1715 NOTE: Examples of privilege boundaries include:

1716 a) restrictions on access to memory regions;

1717 b) restrictions on execution of privileged instructions;

1718 c) limitations on access to security-sensitive hardware resources.

1719 5.8.2 [REQ-BM-INT-002]

1720 Requirement: The boot manager shall verify integrity and authenticity of each boot stage using approved
1721 cryptographic mechanisms as defined in Annex K and shall establish a chain of trust to a root trust anchor before
1722 transferring control.

1723 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with on-boot verification (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

1724 5.8.3 [REQ-BM-INT-003]

1725 Requirement: The boot manager shall prevent boot continuation with components that fail integrity or authenticity
1726 verification.

1727 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with on-boot verification (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

1728 NOTE 1: Examples of verification failures include:

1729 a) invalid, expired, or revoked cryptographic credentials;

1730 b) substituted or tampered components;

1731 c) missing or untrusted verification data.

1732 NOTE 2: Cryptographic verification mechanisms may include digital signatures, message authentication codes
1733 (MACs), or other approved methods providing equivalent assurance.

1734 5.8.4 [REQ-BM-INT-004]

1735 Requirement: The boot manager shall compute and record a cryptographic measurement of each boot stage into
1736 hardware-protected storage before transferring control, establishing a measurement chain rooted in a hardware-based
1737 trust anchor.

1738 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with measured boot (all security profiles).

1739 NOTE 1: Unlike verified boot, measured boot does not prevent execution of unverified components. Instead, it
1740 provides an attestable record that enables a remote or local verifier to determine whether the boot
1741 sequence matches expected values.

1742 NOTE 2: Measurement mechanisms may include:

1743 a) extending hash values into hardware-protected registers (e.g. TPM PCRs);

1744 b) deriving compound device identifiers (e.g. DICE CDI);

1745 c) recording measurements in other tamper-evident storage.

1746 NOTE 3: The integrity of the measurement chain depends on the trustworthiness of the initial measurement by the
1747 hardware root of trust and the correct extension of measurements at each subsequent stage


1748 5.8.5 [REQ-BM-INT-005]

1749 Requirement: The boot manager shall verify authenticity and integrity of update packages before installation, and
1750 additionally after the receipt of content where updates are written to protected storage.

1751 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with update capability where the boot manager performs on-update
1752 verification (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

1753 5.8.6 [REQ-BM-INT-006]

1754 Requirement: The boot manager shall implement software-based cryptographic verification with keys loaded from
1755 protected storage.

1756 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with verified boot when hardware security components are unavailable
1757 (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

1758 5.8.7 [REQ-BM-INT-007]

1759 Requirement: The boot manager shall support configuration among a set of approved signing algorithms.

1760 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with verified boot and with configuration capability, where the trust anchor is
1761 not immutable (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

1762 NOTE: A set of length one is acceptable. The requirement establishes the capability to substitute one approved
1763 algorithm for another, e.g. when an algorithm becomes deprecated.

1764 5.8.8 [REQ-BM-INT-008]

1765 Requirement: The boot manager shall support combined verification using more than one approved signing algorithm.

1766 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with verified boot and with configuration capability, where the trust anchor is
1767 not immutable (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

1768 5.8.9 [REQ-BM-INT-009]

1769 Requirement: The boot manager shall use a design that prevents TOCTOU attacks within its documented threat model.

1770 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with verified boot capability (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

1771 NOTE: Threats addressed by this requirement are those identified in the security analysis (Annex B) for the
1772 declared use case. Physical-attack TOCTOU on the boot medium (T-PHYS-5, T-PHYS-6) is addressed
1773 under Annex D and is not within the scope of this requirement.

1774 5.8.10 [REQ-BM-INT-010]

1775 Requirement: The boot manager shall load components into protected memory before verification, when supported by
1776 the underlying hardware platform.

1777 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with verified boot (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

1778 5.8.11 [REQ-BM-INT-011]

1779 Requirement: The boot manager shall protect the integrity and authenticity of sensitive configuration settings.

1780 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with configuration capability (all profiles).

1781 NOTE: Mechanisms that protect the integrity and authenticity of sensitive configuration settings may include
1782 hardware-protected storage, or authenticated encryption with freshness protection (e.g. nonces or
1783 monotonic counters) and non-deterministic encryption.


1784 5.8.12 [REQ-BM-INT-012]

1785 Requirement: The boot manager shall restore secure default configuration settings when configuration corruption is
1786 detected, where technically feasible.

1787 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with configuration capability (all profiles).

1788 NOTE: When cryptographic material or configuration data are stored in immutable components such as e-fuses or
1789 ROM, complete erasure or restoration may not be possible.

1790 5.8.13 [REQ-BM-INT-013]

1791 Requirement: The boot manager shall authenticate network boot servers using cryptographic certificates before
1792 accepting actions or configuration data from the network boot server.

1793 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with network boot (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

1794 5.8.14 [REQ-BM-INT-014]

1795 Requirement: The boot manager shall reject network boot connections with invalid, or revoked server certificates.

1796 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with network boot (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

1797 NOTE: Expiration checking of cryptographic credentials is conditional on a dependable source of time being
1798 available to the boot manager (see assumption in clause B.3.2). Where no dependable source of time is
1799 available, the boot manager cannot perform expiration checking; revocation checking remains applicable.

1800 5.8.15 [REQ-BM-INT-015]

1801 Requirement: The boot manager shall verify that network configuration and boot-related responses originate from
1802 authorised infrastructure.

1803 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with network boot (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

1804 NOTE: Examples of network configuration and boot-related responses include:

1805 a) DHCP responses;

1806 b) PXE boot offers;

1807 c) network-provided boot configuration data.

1808 5.8.16 [REQ-BM-INT-016]

1809 Requirement: The boot manager shall enforce rollback protection when verifying boot stages and configuration data.

1810 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with update or configuration capability (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

1811 NOTE: In some business models, anti-rollback protection can be configured by the OEM. Refer to note in
1812 clause 5.3.

1813 5.8.17 [REQ-BM-INT-017]

1814 Requirement: The boot manager shall store anti-rollback counters in hardware-backed or tamper-evident storage and
1815 verify signed version metadata before accepting updates.

1816 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with HIGH security profile and update capability.


1817 5.8.18 [REQ-BM-INT-018]

1818 Requirement: The boot manager shall implement anti-rollback mechanisms and verify signed version metadata before
1819 accepting updates.

1820 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with verified boot and measured boot, where measured boot includes remote
1821 attestation (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

1822 NOTE: Certificate-chain verification may include checking:

1823 a) the full chain of trust from the end-entity certificate to the trusted root;

1824 b) certificate validity periods;

1825 c) revocation status through mechanisms such as CRLs or OCSP;

1826 d) compliance with certificate policies or usage constraint.

1827 5.8.19 [REQ-BM-INT-019]

1828 Requirement: The boot manager shall support revocation of mutable compromised keys and certificates.

1829 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with verified boot and measured boot, where measured boot includes remote
1830 attestation (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

1831 NOTE 1: In boot managers without connectivity capability, revocation can either be managed manually (e.g. via
1832 dedicated tools or physical programming) or through authenticated software updates.

1833 NOTE 2: In many embedded systems, the number of revocation slots (especially for verified boot) is limited by
1834 available storage or hardware design. For this reason the number of possible key revocations may be
1835 constrained.

1836 NOTE 3: Revocation mechanisms may include:

1837 a) a revocation database;

1838 b) configuration or policy updates;

1839 c) certificate revocation lists (CRLs);

1840 d) online or offline status information (e.g. OCSP responses);

1841 e) manufacturer- or owner-provided revocation metadata.

1842 5.8.20 [REQ-BM-INT-020]

1843 Requirement: The boot manager shall use cryptographic algorithms, key sizes, and parameters in accordance with
1844 Annex K.

1845 Applicability: Applies to all boot managers (all security profiles).

1846 5.8.21 [REQ-BM-INT-021]

1847 Requirement: The boot manager shall support migration between approved cryptographic algorithms.

1848 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with update capability, where the trust anchor is not immutable (MEDIUM or
1849 HIGH security profile).

1850 NOTE: Migration may be achieved through configuration metadata, controlled algorithm selection mechanisms,
1851 or replacement of the boot manager itself, in alignment with the update capability declared in
1852 clause 4.2.3.2.


1853 5.8.22 [REQ-BM-INT-022]

1854 Requirement: The boot manager shall use collision- and preimage-resistant one-way functions for origin authentication
1855 and verification of boot code provenance.

1856 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with verified or measured boot capability (MEDIUM or HIGH security
1857 profile).

1858 NOTE 1: Examples of collision- and preimage-resistant one-way functions include SHA-2 and SHA-3.

1859 NOTE 2: Non-collision-resistant hashes (e.g. GHASH in AES-GCM) may be used for integrity protection only
1860 when combined with device-specific keys.

1861 5.8.23 [REQ-BM-INT-023]

1862 Requirement: The boot manager shall support replacement of trust anchors used for boot verification.

1863 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with update capability, where the trust anchor is not immutable (MEDIUM or
1864 HIGH security profile).

1865 NOTE: Trust anchor replacement supports recovery from key compromise and aligns with the key provisioning
1866 capability declared in clause 4.2.3.10.

1867 5.8.24 [REQ-BM-INT-024]

1868 Requirement: The boot manager shall protect the storage in which trust anchors, key enrolment records, and policy
1869 database contents used by the code execution authority are held against modification by unauthorised entities.

1870 Applicability: Applies to boot managers that implement one or more code execution authority mechanisms requiring
1871 stored authority data.

1872 5.9 Data minimisation

1873 5.9.0 Introduction to data minimisation requirements

1874 This clause addresses the requirements in the CRA [i.1], Annex I, Part I, point (2)(g). Boot managers shall process only
1875 data necessary for boot operations, security verification, and error indication, given memory and storage constraints.

1876 5.9.1 [REQ-BM-DM-001]

1877 Requirement: The boot manager shall minimise disclosure of information to network infrastructure by limiting
1878 transmitted data to what is necessary for boot operations.

1879 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with network boot (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

1880 NOTE: Examples of measures to minimise network disclosure include:

1881 a) requesting only the files required for the network boot process;

1882 b) negotiating only protocol parameters essential for establishing the boot session;

1883 c) restricting identifiers exposed on the network (e.g. to MAC address and device class).

1884 5.9.2 [REQ-BM-DM-002]

1885 Requirement: The boot manager shall prevent disclosure of sensitive device information on the network and shall
1886 ensure that temporary network credentials are not retained beyond their required use.


1887 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with network boot (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

1888 NOTE: Examples of sensitive device information that should not be disclosed include:

1889 a) hardware serial numbers;

1890 b) internal configuration or diagnostic data.

1891 5.10 Availability protection

1892 5.10.0 Introduction to availability protection requirements

1893 This clause addresses the requirements in the CRA [i.1], Annex I, Part I, point (2)(h). Boot managers shall maintain
1894 availability during failures or attacks through recovery mechanisms, failsafe operations, and resistance to
1895 denial-of-service conditions. Where this clause specifies limits without numeric values, the manufacturer shall
1896 document specific thresholds in security documentation per Annex C.

1897 5.10.1 [REQ-BM-AP-001]

1898 Requirement: The boot manager shall support fallback to previous known-good configuration.

1899 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with configuration capability (all profiles).

1900 5.10.2 [REQ-BM-AP-002]

1901 Requirement: The boot manager shall be able to automatically recover from any interruptions during the update
1902 process.

1903 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with HIGH security profile.

1904 5.10.3 [REQ-BM-AP-003]

1905 Requirement: The boot manager shall enforce timeouts to prevent indefinite blocking during boot-related operations.

1906 Applicability: Applies to all boot managers (all security profiles).

1907 NOTE: Examples of operations that may require timeouts include:

1908 a) parsing or validation of configuration data;

1909 b) network discovery, negotiation, or file retrieval;

1910 c) loading or verifying boot components.

1911 5.10.4 [REQ-BM-AP-004]

1912 Requirement: The boot manager shall limit retry attempts and resource consumption for signature verification and
1913 network operations.

1914 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with verified boot or network boot (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

1915 5.10.5 [REQ-BM-AP-005]

1916 Requirement: The boot manager shall prevent unauthorised bypass of security verification steps during normal
1917 operation.

1918 Applicability: Applies to all boot managers (all security profiles).

1919 NOTE: In specific, controlled scenarios such as in-field debug mode, disabling security verification steps may be
1920 permitted for issue analysis, provided that such actions are strictly authenticated.


1921 5.10.6 [REQ-BM-AP-006]

1922 Requirement: The boot manager shall detect errors in critical data (e.g. cryptographic keys, configuration data) and
1923 mitigate the impact of detected errors. Where the underlying platform supports error correction for critical data, the boot
1924 manager shall additionally use those mechanisms to correct errors.

1925 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with MEDIUM or HIGH security profile.

1926 NOTE 1: Mitigation may include refusing to boot, falling back to a known-good configuration, or initiating a
1927 recovery path. The objective is to prevent execution in a corrupted state.

1928 NOTE 2: Where critical data is stored in immutable elements such as e-fuses, error correction can be implemented
1929 using Forward Error Correction (FEC) codes or similar techniques.

1930 5.10.7 [REQ-BM-AP-007]

1931 Requirement: The boot manager shall implement a mechanism to maintain availability of essential boot code in the
1932 presence of partial storage corruption subject to having enough data available for recovering the correct content of the
1933 essential boot code or failure of stages following the initial boot code.

1934 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with MEDIUM or HIGH security profile, where the boot manager is not
1935 stored in immutable memory.

1936 NOTE 1: The mechanisms may include redundant storage with selection of uncorrupted copies, fallback boot
1937 partitions, or integrity-driven repair where sufficient information is available. The implementation should
1938 be documented in the product description.

1939 NOTE 2: Essential boot code includes components required to initialise the platform and load subsequent boot
1940 stages. The initial boot code (e.g. reset vector and immediate successor instructions) is excluded from this
1941 requirement, as recovery from corruption at that stage requires hardware mechanisms outside the boot
1942 manager's control.

1943 5.10.8 [REQ-BM-AP-008]

1944 Requirement: The boot manager shall require authentication or physical presence before performing sensitive actions
1945 in recovery mode.

1946 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with recovery capability (all security profiles).

1947 NOTE 1: Recovery mode may be triggered automatically upon boot failures; however, any critical or security-
1948 relevant operations performed during recovery mode require authentication or physical presence.

1949 NOTE 2: The boot manager may implement authentication, physical presence, or both as the authorisation
1950 mechanism for sensitive actions in recovery mode. Where physical presence is not a feature of the
1951 product (for example headless infrastructure equipment or communications devices managed exclusively
1952 through network interfaces), authentication is the authorisation mechanism.

1953 5.10.9 [REQ-BM-AP-009]

1954 Requirement: When network boot is supported, the boot manager shall handle network boot failures in a manner that
1955 maintains boot availability.

1956 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with network boot (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

1957 NOTE: The mechanisms for handling network boot failures may include, for example:

1958 a) enforcing timeouts;

1959 b) falling back to a local boot mechanism;

1960 c) performing exponential backoff retries;

1961 d) attempting multiple authorised network boot servers.


1962 5.10.10 [REQ-BM-AP-010]

1963 Requirement: The boot manager shall generate logs for security-relevant failure conditions.

1964 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with verified boot or measured boot and logging capability (MEDIUM or
1965 HIGH security profile).

1966 NOTE: Security-relevant failure conditions may include verification failures, integrity violations, authentication
1967 failures, or unexpected modification of boot components

1968 5.10.11 [REQ-BM-AP-011]

1969 Requirement: The boot manager shall use time representations that remain valid beyond 2038.

1970 Applicability: Applies to all boot managers (all security profiles).

1971 NOTE 1: This requirement applies to all security-relevant uses of time, including:

1972 a) certificate validity periods;

1973 b) internal system time used for boot decisions;

1974 c) timestamps recorded in logs or audit records.

1975 NOTE 2: This requirement helps prevent failures associated with 32-bit time representations (commonly known as
1976 the Year-2038 problem).

1977 5.10.12 [REQ-BM-AP-012]

1978 Requirement: The boot manager shall protect recovery mechanisms from unauthorised modification or disablement.

1979 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with recovery capability (all security profiles).

1980 5.10.13 [REQ-BM-AP-013]

1981 Requirement: The boot manager shall prevent partial execution of boot components when verification has not
1982 completed successfully.

1983 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with verified boot (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

1984 5.10.14 [REQ-BM-AP-014]

1985 Requirement: The boot manager shall not perform security-sensitive operations when required cryptographic
1986 components or services are unavailable.

1987 Applicability: Applies to all boot managers (all security profiles).

1988 5.10.15 [REQ-BM-AP-015]

1989 Requirement: The boot manager shall not bypass security controls when handling security violations or verification
1990 failures.

1991 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with recovery capability (all security profiles).

1992 5.10.16 [REQ-BM-AP-016]

1993 Requirement: The boot manager shall preserve recovery capability across firmware or configuration updates.

1994 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with update and recovery capability (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).


1995 5.11 Non-interference

1996 5.11.0 Introduction to impact minimisation requirements

1997 This clause addresses the requirements in the CRA [i.1], Annex I, Part I, point (2)(i). Boot managers shall limit resource
1998 consumption, release hardware properly, and prevent negative impact on services provided by other devices or
1999 networks.

2000 5.11.1 [REQ-BM-IM-001]

2001 Requirement: The boot manager shall avoid generating harmful or disruptive network behaviour.

2002 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with network boot (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

2003 NOTE: Examples of harmful or disruptive network behaviour include:

2004 a) broadcast storms;

2005 b) network loops.

2006 5.12 Attack surface minimisation

2007 5.12.0 Introduction to attack surfaces minimisation requirements

2008 This clause addresses the requirements in the CRA [i.1], Annex I, Part I, point (2)(j). Boot managers shall minimise the
2009 attack surface by limiting functionality, eliminating debug interfaces, and restricting all non-essential capabilities in
2010 production builds.

2011 5.12.1 [REQ-BM-AMS-001]

2012 Requirement: The boot manager shall, before handing off control to the boot target, ensure that only the resources
2013 necessary for the boot target remain enabled.

2014 Applicability: Applies to all boot managers (all security profiles).

2015 NOTE: Examples of resources that may need to be disabled or released include, but are not limited to:

2016 a) debug or diagnostic interfaces;

2017 b) DMA-capable devices or peripherals;

2018 c) hardware resources not required by the boot target;

2019 d) allocated volatile memory;

2020 e) network or communication buffers; and

2021 f) memory regions that are not required for the operation of the boot target.

2022 5.12.2 [REQ-BM-AMS-002]

2023 Requirement: The boot manager shall exclude non-essential code from production builds.

2024 Applicability: Applies to all boot managers (all security profiles).

2025 NOTE: Examples of non-essential code falling under this requirement may include a) test code; b) debug
2026 instrumentation; c) coverage tools; d) experimental features; e) unsupported platform code.


2027 5.12.3 [REQ-BM-AMS-003]

2028 Requirement: The boot manager shall disable or protect interfaces and functions that are not intended for operational
2029 use.

2030 Applicability: Applies to all boot managers (all security profiles).

2031 NOTE: Examples of interfaces and functions that should be disabled in production configuration include:

2032 a) debug interfaces;

2033 b) diagnostic consoles;

2034 c) test or manufacturing modes;

2035 d) verbose or developer-oriented logging.

2036 5.12.4 [REQ-BM-AMS-004]

2037 Requirement: The boot manager shall remove unused or non-essential interfaces and protocols to reduce the attack
2038 surface.

2039 Applicability: Applies to all boot managers (all security profiles).

2040 NOTE: Examples of interfaces and protocols that should be disabled include:

2041 a) unused hardware interfaces;

2042 b) non-essential network services or discovery mechanisms.

2043 5.12.5 [REQ-BM-AMS-005]

2044 Requirement: The boot manager shall validate all inputs to ensure they match the expected formats.

2045 Applicability: Applies to all boot managers (all security profiles).

2046 NOTE 1: Input validation mechanisms may include:

2047 a) bounds checking;

2048 b) enforcement of size limits;

2049 c) rejection of malformed, truncated, or oversized data.

2050 NOTE 2: Inputs in this context may include:

2051 a) boot images;

2052 b) certificates;

2053 c) configuration;

2054 d) cryptographic data before processing.

2055 5.12.6 [REQ-BM-AMS-006]

2056 Requirement: The boot manager shall detect errors in critical operations and reject non-compliant inputs; transition to
2057 error handling on faults.

2058 Applicability: Applies to all boot managers (all security profiles).


2059 5.12.7 [REQ-BM-AMS-007]

2060 Requirement: The boot manager shall provide a mechanism to disable configuration options that are not required by
2061 the deployment integrator.

2062 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with configuration capability (all profiles).

2063 5.13 Exploit mitigation

2064 5.13.0 Introduction to exploit mitigation requirements

2065 This clause addresses the essential requirement in CRA [i.1], Annex I, Part I, point (2)(k) on mitigating the impact of an
2066 incident. The mechanisms available to boot managers are constrained by the pre-OS execution environment.

2067 5.13.1 [REQ-BM-EM-001]

2068 Requirement: The boot manager shall implement exploitation mitigation mechanisms appropriate to the documented
2069 threat model to prevent unauthorised code execution, privilege escalation between boot stages, and uncontrolled
2070 propagation of compromise.

2071 Applicability: Applies to boot managers where the documented threat model includes runtime code-execution attacks
2072 or stage-to-stage privilege escalation (typically MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

2073 NOTE 1: Annex D provides informative guidance on exploitation mitigation techniques. The techniques listed are
2074 non-exhaustive; selection is appropriate to the toolchain, platform, and threat model. This requirement
2075 does not mandate a specific subset.

2076 NOTE 2: Mitigations addressing hardware-side physical attacks (T-PHYS-5, T-PHYS-6, T-PHYS-9, T-PHYS-11)
2077 are addressed under Annex D component-standard deferrals and are not within the scope of this
2078 requirement.

2079 5.14 Monitoring

2080 5.14.0 Introduction to monitoring requirements

2081 This clause addresses the requirements in the CRA [i.1], Annex I, Part I, point (2)(l). Boot managers provide visibility
2082 into boot processes through logs and attestation within pre-OS constraints of limited storage and no file systems.

2083 5.14.1 [REQ-BM-MON-001]

2084 Requirement: The boot manager shall record measurements of boot components and security-critical configuration in a
2085 tamper-evident way (e.g. tamper-proof storage, or extended into a platform configuration register) before handoff.

2086 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with measured boot and logging capability (MEDIUM or HIGH security
2087 profile).

2088 NOTE: Tamper-evident retention does not require persistent storage. A platform configuration register or
2089 equivalent volatile mechanism provides the required tamper-evident property. Write-endurance
2090 constraints apply where persistent storage is used.

2091 5.14.2 [REQ-BM-MON-002]

2092 Requirement: The boot manager shall provide measurement records in a format that supports remote attestation
2093 mechanisms to ensure freshness against replay.

2094 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with measured boot and logging capability (MEDIUM or HIGH security
2095 profile).


2096 NOTE 1: Freshness mechanisms may include nonces, monotonic counters, timestamps, or challenge-response
2097 protocols.

2098 NOTE 2: Measurement records may include information such as:

2099 a) integrity digests of boot components;

2100 b) indices or identifiers of measured registers or structures;

2101 c) event types or measurement categories;

2102 d) version or revision information of components.

2103 5.14.3 [REQ-BM-MON-003]

2104 Requirement: The boot manager shall indicate security-relevant failures and state changes.

2105 Applicability: Applies to boot managers with logging capability (MEDIUM or HIGH security profile).

2106 NOTE: Examples of security-relevant failures and state changes includes:

2107 a) verification failures;

2108 b) authentication failures;

2109 c) security policy violations;

2110 d) recovery mode activation; and

2111 e) execution of unsigned code.

2112 5.14.4 [REQ-BM-MON-004]

2113 Requirement: The boot manager shall provide version information accessible to operating systems, management
2114 systems or authorised entity.

2115 Applicability: Applies to all boot managers (all security profiles).

2116 5.14.5 [REQ-BM-MON-005]

2117 Requirement: Where the boot manager implements logging capability, the boot manager shall record each authority
2118 transfer as a security-relevant event in the security log, including the mechanism invoked, the entity that initiated the
2119 transfer, the entity that approved the transfer, and the components affected.

2120 Applicability: Applies to boot managers that implement logging capability and provide one or more authority transfer
2121 mechanisms.

2122 5.15 Factory reset and data portability

2123 5.15.0 Introduction

2124 This clause addresses the requirements in the CRA [i.1], Annex I, Part I, point (2)(m).

2125 The present clause specifies obligations for the restoration of the boot manager to its default state as placed on the
2126 market, and for the secure transfer of data and settings to other products or systems where the boot manager provides a
2127 transfer mechanism.

2128 Transparency toward the user on data processed by the boot manager is not a boot manager product characteristic. Boot
2129 managers do not process user personal data in the course of normal boot operations.

2130 NOTE: Where end-of-life data removal procedures require user action, product documentation describes the data
2131 categories processed by the boot manager and the steps to remove them.


2132 5.15.1 [REQ-BM-FRDP-001]

2133 Requirement: The boot manager shall provide a mechanism, invocable by an authorised entity, by which all user-
2134 modifiable data and settings stored by the boot manager are securely and permanently removed, and the boot manager is
2135 restored to its default state as placed on the market.

2136 Applicability: Applies to boot managers that store user-modifiable data or settings (typically MEDIUM or HIGH
2137 security profile).

2138 NOTE: User-modifiable data and settings include boot configuration, user-added trust anchors, audit logs, and
2139 any other persistent state not part of the boot manager's default state as placed on the market. The default
2140 state itself is not removed by this mechanism.

2141 6 Assessment criteria for compliance with technical

2142 requirement

2143 6.1 Introduction to the assessment and compliance criteria

2144 6.1.0 Assessment criteria general structure

2145 This clause provides objective and reproducible assessment criteria to determine whether a product complies with the
2146 technical security requirements of clause 5. The assessment criteria are without prejudice to the conformity assessment
2147 procedures defined in Annex VIII of Regulation (EU) 2024/2847 [i.1]; they apply irrespective of the procedure chosen
2148 by the manufacturer.

2149 For each cybersecurity requirement defined in clause 5, the following clauses specify assessment criteria to determine
2150 whether the requirement is met. The mapping is one-to-one: ACC-BM-ESR-NNN assesses REQ-BM-ESR-NNN.

2151 The assessment criteria for each requirement are structured as follows:

2152  Assessment reference: Refers to the identifier of the concerned technical requirement.

2153  Assessment objective: Defines the security property or capability that shall be verified, ensuring that the
2154 assessment remains focused on the intent of the requirement.

2155  Assessment preparation: Describes the environment, setup, and preconditions required before executing the
2156 assessment with a view to guaranteeing consistent evaluation results. It includes the following elements as
2157 applicable:

2158 - Test environment: Describe the hardware, software, and network setup used for the assessment,
2159 including versions, topology, and any relevant dependencies.

2160 - Preconditions: Specify any configurations, credentials, or operational states that should be established
2161 before the test (e.g. product initialized, certificates loaded, user roles created).

2162 - Required tools: Identify the tools or software necessary to perform the assessment (e.g. vulnerability
2163 scanners, protocol fuzzers, traffic analysers, static code analysers, cryptographic test suites).

2164 - Required information/documentation for the assessment: Specify all information that is necessary to
2165 perform the assessment.

2166 - Reference any vendor-provided setup guides, configuration instructions, or operational manuals, as well
2167 as any relevant standards or technical notes, that define how the product shall be configured or operated
2168 for the assessment.


2169  Assessment activities: Provides execution steps to be performed such that the same assessment verdict would
2170 be reached when repeating these steps now or at a later point in time. Assessment activities may include, as
2171 applicable:

2172 - Review information/documentation for the assessment to confirm that the described implementation
2173 matches the requirement (e.g. verify that the security architecture document specifies TLS 1.2 or higher
2174 for all external interfaces, or that the password policy aligns with the defined threshold).

2175 - Perform security functional tests to verify the completeness and correctness of the
2176 information/documentation for the assessment.

2177 - Perform security functional or penetration tests to verify that implemented controls are correctly
2178 implemented e.g. to prevent unauthorised access or data modification (e.g. via attempting to log in with
2179 invalid credentials to test lockout enforcement or trying to modify protected configuration files without
2180 administrative privileges).

2181 - Analyse code or binaries to identify potential security weaknesses or misconfigurations (e.g. perform
2182 static analysis to detect hardcoded credentials or use dynamic analysis tools to identify buffer overflow
2183 or injection vulnerabilities).

2184 - Inspect configurations to ensure that required security parameters are correctly applied (e.g. check that
2185 weak cipher suites are disabled, two-factor authentication is enabled, and least-privilege access controls
2186 are configured in the system).

2187 - Observe runtime behaviour to confirm that protections such as encryption, authentication, and integrity
2188 verification operate as intended (e.g. monitor network traffic to ensure data in transit is encrypted or
2189 observe system logs to verify successful validation of digital signatures during startup).

2190  Assessment verdict: Defines the pass/fail criteria.

2191 - Pass: The assessment is considered passed if the product demonstrably fulfils the requirement and meets
2192 the defined security thresholds. Examples of such thresholds include:

2193  Minimum cryptographic strength (e.g. AES-128 or higher).

2194  Password policy limits (e.g. minimum of 12 characters).

2195  Login protection mechanisms (e.g. account lockout after five consecutive failed attempts).

2196  Resistance to a specified attack potential (e.g. equivalent to CSA High/AVA_VAN.3 or higher).

2197 - Fail: The assessment is considered failed if the requirement is not fulfilled, or if the defined security
2198 thresholds are not achieved (e.g. insufficient key length, missing authentication enforcement, or
2199 inadequate resistance to the required attack potential).

2200  Assessment evidence: Defines the artefacts and documentation collected to demonstrate that the requirement
2201 has been assessed and fulfilled. The evidence shall be sufficient to enable independent verification of the
2202 assessment results and to demonstrate compliance with the relevant CRA essential requirements. Supporting
2203 evidence includes, where applicable:

2204 - Test or assessment reports showing the steps performed and results obtained.

2205 - Logs, configuration files, or audit traces demonstrating the implementation of the requirement.

2206 - Screenshots, captures, or console outputs confirming the correct execution or protection behaviour.

2207 - Relevant vendor or design documentation describing the applied security measures.

2208 The indexing structure used in the present document is: ACC-BM-ESR-NNN where ACC identifies an assessment and
2209 compliance criterion, BM is the product short name (boot manager), ESR is the abbreviation of the essential
2210 requirement per clause 5, and NNN is the sequence number, matching the corresponding requirement identifier in
2211 clause 5.


2212 6.1.1 Boot manager assessment considerations

2213 Boot manager assessment may require:

2214  Platform-specific test environments due to hardware dependency.

2215  Specialised access to pre-OS execution environment.

2216  System integration context for component-level products.

2217  Physical access to hardware interfaces.

2218 The assessment relies on manufacturer documentation of the test environment and any platform-specific limitations
2219 affecting assessment.

2220 6.1.2 Scope of assessment

2221 The present document defines requirements applicable to boot managers as products. Conformity assessment against the
2222 present document addresses the boot manager as the unit under assessment, independently of any finished product into
2223 which the boot manager may be integrated.

2224 Where a requirement in clause 5 is conditional upon a capability of the platform or the boot target (see clause 4.4), the
2225 assessment uses the platform assumptions recorded in the product technical documentation. Verification that those
2226 assumptions hold in a deployed system is outside the scope of the present document.

2227 6.1.3 Assessment report requirements

2228 The assessment report includes:

2229  the product identifier and version;

2230  the declared use case and security profile described in Table 4.6.4-1;

2231  for each requirement in clause 5:

2232 - the requirement identifier;

2233 - a verdict of PASS, FAIL, or NOT APPLICABLE;

2234 - a reference to the evidence supporting the verdict; and

2235 - for a NOT APPLICABLE verdict, a justification meeting the criteria defined in clause 5.1.3.

2236  an overall conformity statement.

2237 A verdict of NOT APPLICABLE for a requirement shall be justified only when all of the following conditions are met:

2238  the capability referenced in the requirement's Applicability statement is not implemented by the product;

2239  the product's declared use case shown in Table 4.6.4-1 does not assume that capability; and

2240  residual risks arising from the absence of that capability are documented in the product technical
2241 documentation.


2242 6.2 Appropriate level of cybersecurity

2243 6.2.0 Overview of requirements addressed in clause 6.2

2244 Table 6.2.0-1: Requirements addressed in clause 6.2

Requirement Profile applicability
REQ-BM-RRM- 001 All
REQ-BM-RRM- 002 All
REQ-BM-RRM-003 All
REQ-BM-RRM- 004 If reliant on integrated components
REQ-BM-RRM-005 All
2245

2246 6.2.1 [ACC-BM-RRM-001]

2247 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-RRM-001.

2248 Assessment objective: verify that a cybersecurity risk assessment has been conducted for the boot manager product and
2249 is recorded in the product technical documentation.

2250 Assessment preparation:

2251  Test environment: not applicable; assessment is documentation review.

2252  Required information: the product technical documentation, containing or referencing the cybersecurity risk
2253 assessment artefact.

2254 Assessment activities:

2255  Confirm that the technical documentation contains or references a cybersecurity risk assessment artefact for
2256 the boot manager product.

2257  Confirm that the artefact identifies the boot manager product to which it applies and the version of the boot
2258 manager assessed.

2259  Confirm that the artefact records the methodology, scope, the assumptions from clause B.3 applicable to the
2260 product, identified risks, and conclusions.

2261 Assessment verdict:

2262  Pass: the technical documentation contains a risk assessment artefact that identifies the product and version
2263 and records methodology, scope, applicable assumptions, the identified product risks, and final conclusions.
2264 For example, a risk assessment that names the product build, states its method and scope, lists the assumptions
2265 and identified risks, and draws conclusions satisfies the requirement.

2266  Fail: the requirement is not met if the technical documentation contains no risk assessment; if the risk
2267 assessment omits the product or version identification, methodology, scope, assumptions, identified risks, or
2268 conclusions; or where the recorded content is present but incomplete against those items.

2269 Assessment evidence: reference to the risk assessment artefact in the technical documentation; record of completeness
2270 against the items above.

2271 6.2.2 [ACC-BM-RRM-002]

2272 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-RRM-002.

2273 Assessment objective: confirm two properties of the risk assessment artefact: completeness of threat consideration
2274 against the applicable Annex B subset, and consistency of the identified risks with the declared use case.


2275 Assessment preparation:

2276  Test environment: not applicable; assessment is documentation review.

2277  Required information: the cybersecurity risk assessment artefact; the declared use case under clause 5.1.2; the
2278 operational environment description in the technical documentation referencing clause 4.3; the use case
2279 definitions in clause 4.6.3; the security profile mapping in clause B.6.

2280 Assessment activities:

2281  Derive the set of Annex B threats applicable to the declared use case and operational environment.

2282  Confirm that the risk assessment artefact considers each threat in that set, either by analysis or by a
2283 documented non-applicability rationale.

2284  Compare the identified risks against the use case definitions in clause 4.6.3 and the security profile mapping in
2285 clause B.6; confirm the identified risks are consistent with the declared use case.

2286 Assessment verdict:

2287  Pass: the risk assessment addresses each Annex B threat applicable under the declared use case and operational
2288 environment, either by analysis or by a product-specific non-applicability rationale, and the identified risks
2289 remain within the threat surface implied by the declared use case. For example, a UC-VER product with
2290 network boot whose assessment addresses network protocol attacks and network boot persistence, and a sealed
2291 UC-IMM product that marks physical-access threats non-applicable with a rationale citing the sealing, satisfy
2292 the requirement.

2293  Fail: the requirement is not met if the assessment leaves an applicable threat unaddressed; if it surfaces risks
2294 the declared use case excludes; or where an update-capable product's assessment makes no mention of
2295 malicious update or update-distribution attacks.

2296 Assessment evidence: derived set of applicable threats; cross-reference table mapping each applicable threat to its
2297 treatment in the risk assessment artefact; record of the consistency comparison.

2298 6.2.3 [ACC-BM-RRM-003]

2299 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-RRM-003.

2300 Assessment objective: confirm that residual risks identified in the assessment are addressed by documented additional
2301 product-level measures.

2302 Assessment preparation:

2303  Test environment: not applicable; assessment is documentation review.

2304  Required information: the cybersecurity risk assessment artefact; the applicable requirements derived from the
2305 declared use case across clauses 5.3 to 5.15; the technical documentation sections describing implemented
2306 security measures.

2307 Assessment activities:

2308  For each risk identified in the risk assessment artefact, identify whether it is addressed by a requirement in
2309 clauses 5.3 to 5.15 applicable under the declared use case.

2310  For risks not addressed by those requirements, confirm that the technical documentation describes an
2311 additional product-level measure that addresses the risk.

2312 Assessment verdict:

2313  Pass: every risk not addressed by clauses 5.3 to 5.15 is matched to a documented additional product-level
2314 measure. For example, a manufacturing-process supply-chain risk matched by a documented factory-side
2315 attested provisioning step, or a long-term key-handling risk matched by a documented HSM-backed key
2316 escrow with stated rotation, satisfies the requirement.


2317  Fail: the requirement is not met if a residual risk identified in the assessment has no corresponding additional
2318 measure documented; or where the documentation records the risk as accepted without naming a measure that
2319 addresses it.

2320 Assessment evidence: Mapping of risks to requirements / additional measures; description of each additional measure
2321 as documented.

2322 6.2.4 [ACC-BM-RRM-004]

2323 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-RRM-004.

2324 Assessment objective: confirm that the security needs the boot manager places on integrated components are stated and
2325 substantiated by evidence.

2326 Assessment preparation:

2327  Test environment: not applicable; assessment is documentation review.

2328  Required information: the technical documentation section identifying integrated components on which the
2329 boot manager relies for security functions (per clause 4.4.3); the per-component statement of security needs;
2330 the documentary or test evidence supporting fulfilment of each need.

2331 Assessment activities:

2332  Confirm that the integrated components on which the boot manager relies for security functions are
2333 enumerated in the technical documentation.

2334  For each enumerated component, confirm that the security needs placed on it are stated.

2335  For each stated need, confirm that the technical documentation records documentary evidence (for example a
2336 component certification, supplier attestation, or conformance statement) or functional test evidence showing
2337 the component meets the need.

2338 Assessment verdict:

2339  Pass: each integrated component the boot manager relies on for security functions is enumerated in the
2340 technical documentation, with its security needs stated and evidence of fulfilment recorded. For example, a
2341 boot manager using an HSM for trust-anchor protection that enumerates the HSM with the needs "key
2342 confidentiality and physical tamper detection" and records the HSM's vendor conformity declaration covering
2343 those claims satisfies the requirement.

2344  Fail: the requirement is not met if an integrated component the boot manager depends on is missing from the
2345 enumeration; if the security needs placed on it are not stated; or where the evidence does not show the
2346 component meets those needs.

2347 Assessment evidence: enumeration of integrated components; per-component security needs and evidence record.

2348 6.2.5 [ACC-BM-RRM-005]

2349 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-RRM-005.

2350 Assessment objective: confirm that the technical documentation, taken as a whole, presents a coherent and complete
2351 risk-management record.

2352 Assessment preparation:

2353  Test environment: not applicable; assessment is documentation review.

2354  Required information: the cybersecurity risk assessment artefact; the mapping of identified risks to applicable
2355 requirements under clauses 5.3 to 5.15; the description of additional measures implemented under
2356 REQ-BM-RRM-003 (where applicable); the supporting evidence for integrated components under
2357 REQ-BM-RRM-004 (where applicable) the product technical documentation.


2358 Assessment activities:

2359  Confirm presence in the technical documentation of:

2360 a) the cybersecurity risk assessment artefact;

2361 b) the mapping of identified risks to applicable requirements in clauses 5.3 to 5.15;

2362 c) the description of any additional measures implemented under REQ-BM-RRM-003;

2363 d) the supporting evidence for integrated components under REQ-BM-RRM-004 where the boot manager
2364 relies on such components.

2365  Confirm that the recorded material is internally consistent: risks listed in the mapping match risks identified in
2366 the assessment artefact; additional measures address risks flagged as not covered by clauses 5.3 to 5.15;
2367 security needs stated for integrated components match the components enumerated in the assessment.

2368 Assessment verdict:

2369  Pass: each applicable content item is present in the technical documentation and the recorded material is
2370 internally consistent across the items. For example, documentation in which each risk identified in the
2371 assessment also appears in the mapping with its assigned clause 5 requirements, and each integrated-
2372 component evidence item traces to a corresponding assessment entry, satisfies the requirement.

2373  Fail: the requirement is not met if an applicable content item is absent; if the recorded items contradict each
2374 other; or where a risk identified in the assessment is missing from the mapping or an additional measure is not
2375 traceable to a residual risk.

2376 Assessment evidence: record of presence per content item; record of internal consistency check.

2377 6.3 No known exploitable vulnerabilities

2378 6.3.0 Overview of requirements addressed in clause 6.3

2379 The present clause specifies assessment criteria for the requirements in clause 5.3.

2380 Table 6.3.0-1: Requirements addressed in clause 6.3

Requirement Profile applicability
REQ-BM-KEV- 001 All
REQ-BM-KEV-002 MEDIUM, HIGH
REQ-BM-KEV- 003 LOW only
2381

2382 6.3.1 [ACC-BM-KEV-001]

2383 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-KEV-001.

2384 Assessment objective: verify that, at the moment of placing on the market, the boot manager is free of known
2385 exploitable vulnerabilities in its code, configuration, and cryptographic mechanisms.

2386 Assessment preparation:

2387  Test environment: a representative build of the boot manager as placed on the market.

2388  Required information: the pre-market vulnerability assessment record, the SBOM and component inventory,
2389 the list of cryptographic mechanisms used, and the declared component and dependency versions.

2390  Required tools: vulnerability scanners; SBOM analysis tools; access to recognised vulnerability databases
2391 including EUVD.


2392 Assessment activities:

2393  Review the pre-market vulnerability assessment record and confirm that its scope covers the boot manager's
2394 code, configuration, and cryptographic mechanisms.

2395  Cross-reference the SBOM and component inventory against EUVD and other recognised vulnerability
2396 databases as of a cut-off date recorded in the assessment evidence.

2397  Inspect the shipped configuration for known insecure settings (e.g. deprecated cryptographic algorithms,
2398 disabled verification).

2399  Verify that for each vulnerability identified during cross-reference, the boot manager either:

2400 a) does not contain the affected component or affected version in the shipped build, or

2401 b) does not expose the vulnerable component through its documented attack surface as specified in clause 4.

2402 Assessment verdict:

2403  Pass: no known exploitable vulnerability is present in components reachable through the boot manager's
2404 documented attack surface. A typical Pass record shows several cross-reference hits against bundled libraries,
2405 each either absent from the shipped build (version-bumped past the affected range, or component replaced) or
2406 non-reachable through the boot manager's interfaces (e.g. a log-parsing CVE in a library the boot manager
2407 never feeds external input to).

2408  Fail: an exploitable vulnerability remains reachable, or a non-reachable classification lacks architectural
2409 support. Recognisable patterns include an unpatched CVE in the bundled signature-verification library
2410 invoked during verified boot; an unpatched CVE in a network-protocol library invoked during network boot;
2411 or a "not exploitable" claim for a bundled crypto library CVE without identifying which clause 4 architectural
2412 element excludes the vulnerable code path.

2413 Assessment evidence: this may include any of the following: pre-market vulnerability assessment report; SBOM and
2414 component inventory; record of the EUVD cross-reference with cut-off date; configuration inspection records; clause 4
2415 architectural references supporting any non-reachable classification.

2416 6.3.2 [ACC-BM-KEV-002]

2417 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-KEV-002.

2418 Assessment objective: verify that security updates addressing known exploitable vulnerabilities are available
2419 throughout the declared support period.

2420 Assessment preparation:

2421  Required tools: access to the update channel; signature verification tools.

2422  Test environment: the boot manager in its configuration to receive updates.

2423  Required information: the declared support period as stated in the product technical documentation, the update
2424 distribution channel, the update release history, and the mapping between addressed vulnerabilities and
2425 released updates.

2426  Required tools: access to the update channel; signature verification tools.

2427 Assessment activities:

2428  Review the declared support period and confirm it is stated in the product technical documentation.

2429  Verify that the vulnerability handling process produces security updates addressing known exploitable
2430 vulnerabilities within the support period; alignment with prEN 40000-1-3 [i.4] is one way to demonstrate this.

2431  Confirm that the update distribution channel is operational and that delivered updates are signed and verifiable
2432 (see the assessment of REQ-BM-INT-005 in clause 6.8.5).


2433  Sample the update release history and confirm that past known exploitable vulnerabilities applicable to the
2434 boot manager have been addressed by released updates.

2435 Assessment verdict:

2436  Pass: security updates addressing known exploitable vulnerabilities are available throughout the declared
2437 support period. A typical Pass record shows the technical documentation declaring a support period; the
2438 update distribution channel operational; and a release history that includes security updates issued in response
2439 to published CVEs against bundled components within the support period window.

2440  Fail: security updates are not consistently available. Recognisable patterns include a support period stated but
2441 no operational distribution channel (the update endpoint is unreachable or serves unsigned artefacts); a
2442 published CVE applicable to a bundled component remaining outstanding without an addressing update; or
2443 technical documentation that does not declare a support period at all.

2444 Assessment evidence: support period statement from technical documentation; update release history; sample signed
2445 update artefacts; vulnerability-to-update mapping records.

2446 6.3.3 [ACC-BM-KEV-003]

2447 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-KEV-003.

2448 Assessment objective: verify that, for a boot manager without update capability, the product technical documentation
2449 states the absence of update capability as a residual risk, records the date of the pre-market vulnerability assessment,
2450 and describes the defence-in-depth measures compensating for the absence of post-deployment remediation.

2451 Assessment preparation:

2452  Test environment: not applicable; assessment is documentation review.

2453  Required information: the product technical documentation.

2454 Assessment activities:

2455  Inspect the product technical documentation and confirm each of the following is present:

2456 - the absence of update capability identified as a residual risk;

2457 - the date of the pre-market vulnerability assessment;

2458 - the defence-in-depth measures mitigating the inability to remediate post-deployment vulnerabilities.

2459 Assessment verdict:

2460  Pass: the technical documentation states the absence of update capability as a residual risk, records the pre-
2461 market vulnerability assessment date, and describes defence-in-depth measures that each address an identified
2462 consequence of the no-update condition. A typical Pass record might describe a shipping configuration that
2463 enables only a single boot target with network-boot and removable-media interfaces disabled, restricted I/O
2464 exposure that limits the parsers reachable from untrusted input, and a documented operational environment
2465 requiring controlled physical access to the device with each linked to the exposure it compensates for.

2466  Fail: the technical documentation does not adequately document one or more required elements. Recognisable
2467 patterns include the absence of update capability listed as a feature note without acknowledging it as a residual
2468 risk; an absent or undated vulnerability assessment statement; or defence-in-depth measures described in
2469 generic terms (e.g. "standard hardening measures") without identifying which architectural element addresses
2470 which exposure.

2471 Assessment evidence: relevant extracts from the product technical documentation.


2472 6.4 Secure by default configuration

2473 6.4.0 Overview of requirements addressed in clause 6.4

2474 The present clause specifies assessment criteria for the requirements in clause 5.4.

2475 Table 6.4.0-1: Requirements addressed in clause 6.4

Requirement Profile applicability
REQ-BM-SBD-001 MEDIUM, HIGH (LOW if implemented)
REQ-BM-SBD- 002 All
REQ-BM-SBD-003 All (if configuration capability with password authentication)
REQ-BM-SBD- 004 MEDIUM, HIGH (LOW if implemented)
REQ-BM-SBD- 005 All (if configuration capability)
REQ-BM-SBD-006 All (if configuration capability)
2476

2477 6.4.1 [ACC-BM-SBD-001]

2478 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-SBD-001.

2479 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager has cryptographic validation enabled by default when placed on the
2480 market.

2481 Assessment preparation:

2482  Test environment: a representative build of the boot manager in its shipped state, without any post-
2483 manufacturing configuration change.

2484  Required information: the documentation of the default state of cryptographic validation; the interfaces and
2485 mechanisms controlling the validation state.

2486  Required tools: a trusted-key test image (signed with a key in the documented trust store); an untrusted test
2487 image (unsigned or signed with a key not in the trust store).

2488 Assessment activities:

2489  Submit the trusted-key test image to the boot manager and confirm that validation succeeds and boot
2490 completes.

2491  Submit the untrusted test image and confirm that validation rejects the image and boot is halted.

2492  Inspect the boot manager's default configuration and confirm that cryptographic validation is enabled without
2493 any prior enabling step.

2494 Assessment verdict:

2495  Pass: cryptographic validation is enabled in the shipped state. A typical Pass record shows the untrusted test
2496 image rejected at the validation step with boot halted, the trusted-key test image accepted and boot completing,
2497 and the shipped configuration showing validation enabled without any operator-side step preceding these tests.

2498  Fail: cryptographic validation is not effective in the shipped state. Recognisable patterns include the untrusted
2499 test image accepted and boot proceeding (validation effectively disabled or bypassed); a shipped configuration
2500 that documents validation as disabled by default and requires an enable step before validation can occur; or
2501 validation that runs but treats untrusted signatures as warnings rather than rejections.

2502 Assessment evidence: record of the default-state configuration; record of boot with a signed image; record of rejection
2503 of an untrusted image.

2504 6.4.2 [ACC-BM-SBD-002]

2505 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-SBD-002.


2506 Assessment objective: verify the absence of unauthorised or undocumented mechanisms for bypassing the boot
2507 manager's authentication or security controls.

2508 Assessment preparation:

2509  Test environment: the boot manager in its shipped state with access to all exposed interfaces.

2510  Required information: the documented list of interfaces, commands, and authentication mechanisms; the
2511 product technical documentation.

2512  Required tools: interface enumeration tools appropriate to the platform; credential testing tools; binary analysis
2513 tools where source is not available.

2514 Assessment activities:

2515  Enumerate the interfaces exposed by the boot manager (e.g. shell, management commands, debug endpoints)
2516 and compare against the documented interface list; investigate any undocumented interface.

2517  Test each authenticated interface against default and hardcoded credential dictionaries and confirm that no
2518 such credential grants access.

2519  Inspect documentation and binary for maintenance or service modes; where present, confirm that entry is
2520 authenticated, documented, and does not bypass authentication or security controls.

2521  Review the binary for strings or code paths suggestive of backdoor or bypass functionality.

2522 Assessment verdict:

2523  Pass: the boot manager exposes no unauthorised or undocumented bypass mechanism. A typical Pass record
2524 shows interface enumeration matching the documented list with no undocumented endpoints discovered;
2525 credential testing against default and hardcoded credential dictionaries returning no successful access; and any
2526 maintenance or service mode found being authenticated, documented, and operating within the boot manager's
2527 security controls.

2528  Fail: the boot manager exposes a bypass mechanism. Recognisable patterns include an undocumented debug
2529 or service interface accessible without authentication (e.g. a JTAG or serial console exposed in the shipped
2530 state); a default or hardcoded credential accepted by an authenticated interface (e.g. admin/admin on a
2531 management endpoint); or a maintenance mode that disables or weakens authentication or security controls
2532 upon entry.

2533 Assessment evidence: interface enumeration record; credential test record; maintenance or service mode analysis;
2534 binary inspection findings.

2535 6.4.3 [ACC-BM-SBD-003]

2536 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-SBD-003.

2537 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager supports the establishment of passwords during initial deployment
2538 for interfaces that can compromise the system's core security guarantees.

2539 Assessment preparation:

2540  Test environment: the boot manager in a state representing initial deployment (first boot, manufacturer
2541 defaults).

2542  Required information: the identification of interfaces that can compromise core security guarantees and are
2543 protected by passwords, from the product technical documentation; the initial-deployment workflow.

2544  Required tools: interaction tool for the identified interfaces.

2545 Assessment activities:

2546  Identify, from the product technical documentation, each interface that can compromise core security
2547 guarantees and is protected by password authentication.


2548  Execute the initial-deployment workflow and confirm that access to each such interface is either gated on
2549 password establishment during the workflow or denied until a password is established.

2550  Confirm that no empty or default password grants access to the identified interfaces in the deployed state.

2551 Assessment verdict:

2552  Pass: for each identified interface, the boot manager either requires a password to be set during the initial-
2553 deployment workflow or denies access until one is set; and no empty or default password grants access in the
2554 deployed state. A typical Pass record shows the initial deployment workflow including a "set password" step
2555 that gates access to a management interface, and post-deployment attempts using common default credentials
2556 being rejected.

2557  Fail: the boot manager does not gate access on password establishment for at least one identified interface, or a
2558 default credential grants access. Recognisable patterns include a management interface accessible immediately
2559 after first boot without any prompt establishment the password; or a default password such as "admin" or
2560 "root" accepted after initial deployment.

2561 Assessment evidence: list of identified interfaces; record of the initial deployment workflow; records of access
2562 attempts after deployment.

2563 6.4.4 [ACC-BM-SBD-004]

2564 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-SBD-004.

2565 Assessment objective: verify that fallback to a boot mode weakening verification or rollback protection requires
2566 explicit authorisation and does not occur automatically.

2567 Assessment preparation:

2568  Test environment: the boot manager configured with verification and rollback protection active, with the
2569 ability to induce failure conditions in normal boot paths.

2570  Required information: the enumeration of fallback boot modes, the conditions under which each may be
2571 entered, and the authorisation step required for each.

2572  Required tools: fault-injection tools capable of triggering documented failure conditions (e.g. corrupted
2573 primary image, failed rollback counter read).

2574 Assessment activities:

2575  For each documented fallback mode, induce the failure condition that would normally trigger consideration of
2576 fallback.

2577  Confirm that no transition to a weakened fallback mode occurs automatically in response.

2578  Confirm that the boot manager either halts or remains in a mode preserving verification and rollback
2579 protection in the absence of the documented authorisation step.

2580 Assessment verdict:

2581  Pass: under each induced failure condition, the boot manager does not transition automatically to a fallback
2582 mode that weakens verification or rollback protection. A typical Pass record shows the boot manager halting at
2583 a verification-failed state when the primary boot image is corrupted, and halting rather than continuing the
2584 boot with rollback protection bypassed when the rollback counter read fails.

2585  Fail: under at least one induced failure condition, the boot manager transitions automatically to a weakened
2586 fallback mode. Recognisable patterns include a corrupted primary image triggering an automatic load of an
2587 unsigned recovery image; a failed rollback counter read causing the boot manager to bypass rollback
2588 protection on subsequent boots; or a verification key revocation triggering an automatic fallback to previously-
2589 trusted but now-revoked keys.

2590 Assessment evidence: enumeration of fallback modes; records of fault-injection tests and the boot manager's response
2591 under each.


2592 6.4.5 [ACC-BM-SBD-005]

2593 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-SBD-005.

2594 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager presents a prominent indication appropriate for the device's
