2595 interface capabilities when a security-relevant protection is reduced or disabled.

2596 Assessment preparation:

2597  Test environment: the boot manager configured for observation through the indication channel(s) appropriate
2598 to the device (display, audio output, LED, or log capture).

2599  Required information: the enumeration of security-relevant protections whose reduction or disablement
2600 triggers an indication; the form and observation channel of each indication.

2601  Required tools: configuration tool to reduce or disable each enumerated protection; capture means appropriate
2602 to the indication channel (e.g. display capture, audio capture, LED state observation, log capture).

2603 Assessment activities:

2604  For each enumerated security-relevant protection, reduce or disable the protection via its configuration
2605 interface.

2606  Observe the indication channel during and after the change and confirm that the documented indication is
2607 presented.

2608  Restore the protection and confirm that the indication is removed or updated consistently with the documented
2609 behaviour.

2610 Assessment verdict:

2611  Pass: reducing or disabling each enumerated protection produces the documented indication on the appropriate
2612 channel; restoring the protection updates or removes the indication consistently. A typical Pass record shows a
2613 boot manager with a display presenting an on-screen "verification disabled" message when verified boot is
2614 turned off in configuration, and the message clearing when verification is restored; for a headless device, the
2615 same Pass record shows a structured log entry recorded at the time of the configuration change naming the
2616 protection that was reduced.

2617  Fail: reducing or disabling a protection produces no indication on the documented channel, or the indication is
2618 inconsistent with the documented behaviour. Recognisable patterns include verified boot being disabled via
2619 configuration without any indication appearing on any documented channel; an LED indicator that remains in
2620 "secure" state after a security protection is reduced; or a log entry that mentions the configuration change
2621 without naming the protection that was reduced.

2622 Assessment evidence: enumeration of security-relevant protections; records of indication channel capture for each state
2623 transition.

2624 6.4.6 [ACC-BM-SBD-006]

2625 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-SBD-006.

2626 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager supports restoring its configuration to specified secure default
2627 settings.

2628 Assessment preparation:

2629  Test environment: the boot manager configured to a non-default state via documented configuration interfaces.

2630  Required information: the specification of the secure default configuration; the restoration mechanism; any
2631 documented limitations to restoration arising from immutable configuration or keys.

2632  Required tools: configuration tool capable of applying and reading configuration state; inspection tool for
2633 immutable-configuration elements where relevant.


2634 Assessment activities:

2635  Apply a documented non-default configuration and confirm the change is reflected in the boot manager's
2636 configuration state.

2637  Invoke the restoration mechanism per the documented procedure.

2638  Compare the resulting configuration against the specified secure default; confirm that all mutable
2639 configuration items are restored and that any items not restored correspond to documented immutable-
2640 configuration limitations.

2641 Assessment verdict:

2642  Pass: the restoration mechanism returns all mutable configuration items to the specified secure default, and any
2643 items not restored correspond to documented immutable-configuration limitations. A typical Pass record
2644 shows the boot manager configured with non-default settings (e.g. custom password policy, additional trust
2645 anchors) returned to the documented secure default after the restoration mechanism is invoked, with a fuse-
2646 burned trust anchor remaining unchanged and explicitly listed in the documented limitations.

2647  Fail: mutable configuration items are not restored to the specified secure default, or limitations are not
2648 documented as they appear in practice. Recognisable patterns include the restoration mechanism completing
2649 but leaving a non-default configuration item in place (e.g. a custom password policy persists); or an immutable
2650 item excluded from restoration without appearing in the documented limitations list.

2651 Assessment evidence: specification of secure defaults; record of non-default configuration; record of configuration
2652 after restoration; documented limitations reference.

2653 6.5 Secure updates

2654 6.5.0 Overview of requirements addressed in clause 6.5

2655 The present clause specifies assessment criteria for the requirements in clause 5.5.

2656 Table 6.5.0-1: Requirements addressed in clause 6.5

Requirement Profile applicability
REQ-BM-SU- 001 MEDIUM, HIGH (if UI implemented)
REQ-BM-SU-002 MEDIUM, HIGH
REQ-BM-SU- 003 All (if configuration capability)
REQ-BM-SU-004 MEDIUM, HIGH
REQ-BM-SU- 005 MEDIUM, HIGH (if HW present)
REQ-BM-SU-006 MEDIUM, HIGH
REQ-BM-SU-007 MEDIUM, HIGH
2657

2658 6.5.1 [ACC-BM-SU-001]

2659 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-SU-001.

2660 Assessment objective: verify that, where a user interface is available, the boot manager indicates when an update is
2661 available, or relies on authorised components to present that indication.

2662 Assessment preparation:

2663  Test environment: the boot manager operated through its user interface, with the means to induce an update
2664 being available and no update being available, and any additional update states the product indicates.

2665  Required information: the set of update conditions the product indicates and the indication used for each;
2666 where the boot manager relies on authorised components, the identity of those components and the interface
2667 through which status is passed to them.


2668  Required tools: display or output capture for the user interface; an inspection method for any interface exposed
2669 to authorised components.

2670 Assessment activities:

2671  Induce an available update and, separately, no available update; observe the user interface and record the
2672 indication presented in each case.

2673  Where the product indicates additional update states (for example update in progress or update failed), induce
2674 and observe those as well.

2675  Where the boot manager relies on authorised components instead of a user-visible indication, exercise each
2676 condition and confirm the corresponding status reaches the component through the declared interface.

2677 Assessment verdict:

2678  Pass: an available update and the absence of one each produce a distinct, observable indication, or that status
2679 reaches a declared authorised component. For a boot manager with a display, a pending update surfaces an on-
2680 screen state distinct from the up-to-date state; for one that delegates, the firmware management service
2681 receives the matching status over the declared interface.

2682  Fail: an available update produces no indication and reaches no authorised component. A boot manager that
2683 continues to show an up-to-date state while an update is pending does not meet the requirement.

2684 Assessment evidence: the list of update conditions and their indications; user-interface captures taken under each
2685 induced condition; records of the of interface inspection for code paths that rely on authorised components.

2686 6.5.2 [ACC-BM-SU-002]

2687 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-SU-002.

2688 Assessment objective: verify that, when network capability is available, the boot manager supports a mechanism to
2689 check whether an update is available, or relies on authorised components to perform that check.

2690 Assessment preparation:

2691  Test environment: the boot manager configured with network capability, in a controlled environment where
2692 the update source can be made to offer an available update or none.

2693  Required information: the update-availability check mechanism the product uses, including its protocol,
2694 endpoint, and schedule where applicable; or, where the check is delegated, the authorised components relied
2695 upon and the interface to them.

2696  Required tools: a controllable update source or emulator; a network traffic analyser; an inspection method for
2697 any interface to authorised components.

2698 Assessment activities:

2699  Make an update available at the source and invoke the check; record whether the boot manager, or the
2700 component it relies on, reports the update as available.

2701  Offer no update at the source and invoke the check; record what is reported.

2702  Where the check is delegated, exercise it and confirm the boot manager hands the check to the authorised
2703 component through the declared interface.

2704 Assessment verdict:

2705  Pass: the check reports an update as available when one is present and reports none when the source offers
2706 none, whether the boot manager performs the check itself or delegates it. A boot manager that queries its
2707 update endpoint and surfaces a pending update, or one that hands the query to the operating system's update
2708 service, both satisfy the requirement.


2709  Fail: the check does not reflect what the source offers. A boot manager that reports no update while one is
2710 available, that never contacts the source, or that neither performs nor delegates the check, does not meet the
2711 requirement.

2712 Assessment evidence: the specification of the check mechanism; records of the check with an update available and
2713 with none available; records of the delegated interface where authorised components perform the check.

2714 6.5.3 [ACC-BM-SU-003]

2715 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-SU-003.

2716 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager allows security policy to be updated through configuration, allows
2717 features to be disabled so that can be addressed, and retains this configuration update capability for the product's support
2718 period.

2719 Assessment preparation:

2720  Test environment: the boot manager accessible through its configuration interface.

2721  Required information: the security policy items that can be updated through configuration; the features that
2722 can be disabled; the documented commitment to retain configuration update capability over the product's
2723 lifetime.

2724  Required tools: a configuration tool; an inspection method for the boot manager's active policy and feature
2725 state.

2726 Assessment activities:

2727  Apply a security policy change through the configuration interface and confirm it takes effect in the boot
2728 manager's active state (for example tightening a verification policy or replacing a trust anchor).

2729  Disable a feature through the configuration interface and confirm it is no longer active.

2730  Review how configuration update capability is retained over the product's lifetime; confirm nothing disables it
2731 beforehand (for example a fixed expiry or a one-time configuration lock) and that the commitment covers the
2732 declared lifetime.

2733 Assessment verdict:

2734  Pass: a security policy change and a feature being disabled both take effect through the configuration interface,
2735 and the configuration update path stays available for the product's lifetime. A boot manager that accepts a
2736 stricter verification policy, lets a vulnerable network boot path be switched off, and keeps that configuration
2737 path open for its declared lifetime satisfies the requirement.

2738  Fail: a configuration change is rejected or has no effect, a feature cannot be disabled, or the configuration
2739 update path closes early. A boot manager that locks its configuration after first boot, or whose configuration
2740 update capability lapses while the product is still in service, does not meet the requirement.

2741 Assessment evidence: records of the policy-change and feature-disable tests showing before and after state; the
2742 documented commitment to configuration update availability over the product's lifetime.

2743 6.5.4 [ACC-BM-SU-004]

2744 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-SU-004.

2745 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager, where it performs on-update verification, accepts updates only
2746 from sources that are both authenticated and authorised.

2747 Assessment preparation:

2748  Test environment: the boot manager in its on-update verification configuration.


2749  Required information: the source authentication mechanism the product uses (for example signed update
2750 manifests, authenticated transport, or trusted source identifiers) and the authorisation policy applied to
2751 authenticated sources.

2752  Required tools: an update source that is authorised; one that is unauthenticated; one that is authenticated but
2753 not authorised.

2754 Assessment activities:

2755  Offer an update from the authorised source and confirm it is accepted into the subsequent update steps.

2756  Offer an update from the unauthenticated source and confirm it is rejected before any update action begins.

2757  Offer an update from a source that authenticates successfully but is not authorised (for example a valid
2758 signature under an identity outside the authorised set) and confirm rejection.

2759  Confirm the source authentication and authorisation decision is reached before the package verification of
2760 REQ-BM-INT-005 is invoked (assessed in clause 6.8.5).

2761 Assessment verdict:

2762  Pass: only the authenticated, authorised source is accepted, and both the unauthenticated source and the
2763 authenticated-but-unauthorised source are turned away before any update action. A boot manager that fetches
2764 from a trusted, identity-checked update server while refusing one offered by an unknown server, and rejecting
2765 a package signed by a retired signer no longer in the authorised set, satisfies the requirement.

2766  Fail: an update is accepted from a source that is not authenticated, or from one that authenticates but falls
2767 outside the authorisation policy, or the source decision is made only after the update has begun to be applied.
2768 A boot manager that accepts any reachable update server, or admits a correctly signed package from a
2769 decommissioned signer, does not meet the requirement.

2770 Assessment evidence: the source authentication and authorisation specification; test records for the authorised,
2771 unauthenticated, and authenticated-but-unauthorised sources; the record showing the source decision precedes package
2772 verification.

2773 6.5.5 [ACC-BM-SU-005]

2774 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-SU-005.

2775 Assessment objective: verify that, when hardware security components are available, the boot manager stores the keys
2776 used for update verification in those components.

2777 Assessment preparation:

2778  Test environment: the boot manager on a platform whose hardware security components are documented and
2779 inspectable.

2780  Required information: whether hardware security components are available on the target platform; where they
2781 are, the identity of those components and the interface through which the keys are stored and used.

2782  Required tools: an inspection method for the hardware security component appropriate to the platform (for
2783 example a TPM command interface, or a secure-element interface within the authorised scope).

2784 Assessment activities:

2785  Determine whether hardware security components are available on the platform under assessment; where none
2786 are, record the requirement as not applicable and close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

2787  Where hardware security components are available, locate where the update-verification keys are held;
2788 confirm they reside in the hardware security component and not in storage reachable by software.

2789  Exercise an update verification and confirm the boot manager uses the keys through the component's protected
2790 interface, with no key material leaving the component.

2791 Assessment verdict:


2792  Pass: the update-verification keys are held inside the available hardware security component, and verification
2793 draws on them through the component's protected interface without the key material being exported. A boot
2794 manager that holds its update-verification key in a TPM or secure element and calls the component to perform
2795 the check, rather than reading the key out into software, satisfies the requirement.

2796  Fail: a hardware security component is present yet the update-verification keys sit in software-readable
2797 storage, or the boot manager exports the key from the component to verify in software. A boot manager that
2798 loads its verification key from an unprotected flash region while a TPM is available does not meet the
2799 requirement.

2800 NOTE: Trust anchors may be firmware-embedded; assessment should consider documented storage location
2801 regardless of TPM/HSM presence.

2802 Assessment evidence: record of whether hardware security components are present on the platform; record of where
2803 the update-verification keys are held; record of the interface through which the keys are used during verification.

2804 6.5.6 [ACC-BM-SU-006]

2805 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-SU-006.

2806 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager, where it performs on-update verification, keeps its update logic
2807 isolated from the normal boot.

2808 Assessment preparation:

2809  Test environment: the boot manager exercised in both normal boot and on-update verification.

2810  Required information: how the update logic is separated from the normal boot path (for example a separate
2811 execution context, memory isolation, distinct code paths, or a state-machine boundary), and where the two
2812 paths share resources.

2813  Required tools: an inspection method for the boot manager's runtime state and the code paths it activates, as
2814 supported by the platform.

2815 Assessment activities:

2816  Execute a normal boot and inspect which code paths and memory regions become active; confirm the update
2817 logic is not among them.

2818  Trigger on-update verification and inspect which code paths and memory regions become active; confirm the
2819 normal boot path's decision state (boot target selection, trust anchors, verification policy) is not writable from
2820 the update logic.

2821  Where the two paths share resources, follow the handoff between them and confirm the update logic cannot
2822 alter normal-boot state through that shared resource, and the reverse.

2823 Assessment verdict:

2824  Pass: the update logic stays inactive during normal boot, and during update handling it cannot reach or modify
2825 the state the boot path relies on. A boot manager that runs update parsing in a separate context entered only
2826 after a stage boundary, so that a fault while parsing a malformed update package cannot overwrite the boot
2827 target or trust anchors, satisfies the requirement.

2828  Fail: the update logic runs as part of normal boot, or the two paths share memory or state such that update
2829 handling can influence a boot decision. A boot manager whose update-package parser writes into the same
2830 buffers that hold the boot target selection, so that a malformed package can redirect the boot, does not meet the
2831 requirement.

2832 Assessment evidence: execution trace of normal boot; execution trace of on-update verification; record of the
2833 separation mechanism and of any shared-resource handoff.


2834 6.5.7 [ACC-BM-SU-007]

2835 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-SU-007.

2836 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager applies updates atomically, so that an interrupted or failed update
2837 does not leave it in a partially updated state, and that on a failure it reverts to the previously operational state and
2838 remains bootable.

2839 Assessment preparation:

2840  Test environment: the boot manager in its update configuration, with the means to interrupt an update in
2841 progress (for example cutting power, forcing a reset, or severing the update source) and to corrupt or truncate
2842 an update package so that it fails partway.

2843  Required information: the point at which an update becomes committed; how the previously operational state
2844 is retained and selected on failure (for example a redundant image or a recovery image); the conditions under
2845 which the boot manager treats an update as failed.

2846  Required tools: a controllable update source; a means to interrupt the update at chosen points; an inspection
2847 method for the active boot manager image and configuration after each trial; a way to confirm the device still
2848 boots.

2849 Assessment activities:

2850  Determine whether the boot manager applies updates itself; where update application is performed by a trusted
2851 platform component instead, record the requirement as not applicable and close this assessment per
2852 clause 5.1.3.

2853  Apply a valid update without interruption and confirm it completes and the boot manager boots from the
2854 updated state.

2855  Interrupt the update at several points across its progress (before commit, during the write, and around the
2856 commit point); after each interruption, restart the device and record which state it boots into and whether any
2857 partially updated state remains.

2858  Supply an update that fails partway (for example a package truncated or corrupted after application has begun)
2859 and confirm the boot manager abandons it and returns to the previously operational state.

2860  After each failed or interrupted trial, confirm the boot manager boots and runs the previously operational
2861 image and configuration.

2862 Assessment verdict:

2863  Pass: every interrupted or failed update leaves the boot manager either fully updated or fully on its previous
2864 operational state, never in between, and the device boots in each case. A boot manager that writes the new
2865 image to a second slot and switches only after the write and verification complete, so that power loss mid-
2866 write simply boots the old slot, satisfies the requirement.

2867  Fail: an interrupted or failed update leaves the boot manager unable to boot, or running a mixture of old and
2868 new components. A boot manager that overwrites its only image in place, so that power loss during the write
2869 leaves a corrupt image and no working fallback, does not meet the requirement.

2870 Assessment evidence: record of the uninterrupted update; per-trial records of the interruption point, the state booted
2871 afterwards, and whether partial state was found; record of the retained previous state and the selection mechanism.

2872 6.6 Authentication and access control

2873 6.6.0 Overview of requirements addressed in clause 6.6

2874 The present clause specifies assessment criteria for the requirements in clause 5.6.


2875 Table 6.6.0-1: Requirements addressed in clause 6.6

Requirement Profile applicability
REQ-BM-AC- 001 All (if configuration capability)
REQ-BM-AC-002 All (if configuration capability)
REQ-BM-AC- 003 All (if configuration capability)
REQ-BM-AC-004 All (if configuration capability with password authentication)
REQ-BM-AC- 005 MEDIUM, HIGH (if verified or measured boot and configuration capability
REQ-BM-AC- 006 All (if configuration capability)
REQ-BM-AC- 007 MEDIUM, HIGH (if verified or measured boot)
REQ-BM-AC-008 All
REQ-BM-AC- 009 All (if authority transfer implemented)
REQ-BM-AC-010 All
REQ-BM-AC- 011 All (if authority transfer implemented)
2876

2877 6.6.1 [ACC-BM-AC-001]

2878 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AC-001.

2879 Assessment objective: verify that changes to trusted keys, certificates, or trust anchor databases are authorised only
2880 through direct physical presence at the device, or through a signed artefact whose authenticity and integrity the boot
2881 manager verifies before applying it.

2882 Assessment preparation:

2883  Test environment: the boot manager configured with an established trust anchor database, a physical-presence
2884 detection mechanism where supported, and the interface through which signed artefacts are submitted.

2885  Required information: the physical-presence detection mechanism, where implemented; the signed-artefact
2886 format, the trusted signer identities, and the verification algorithm.

2887  Required tools: a hardware means of asserting and de-asserting physical presence (for example a jumper,
2888 button, or hardware key); an artefact generation tool able to sign with trusted and untrusted signers.

2889 Assessment activities:

2890  Attempt a change to a trusted key, certificate, or trust anchor with neither physical presence asserted nor a
2891 signed artefact submitted; confirm it is rejected.

2892  Attempt the same change with physical presence asserted; confirm it is accepted.

2893  Attempt the same change through an artefact signed by a trusted signer with valid authenticity and integrity;
2894 confirm it is accepted.

2895  Attempt the same change through an artefact signed by an untrusted signer, or with an altered signature or
2896 content; confirm it is rejected before the change is applied.

2897 Assessment verdict:

2898  Pass: a change to a trust anchor takes effect only when physical presence is asserted at the device or when it
2899 arrives in a signed artefact that verifies against a trusted signer, and every attempt with neither is refused. A
2900 trust-anchor update offered over the configuration interface with no presence assertion and no valid signature
2901 is refused, while the same update carried in an artefact signed by the trusted key is applied.

2902  Fail: a trust-anchor change takes effect through neither asserted presence nor a verified signed artefact, or an
2903 artefact with a broken or untrusted signature is applied. A boot manager that accepts a trust-anchor edit over its
2904 configuration interface without any presence assertion, or that applies an artefact whose signature it never
2905 checks, does not meet the requirement.

2906 Assessment evidence: specification of the physical-presence mechanism; specification of signed-artefact submission;
2907 test records for each of the four attempt categories.


2908 6.6.2 [ACC-BM-AC-002]

2909 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AC-002.

2910 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager provides a means to protect boot-process configuration settings
2911 against unauthorised modification, and that where this protection is configured the protected settings cannot be
2912 modified without authorisation.

2913 Assessment preparation:

2914  Test environment: the boot manager accessible through its configuration interface.

2915  Required information: the boot-process configuration settings the boot manager can protect (for example boot
2916 order, boot parameters, boot target or mode selection); how the protection is configured; the authorisation
2917 required once it is configured.

2918  Required tools: a configuration tool; an inspection method for the boot manager's configuration and its
2919 protection state.

2920 Assessment activities:

2921  Identify the boot-process configuration settings the boot manager can protect, and confirm the protection can
2922 be configured for them.

2923  With protection configured for a setting, attempt to modify it without the required authorisation; confirm the
2924 modification is rejected.

2925  With protection configured, perform an authorised modification of the same setting; confirm it is accepted.

2926  Where protection is not configured for a setting, confirm the boot manager behaves as documented; the
2927 requirement makes the protection conditional on configuration, so an unprotected setting is not itself a failure.

2928 Assessment verdict:

2929  Pass: the boot manager can protect its boot-process configuration settings, and once that protection is
2930 configured an unauthorised modification is refused while an authorised one succeeds. A boot manager that,
2931 with boot-order protection enabled, rejects a change to the boot order over an unauthenticated interface but
2932 accepts it after authorisation, satisfies the requirement.

2933  Fail: the boot manager offers no means to protect boot-process configuration settings, or a setting configured
2934 as protected can still be modified without authorisation. A boot manager that exposes a "lock boot
2935 configuration" option which, once set, still lets the boot order be rewritten without authorisation, does not meet
2936 the requirement.

2937 Assessment evidence: the list of protectable boot-process configuration settings and how protection is configured;
2938 records of modification attempts with protection configured (authorised and unauthorised), and of the documented
2939 behaviour where protection is not configured.

2940 6.6.3 [ACC-BM-AC-003]

2941 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AC-003.

2942 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager requires explicit authentication before any modification of
2943 security-critical configuration.

2944 Assessment preparation:

2945  Test environment: the boot manager with its configuration interface available and an authentication
2946 mechanism configured.

2947  Required information: the security-critical configuration settings (for example settings that weaken or disable
2948 secure defaults, downgrade security parameters, or change verification policies or trust anchors); the
2949 authentication mechanism required before such a modification.


2950  Required tools: a configuration interaction tool; a means of attempting modification without authenticating and
2951 of replaying or scripting a modification to test for an implicit path.

2952 Assessment activities:

2953  For a security-critical setting, attempt a modification without authenticating; confirm it is rejected.

2954  Attempt the same modification with the required authentication explicitly performed; confirm it is accepted.

2955  Attempt the modification through a path that supplies no fresh authentication (for example replaying a prior
2956 session's credentials, or a scripted invocation that bypasses the authentication step); confirm it is rejected.

2957 Assessment verdict:

2958  Pass: a security-critical setting changes only after authentication is explicitly performed, and a modification
2959 that presents no fresh authentication is refused. A boot manager that lets a verification policy be relaxed only
2960 once the operator authenticates at that point, while rejecting a scripted attempt that reuses an earlier session,
2961 satisfies the requirement.

2962  Fail: a security-critical setting can be modified without authentication, or through a path that inherits or replays
2963 authentication rather than requiring it explicitly. A boot manager that applies a trust-anchor change carried in
2964 an automated sequence without a distinct authentication step does not meet the requirement.

2965 Assessment evidence: the list of security-critical configuration settings and the authentication required; test records for
2966 the unauthenticated attempt, the explicitly authenticated attempt, and the implicit-path attempt.

2967 6.6.4 [ACC-BM-AC-004]

2968 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AC-004.

2969 Assessment objective: verify that, where passwords are used for authentication, the boot manager limits authentication
2970 attempts through hardware-bound throttling, by limiting attempts, imposing increasing delays, or using a deliberately
2971 slow key derivation function.

2972 Assessment preparation:

2973  Test environment: the boot manager configured with password authentication on a documented interface.

2974  Required information: the throttling mechanism the product uses (its type and parameters, and whether it is
2975 hardware-bound or based on a slow key derivation function); the intended cost per authentication attempt.

2976  Required tools: an automated authentication attempt tool; a timing measurement tool.

2977 Assessment activities:

2978  Measure the cost per authentication attempt under sustained unsuccessful attempts (time per attempt, the
2979 attempt count before lockout, and the delay pattern across attempts).

2980  Confirm the measured behaviour matches the throttling the product documents.

2981  Where the mechanism is hardware-bound, repeat unsuccessful attempts across power cycles and confirm the
2982 throttling state is carried over rather than reset.

2983  Where a slow key derivation function is the mechanism, confirm its parameters (for example iteration count or
2984 memory cost) produce the intended per-attempt cost.

2985 Assessment verdict:

2986  Pass: the measured per-attempt cost and the lockout or delay behaviour match the documented mechanism,
2987 and a hardware-bound mechanism keeps its throttling state across power cycles. A boot manager that imposes
2988 an increasing delay backed by a monotonic hardware counter, so that power-cycling does not clear the
2989 accumulated delay, or one whose slow key derivation function measures at its documented cost, satisfies the
2990 requirement.


2991  Fail: throttling is absent, measures materially weaker than documented, or resets so that attempts can be retried
2992 freely. A boot manager whose attempt counter returns to zero on reboot, allowing unlimited guesses across
2993 power cycles, or whose claimed slow key derivation function completes far faster than documented, does not
2994 meet the requirement.

2995 Assessment evidence: the throttling specification; per-attempt cost measurements; records of throttling persistence
2996 across power cycles where the mechanism is hardware-bound.

2997 6.6.5 [ACC-BM-AC-005]

2998 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AC-005.

2999 Assessment objective: verify that, where security configuration policies are provided as separate signed artefacts, the
3000 boot manager verifies their authenticity and integrity before importing or enforcing them.

3001 Assessment preparation:

3002  Test environment: the boot manager with the interface for importing or enforcing security configuration
3003 policies accessible.

3004  Required information: whether security configuration policies are provided as separate signed artefacts; where
3005 they are, the artefact format, the trusted signer identities, and the verification algorithm.

3006  Required tools: an artefact generation tool able to produce artefacts signed by trusted and untrusted signers,
3007 and to alter content after signing.

3008 Assessment activities:

3009  Where security configuration policies are not provided as separate signed artefacts (for example policies built
3010 into the boot manager), record the requirement as not applicable and close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

3011  Submit an artefact signed by a trusted signer with unaltered content; confirm the policy is imported and
3012 enforced.

3013  Submit an artefact whose content has been altered after signing, so the signature no longer matches; confirm it
3014 is rejected before import or enforcement.

3015  Submit an artefact signed by an untrusted signer; confirm it is rejected before import or enforcement.

3016 Assessment verdict:

3017  Pass: a policy artefact is imported and enforced only when it carries a trusted signer's signature over unaltered
3018 content, and any artefact that fails the authenticity or integrity check is turned away before the policy takes
3019 effect. A boot manager that imports a policy signed by the trusted configuration key, while refusing one whose
3020 bytes were changed after signing and one signed by a key outside its trust store, satisfies the requirement.

3021  Fail: an artefact with altered content or an untrusted signer is imported or enforced, or the verification happens
3022 only after the policy has been imported or enforced. A boot manager that applies a configuration policy and
3023 validates the signature afterwards, or that imports a policy whose signature does not match its content, does
3024 not meet the requirement.

3025 Assessment evidence: the artefact format specification; test records for the trusted-unaltered, altered-content, and
3026 untrusted-signer artefacts; the record confirming verification precedes import or enforcement.

3027 6.6.6 [ACC-BM-AC-006]

3028 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AC-006.

3029 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager indicates when it is running with non-default security-critical
3030 configuration, through a persistent visual indication or, where logging is supported, through logged events.

3031 Assessment preparation:

3032  Test environment: the boot manager with a documented user interface or logging capability available.


3033  Required information: the security-critical configuration items whose non-default state is indicated; the
3034 indication used for each (visual, logged, or both) and its form.

3035  Required tools: a configuration tool; display or output capture for visual indications; a log capture tool for
3036 logged-event indications.

3037 Assessment activities:

3038  Place each security-critical configuration item into its non-default state in turn.

3039  Where the indication is visual, observe the user interface across the boot manager's execution and confirm the
3040 indication is present throughout, not only momentarily.

3041  Where the indication is a logged event, capture the log and confirm the documented entry is recorded.

3042  Return the item to its default state and confirm the indication is removed or superseded.

3043 Assessment verdict:

3044  Pass: each security-critical item in a non-default state produces its declared indication, and returning the item
3045 to default clears or supersedes it. A boot manager that holds a persistent on-screen notice while secure boot is
3046 disabled, or records a logged event noting a non-default verification policy, satisfies the requirement.

3047  Fail: a non-default item produces no indication, or a visual indication declared as persistent appears only
3048 briefly. A boot manager that shows a warning once at startup when verification is disabled and then nothing
3049 for the rest of its execution does not meet the requirement.

3050 Assessment evidence: the list of security-critical items and their indications; records of visual indication capture across
3051 execution; records of logged-event capture.

3052 6.6.7 [ACC-BM-AC-007]

3053 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AC-007.

3054 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager protects trusted certificate stores from unauthorised modification.

3055 Assessment preparation:

3056  Test environment: the boot manager with the trusted certificate store populated and accessible through its
3057 documented interfaces.

3058  Required information: the trusted certificate store, its storage location, the protection mechanism (for example
3059 access control, integrity protection, or hardware-backed storage), and the authorised modification path.

3060  Required tools: a certificate-store inspection tool; modification attempt tools for each interface that exposes the
3061 store.

3062 Assessment activities:

3063  Attempt to modify the trusted certificate store through each documented interface without following the
3064 authorised modification path (for example without physical presence, a signed artefact, or authentication, as
3065 applicable); confirm each attempt is rejected.

3066  Attempt to modify the store through any undocumented interface that exists (for example a direct memory
3067 access path or a debug interface); confirm rejection.

3068  Where inspection access allows, alter the store directly in its storage location and confirm that on the next use
3069 the integrity check detects the alteration before the store is relied upon.


3070 Assessment verdict:

3071  Pass: the certificate store cannot be modified through any interface without the authorised path, and a direct
3072 alteration of its stored content is caught by an integrity check before the store is used. A boot manager that
3073 refuses a store write offered over its configuration interface without authorisation, blocks the same write over a
3074 debug interface, and on the next boot detects that the store was patched directly in flash, satisfies the
3075 requirement.

3076  Fail: the store can be modified through some interface without the authorised path, or a direct alteration goes
3077 undetected and the tampered store is used. A boot manager that gates its configuration interface but leaves a
3078 debug interface able to overwrite the store, or that relies on a directly patched store without checking its
3079 integrity, does not meet the requirement.

3080 Assessment evidence: the certificate store specification; records of modification attempts per interface; the record of
3081 detection of a direct-storage alteration.

3082 6.6.8 [ACC-BM-AC-008]

3083 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AC-008.

3084 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager is accompanied by documentation declaring its code execution
3085 authority model with the elements required by REQ-BM-AC-008.

3086 Assessment preparation:

3087  Test environment: not applicable; this assessment is a documentation review, taking the boot manager's
3088 behaviour observed under the other assessments in clause 6.6 as a consistency reference.

3089  Required information: the documentation accompanying the boot manager that declares the code execution
3090 authority model.

3091 Assessment activities:

3092  Confirm the documentation declares:

3093 a) the mechanisms and entities that constitute the code execution authority model;

3094 b) their scope and relationships;

3095 c) the default state as placed on the market;

3096 d) any external dependencies of the mechanisms; and

3097 e) the processes by which the model can be changed where any aspect is mutable.

3098  Where the documentation declares that no entity or mechanism has authority to decide which code may be
3099 executed, confirm the declaration is explicit (see note under REQ-BM-AC-008).

3100  Confirm the declared model does not contradict the boot manager's behaviour observed under the other
3101 assessments in this clause.

3102 Assessment verdict:

3103  Pass: the documentation declares all five elements, or states explicitly that no entity or mechanism decides
3104 which code may run, and the declaration is consistent with the boot manager's observed behaviour.
3105 Documentation stating that verified boot with a pre-installed key is enabled at market placement, that the
3106 integrator may enrol an additional key through a defined process, and that verification depends on a platform
3107 security component, declares a usable model.

3108  Fail: an element is missing, stated too vaguely to convey the model, or contradicts the boot manager's
3109 behaviour. Documentation that sets out a key hierarchy but never states the default state at market placement,
3110 or omits an external dependency the boot manager in fact relies on, does not meet the requirement.

3111 Assessment evidence: the documentation under review; a record identifying each declared element by its location in
3112 the documentation; a note of any contradiction with observed behaviour.


3113 6.6.9 [ACC-BM-AC-009]

3114 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AC-009.

3115 Assessment objective: verify that, for each authority transfer mechanism the boot manager provides, the accompanying
3116 documentation declares the entities permitted to initiate or approve the transfer, the components covered, and the
3117 permanence of the transfer.

3118 Assessment preparation:

3119  Where the boot manager provides no authority transfer mechanism, record the requirement as not applicable
3120 and close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

3121  Enumerate the authority transfer mechanisms declared in the documentation.

3122  For each mechanism, confirm the documentation declares:

3123 a) the entities that can initiate or approve the transfer;

3124 b) the components covered by the transfer; and

3125 c) whether the transfer is permanent or reversible.

3126  Confirm that no authority transfer mechanism observed under the other assessments in this clause is absent
3127 from the documentation.

3128 Assessment activities:

3129  Enumerate the authority transfer mechanisms declared in the documentation.

3130  For each mechanism, confirm the documentation declares: (a) the entities that can initiate or approve the
3131 transfer; (b) the components covered by the transfer; and (c) whether the transfer is permanent or reversible.

3132 Assessment verdict:

3133  Pass: every authority transfer mechanism the boot manager provides is documented with its initiating or
3134 approving entities, the components it covers, and its permanence, and no provided mechanism is left
3135 undeclared. Documentation that, for a key-enrolment transfer, names the integrator as the approving entity,
3136 states that it covers the platform verification key, and that the transfer is reversible by a later enrolment,
3137 declares a usable mechanism.

3138  Fail: a declared mechanism is missing one of the three elements, or a mechanism the boot manager actually
3139 provides is not declared at all. Documentation that describes who may enrol a key but never states whether the
3140 enrolment is permanent, or that omits a recovery-mode transfer the boot manager in fact supports, does not
3141 meet the requirement.

3142 Assessment evidence: the documentation under review; a record mapping each declared mechanism to its three
3143 declared elements; a note of any provided mechanism found undeclared.

3144 6.6.10 [ACC-BM-AC-010]

3145 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AC-010.

3146 Assessment objective: verify that the documentation declares how the integrator or a downstream party can verify
3147 whether a given piece of software is authorised to run on the boot manager, including the tools, public keys, or
3148 mechanisms required.

3149 Assessment preparation:

3150  Test environment: the boot manager with its configured authority model in place; a sample of software signed
3151 by a declared trusted signer and a sample signed by an untrusted signer.

3152  Required information: the documentation describing the verification procedure, including the tools, public
3153 keys, or mechanisms it requires.


3154 Assessment activities:

3155  Confirm the documentation sets out the verification procedure from input to result, naming the tools and keys
3156 needed and the expected outcome for an authorised and for an unauthorised piece of software.

3157  Follow the documented procedure on the software signed by the declared trusted signer; confirm it reports the
3158 software as authorised.

3159  Follow the documented procedure on the software signed by the untrusted signer; confirm it reports the
3160 software as not authorised.

3161 Assessment verdict:

3162  Pass: the documented procedure can be followed to completion using only what it names, and it reports the
3163 trusted-signer sample as authorised and the untrusted-signer sample as not authorised. Documentation that
3164 gives the verification tool, the public key to check against, and the commands to run, so that an assessor
3165 reproduces both results without further information, satisfies the requirement.

3166  Fail: the procedure cannot be completed as written, needs information it does not provide, or reports a result
3167 that does not match the sample. Documentation that refers to a verification tool without saying where the
3168 trusted public key comes from, so the procedure cannot be run, does not meet the requirement.

3169 Assessment evidence: the documentation under review; a record of executing the procedure, with the inputs, tools
3170 used, and outputs for both samples.

3171 6.6.11 [ACC-BM-AC-011]

3172 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AC-011.

3173 Assessment objective: verify that any authority transfer initiated through a mechanism the boot manager provides
3174 requires explicit authorisation by the entity declared in the authority model as competent to authorise it, and is not
3175 performed as part of an automatic update or as a condition for continued operation.

3176 Assessment preparation:

3177  Test environment: the boot manager with its configured authority model in place; access to each authority
3178 transfer mechanism declared under REQ-BM-AC-009; the means to drive an automatic update cycle.

3179  Required information: the documentation of the authority transfer mechanisms; the declared identity of the
3180 entity competent to authorise each transfer.

3181  Required tools: a signed-artefact generation tool for the automatic update path; a means of asserting explicit
3182 authorisation as documented (for example physical presence, a signed transfer artefact, or console interaction).

3183 Assessment activities:

3184  Where the boot manager provides no authority transfer mechanism, record the requirement as not applicable
3185 and close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

3186  For each declared mechanism, drive an automatic update without explicit authorisation by the competent
3187 entity; confirm the authority transfer is not performed.

3188  Repeat with the boot manager configured so that continued operation would depend on the transfer; confirm
3189 the transfer is still refused without explicit authorisation.

3190  For each declared mechanism, perform the transfer with explicit authorisation by the competent entity as
3191 documented; confirm the transfer is performed.

3192 Assessment verdict:

3193  Pass: an authority transfer takes place only when the competent entity explicitly authorises it, and neither an
3194 automatic update nor a dependency on continued operation brings one about. A boot manager that enrols a
3195 new platform key only after the integrator authorises the enrolment at the console, while ignoring a key-
3196 enrolment instruction carried in a routine update package, satisfies the requirement.


3197  Fail: a transfer occurs through an automatic update, as a precondition for the device to keep running, or
3198 otherwise without explicit authorisation by the competent entity. A boot manager that silently enrols a key
3199 delivered in an update, or that forces a trust-anchor change before it will continue to boot, does not meet the
3200 requirement.

3201 Assessment evidence: test records for each declared authority transfer mechanism, covering the automatic-update path,
3202 the continued-operation path, and the explicit-authorisation path.

3203 6.7 Confidentiality protection

3204 6.7.0 Overview of requirements addressed in clause 6.7

3205 The present clause specifies assessment criteria for the requirements in clause 5.7.

3206 Table 6.7.0-1: Requirements addressed in clause 6.7

Requirement Profile applicability
REQ-BM-CP- 001 All (if cryptographic keys used)
REQ-BM-CP- 002 MEDIUM, HIGH (LOW if verified boot implemented)
REQ-BM-CP- 003 MEDIUM, HIGH (LOW if verified/measured boot implemented)
REQ-BM-CP- 004 MEDIUM, HIGH (if logging implemented)
REQ-BM-CP- 005 All (if configuration and recovery implemented)
REQ-BM-CP- 006 MEDIUM, HIGH (if network boot implemented)
REQ-BM-CP- 007 MEDIUM, HIGH (LOW if verified/measured boot implemented)
REQ-BM-CP- 008 All (if secure disposal implemented)
REQ-BM-CP-009 MEDIUM, HIGH (if network boot implemented)
REQ-BM-CP- 010 All
3207

3208 6.7.1 [ACC-BM-CP-001]

3209 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-CP-001.

3210 Assessment objective: verify that access to cryptographic key material is restricted to authorised boot components as
3211 defined by the boot manager's security policy.

3212 Assessment preparation:

3213  Test environment: the boot manager with cryptographic keys provisioned and the security policy active.

3214  Required information: the security policy identifying key material and the authorised boot components for
3215 each; the access-control mechanism used (e.g. isolation boundaries, access tokens, protected storage with
3216 enforced access).

3217  Required tools: inspection tool for memory regions and access-control state on the target platform; test harness
3218 capable of invoking non-authorised components that attempt key access.

3219 Assessment activities:

3220  For each key item, identify the authorised component set per the security policy.

3221  Attempt access to the key from each authorised component and confirm acceptance; attempt access from a
3222 non-authorised component and confirm rejection.

3223  Inspect memory regions and access-control state to confirm that key material is not reachable from
3224 components outside the documented authorised set, including via shared resources (e.g. caches, DMA paths).

3225  Where the boot manager does not use cryptographic key material, record the requirement as not applicable per
3226 clause 5.1.3 and terminate this assessment.


3227 Assessment verdict:

3228  Pass: each item of key material is accessible to the boot components named as authorised for it in the security
3229 policy and to no others; access attempts from components outside the authorised set are refused; and
3230 inspection finds no path, direct or via shared caches, DMA, or overlapping memory mappings, by which an
3231 unauthorised component could read the key. For example, a key held in a hardware key slot that is released
3232 only to the verified-boot stage and locked before control passes onward satisfies the requirement.

3233  Fail: a component outside the authorised set reads the key directly (e.g. a diagnostic or recovery module with
3234 unrestricted memory access); the key remains in a shared buffer or a DMA-reachable region after the
3235 authorised stage completes, so a later unauthorised stage can recover it; access is gated only by software
3236 convention (naming, documentation) with no enforced isolation or access-control boundary.

3237 Assessment evidence: mapping of keys to components per security policy; records of access tests per component;
3238 record of memory and access-control inspection.

3239 6.7.2 [ACC-BM-CP-002]

3240 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-CP-002.

3241 Assessment objective: verify that symmetric verified-boot operations use device-specific keys and that global secret
3242 keys are not used for verified-boot purposes.

3243 Assessment preparation:

3244  Test environment: the boot manager configured for verified boot using symmetric cryptography.

3245  Required information: key-provisioning documentation identifying the derivation or generation path for each
3246 symmetric verified-boot key and demonstrating its device-specific nature (e.g. derivation from a per-device
3247 hardware secret, per-device factory provisioning).

3248  Required tools: tooling to extract or compare key values across two distinct devices of the same model; key-
3249 provenance inspection where manufacturer documentation does not suffice.

3250 Assessment activities:

3251  Where the boot manager does not perform verified or measured boot, or uses no cryptographic key material,
3252 record the requirement as not applicable per clause 5.1.3 and terminate this assessment.

3253  For each symmetric key used in verified boot, inspect the documented derivation or provisioning path and
3254 confirm it yields per-device unique values.

3255  Compare the symmetric verified-boot keys across two distinct devices of the same model; confirm non-
3256 equality.

3257  For a key whose designation excludes a given operation, invoke the boot manager along a path that would
3258 require that excluded use (e.g. presenting data that could only be processed by using a verification-only key for
3259 decryption); confirm the boot manager does not perform the operation with that key.

3260 Assessment verdict:

3261  Pass: every symmetric key used in verified boot is unique to the device, established both by the documented
3262 derivation or provisioning path and by direct comparison across the tested devices. For example, each device
3263 deriving its verified-boot key from a per-device hardware secret fused at manufacture, with the compared
3264 devices yielding different key values, satisfies the requirement.

3265  Fail: the requirement is not met if the same symmetric verified-boot key value appears on two or more distinct
3266 devices of the same model; if the documented provisioning path is global or batch-wide, so keys cannot be
3267 per-device unique regardless of comparison results; or where the provisioning path is undocumented and
3268 device-uniqueness cannot be established by comparison.

3269 Assessment evidence: documentation of key provisioning; record of key comparison across devices; record of
3270 provenance inspection where used.


3271 6.7.3 [ACC-BM-CP-003]

3272 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-CP-003.

3273 Assessment objective: verify that key material is not used for cryptographic purposes other than those for which it was
3274 designated.

3275 Assessment preparation:

3276  Test environment: the boot manager with cryptographic operations observable.

3277  Required information: key-designation table listing each key and the set of cryptographic purposes for which it
3278 is authorised (e.g. this key for signature verification only; that key for measurement attestation only).

3279  Required tools: inspection tool for the cryptographic operations performed by the boot manager, including the
3280 key used in each operation.

3281 Assessment activities:

3282  Where the boot manager does not perform verified or measured boot, or uses no cryptographic key material,
3283 record the requirement as not applicable per clause 5.1.3 and terminate this assessment.

3284  For each key, observe the cryptographic operations performed during a representative boot and record which
3285 key is used for which purpose.

3286  Compare observed use against the key-designation table; flag any use of a key outside its designated purpose
3287 set.

3288  For a key whose designation excludes a given operation, invoke the boot manager along a path that would
3289 require that excluded use (e.g. presenting data that could only be processed by using a verification-only key for
3290 decryption); confirm the boot manager does not perform the operation with that key.

3291 Assessment verdict:

3292  Pass: every cryptographic operation observed during boot uses a key drawn from its designated purpose set,
3293 and attempts to exercise a key outside its designation are not carried out. For example, a key designated for
3294 signature verification is observed only in verification operations, is never used to decrypt or to derive other
3295 keys, and a path that would require such off-designation use is e-fused.

3296  Fail: the requirement is not met if an observed operation uses a key for a purpose outside its designated set,
3297 such as a verification key reused for key wrapping or decryption; if the boot manager carries out an operation
3298 along a path that requires off-designation key use; or where one key serves multiple unrelated purposes with
3299 no designation recorded, so confinement of each key to its designated purpose cannot be established.

3300 Assessment evidence: table of key designations; record of observed operations; records of misuse-attempt tests.

3301 6.7.4 [ACC-BM-CP-004]

3302 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-CP-004.

3303 Assessment objective: verify that sensitive data is not included in crash dumps or log output.

3304 Assessment preparation:

3305  Test environment: the boot manager in a state where crash handling and log emission can be exercised; the
3306 sensitive-data categories documented.

3307  Required information: enumeration of sensitive data categories; the crash-dump and log-emission paths.

3308  Required tools: fault-injection tool capable of inducing each documented crash condition; log and crash-dump
3309 capture tool.


3310  Search both capture sets for each sensitive-data category, covering at minimum the categories in the
3311 requirement note (cryptographic key material, authentication credentials, security-critical configuration
3312 parameters, and personal or otherwise confidential information processed during boot) together with any
3313 further categories declared for the product; confirm no such data appears.

3314 Assessment activities:

3315  Where the boot manager has no logging capability, record the requirement as not applicable per clause 5.1.3
3316 and terminate this assessment.

3317  Induce each documented crash condition and capture the resulting crash dump.

3318  Generate log output under nominal and error conditions and capture the log content.

3319  Search both capture sets for each sensitive-data category; confirm no sensitive data appears.

3320 Assessment verdict:

3321  Pass: across every induced crash condition and every nominal and error log path, no data from any category in
3322 scope appears in crash dumps or log output. For example, a boot manager that logs a verification failure as an
3323 event code and component identifier, with the failing key and credential values absent from both the log and
3324 any crash dump, satisfies the requirement.

3325  Fail: the requirement is not met if a value from any in-scope category appears in a crash dump or log entry,
3326 such as a key, password, or recovery secret written verbatim on an error path; if a crash dump captures a
3327 memory region holding sensitive data without redaction; or where the declared category list omits a category
3328 named in the requirement note, so the search cannot establish that all required categories are excluded.

3329 Assessment evidence: list of sensitive data categories; crash-dump captures; log captures; search results per category.

3330 6.7.5 [ACC-BM-CP-005]

3331 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-CP-005.

3332 Assessment objective: verify that stored credentials are protected using approved mechanisms that prevent recovery of
3333 the original credential values.

3334 Assessment preparation:

3335  Test environment: the boot manager with credentials provisioned and the credential storage inspectable.

3336  Required information: the manufacturer's documentation of the credential-storage mechanism (e.g. salted hash
3337 function, hardware-protected key-wrap) and the claim that original credentials cannot be recovered; reference
3338 to Annex K for approved mechanisms.

3339  Required tools: credential-storage inspection tool; cryptanalysis or recovery-attempt tooling appropriate to the
3340 declared mechanism.

3341 Assessment activities:

3342  Where the boot manager stores no credentials, or has no configuration and recovery capability, record the
3343 requirement as not applicable per clause 5.1.3 and terminate this assessment.

3344  Inspect the credential-storage format and confirm it matches the declared mechanism and that the mechanism
3345 is listed in Annex K.

3346  Confirm the stored form does not contain the original credential in recoverable form (e.g. plaintext, reversible
3347 encoding).

3348  Where applicable, attempt offline credential recovery against the stored form using tools proportionate to the
3349 declared mechanism's attack surface; confirm recovery is not feasible within the declared strength.

3350 Where a stored value is a tokenised reference rather than the credential itself, confirm from the documentation
3351 that the value is a token and exclude it from the recovery-resistance assessment; the protection obligation
3352 applies to the credential values, not to tokens that do not reveal them.


3353 Assessment verdict:

3354  Pass: every stored credential is held through an Annex K approved mechanism whose stored form does not
3355 reveal the original value, and recovery attempts proportionate to the declared strength do not yield it; values
3356 identified as tokens are outside this obligation. For example, user passwords stored as salted hashes using an
3357 Annex K key-derivation function, where the stored digests cannot be reversed within the declared work factor,
3358 satisfy the requirement.

3359  Fail: the requirement is not met if a credential is stored in plaintext or in a reversible encoding; if the storage
3360 mechanism is not listed in Annex K; if offline recovery against the stored form succeeds within the declared
3361 strength; or where a value is claimed as a token to avoid protection but in fact reveals or reconstructs the
3362 underlying credential.

3363 Assessment evidence: specification of credential storage; record of storage-form inspection; record of recovery-attempt
3364 tests where applicable.

3365 6.7.6 [ACC-BM-CP-006]

3366 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-CP-006.

3367 Assessment objective: verify that network boot parameters containing authentication information are protected by
3368 approved mechanisms preventing unauthorised disclosure.

3369 Assessment preparation:

3370  Test environment: the boot manager with network boot configured and the network-boot parameter storage
3371 and transmission paths accessible.

3372  Required information: the identification of network-boot parameters that contain authentication information;
3373 the applied protection mechanism for each (at rest, in transit); Annex K reference for approved mechanisms.

3374  Required tools: parameter-storage inspection tool; network traffic analyser capable of inspecting transmitted
3375 parameters.

3376 Assessment activities:

3377  Where the boot manager stores no credentials, or has no configuration and recovery capability, record the
3378 requirement as not applicable per clause 5.1.3 and terminate this assessment.

3379  For each identified parameter, inspect its storage form and confirm it is protected using the declared
3380 mechanism listed in Annex K.

3381  Capture transmissions containing the parameters and confirm the transmitted form is protected (e.g. encrypted
3382 transport, encrypted payload).

3383  Attempt to read the parameter in plaintext from storage and from the transmission; confirm neither yields the
3384 authentication information.

3385 Assessment verdict:

3386  Pass: every network-boot parameter carrying authentication information is protected by an Annex K approved
3387 mechanism both where it is stored and where it is transmitted, and neither storage inspection nor traffic capture
3388 yields the authentication information in readable form. For example, a network-boot credential held in sealed
3389 storage and carried only inside an encrypted transport session, where inspection of the stored form and of the
3390 captured traffic both yield only ciphertext, satisfies the requirement.

3391  Fail: the requirement is not met if an authentication parameter is readable in plaintext from storage or from
3392 captured transmission; if the protection mechanism applied to it is not listed in Annex K; or where the
3393 parameter is protected in only one location, such as encrypted in transit but stored in the clear, so disclosure
3394 remains possible at the unprotected point.

3395 Assessment evidence: record of parameter identification; record of storage inspection; record of transmission capture.


3396 6.7.7 [ACC-BM-CP-007]

3397 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-CP-007.

3398 Assessment objective: verify that secure disposal cryptographically erases sensitive data and clears security-critical
3399 configuration, where technically feasible.

3400 Assessment preparation:

3401  Test environment: the boot provisioned with sensitive data and security-critical configuration, with the secure-
3402 disposal operation accessible.

3403  Required information: the specification of the configuration for sensitive data and security critical items
3404 subject to secure disposal; the cryptographic erase mechanism; the documented limitations od technical
3405 feasibility and the rationale for each.

3406  Required tools: storage inspection tool for sensitive data and configuration regions after disposal.

3407 Assessment activities:

3408  Where the boot manager does not perform secure disposal, record the requirement as not applicable and close
3409 this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

3410  Invoke the secure-disposal operation with representative sensitive data and security-critical configuration
3411 populated.

3412  Inspect the post-disposal storage for each enumerated item; confirm cryptographic erasure or clearance per the
3413 declared mechanism.

3414  For items documented as outside technical feasibility, confirm the rationale is recorded and the corresponding
3415 residual-risk entry exists in the product technical documentation.

3416 Assessment verdict:

3417  Pass: every security-critical configuration and sensitive data item subject to secure disposal is
3418 cryptographically erased or cleared after the operation, and each item excluded on grounds of technical
3419 feasibility carries a documented rationale and a corresponding entry for residual risk in the product technical
3420 documentation. For example, a boot manager that destroys the key-encryption key sealing all stored secrets,
3421 rendering them unrecoverable, and records the contents of a one-time-programmable fuse as a documented
3422 feasibility exclusion with its residual risk, satisfies the requirement.

3423  Fail: the requirement is not met if an item subject to secure disposal retains recoverable content after the
3424 operation; if security-critical configuration survives disposal; or where an item is excluded from erasure
3425 without a documented feasibility rationale and entry for residual risk.

3426  Pass: every item subject to secure disposal is cryptographically erased or cleared; any items excluded by
3427 technical feasibility are documented with rationale and residual-risk entry.

3428  Fail: an item subject to secure disposal retains recoverable content after the operation, or an excluded item
3429 lacks documented rationale.

3430 Assessment evidence: inventory of sensitive data and configuration; records of inspection after disposal;
3431 documentation of technical feasibility and residual risk.

3432 6.7.8 [ACC-BM-CP-008]

3433 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-CP-008.

3434 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager, where secure disposal is supported, indicates successful
3435 completion of sanitisation.


3436 Assessment preparation:

3437  Test environment: the boot manager with secure disposal supported and the completion-indication channel
3438 accessible.

3439  Required information: the declaration of whether secure disposal is supported; where supported, the form and
3440 channel of the completion indication.

3441  Required tools: observation tool for the completion-indication channel (visual, log output, programmatic
3442 response).

3443 Assessment activities:

3444  Where the boot manager does not support secure disposal, record the requirement as not applicable and close
3445 this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

3446  Where supported, invoke secure disposal and observe the documented completion-indication channel; confirm
3447 the indication is presented upon successful completion.

3448  Abort or interrupt a secure-disposal operation and confirm that the success indication is not presented.

3449 Assessment verdict:

3450  Pass: a successfully completed sanitisation produces the documented completion indication on its declared
3451 channel, and an interrupted or failed operation does not. For example, a boot manager that emits a signed
3452 completion record to its audit log only after sanitisation finishes, and emits nothing when the operation is
3453 aborted partway, satisfies the requirement.

3454  Fail: the requirement is not met if a successful sanitisation produces no completion indication; if the indication
3455 appears on a channel other than the one documented; or where the success indication is presented for an
3456 operation that was interrupted or did not complete.

3457 Assessment evidence: declaration of support for secure disposal; record of indication on successful completion; record
3458 indication when the operation is interrupted.

3459 6.7.9 [ACC-BM-CP-009]

3460 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-CP-009.

3461 Assessment objective: verify that boot configuration data transmitted over the network is protected for confidentiality
3462 and integrity.

3463 Assessment preparation:

3464  Confirm that authentication of the network boot server and of the origin of network responses is assessed
3465 under clause 6.8 (ACC-BM-INT-013, ACC-BM-INT-014, ACC-BM-INT-015); this assessment addresses the
3466 confidentiality and integrity of the transmitted boot configuration data payload itself.

3467  Test environment: the boot manager configured for network boot in a controlled environment supporting
3468 active man-in-the-middle modifications.

3469  Required information: the documentation of the transport protection mechanism applied to boot configuration
3470 data (e.g. authenticated encryption, TLS, payload that is both signed and encrypted); Annex K reference.

3471  Required tools: passive network capture tool; active man-in-the-middle tool capable of modifying transmitted
3472 data.

3473 Assessment activities:

3474  Where the boot manager has no network boot capability, record the requirement as not applicable and close
3475 this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

3476  Capture network transmissions of boot configuration data and confirm the payload is not in plaintext form and
3477 is protected by the declared mechanism listed in Annex K.


3478  Execute a man-in-the-middle modification of a boot configuration data payload; confirm the boot manager
3479 detects the integrity violation and rejects the modified data.

3480  Attempt a passive decryption of the captured payload using tools proportionate to the declared mechanism's
3481 strength; confirm infeasibility.

3482 Assessment verdict:

3483  Pass: boot configuration data transmitted over the network is carried in a form that an Annex K mechanism
3484 protects for both confidentiality and integrity, a modification injected in transit is detected and the data
3485 rejected, and passive decryption of the captured payload is infeasible within the declared strength. For
3486 example, boot configuration delivered inside an authenticated encryption transport session, where the captured
3487 payload is ciphertext, a tampered byte causes the boot manager to reject the data, and offline decryption of the
3488 capture does not succeed, satisfies the requirement.

3489  Fail: the requirement is not met if a boot configuration payload is transmitted in plaintext or in a form not
3490 protected by an Annex K mechanism; if a payload modified in transit is accepted rather than detected and
3491 rejected; or where passive decryption of the captured payload succeeds within the declared strength.

3492 Assessment evidence: specification of transport protection; record of captured payload; record of integrity-violation
3493 detection.

3494 6.7.10 [ACC-BM-CP-010]

3495 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-CP-010.

3496 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager overwrites confidential or secret data after use, clears credentials
3497 and temporary data structures before boot target handoff, and does not persist authentication credentials or confidential
3498 cryptographic material beyond the operating system handoff, with the exception of measurements and credentials used
3499 for attestation.

3500 Assessment preparation:

3501  Test environment: the boot manager with memory inspection capability at handoff and across power-cycle
3502 boundaries.

3503  Required information: enumeration of confidential or secret data, credentials, and temporary data structures
3504 processed during boot; the documented attestation material exempt from clearance; the clearing mechanism for
3505 each item.

3506  Required tools: memory inspection tool at handoff; persistent-storage inspection tool across power cycles.

3507 Assessment activities:

3508  Drive the boot manager through a complete boot with enumerated sensitive items exercised.

3509  Immediately before handoff, inspect memory and relevant data structures for residual sensitive content;
3510 confirm overwriting or clearance for all enumerated items except the documented attestation exceptions.

3511  Power-cycle the device and inspect persistent storage for authentication credentials or confidential
3512 cryptographic material; confirm no persistence beyond the current boot cycle except for documented
3513 attestation material.

3514 Assessment verdict:

3515  Pass: at boot target handoff every enumerated confidential or sensitive item is overwritten or cleared except
3516 the documented attestation material, and across a power cycle no authentication credential or confidential
3517 cryptographic material persists beyond the documented attestation exceptions. For example, a boot manager
3518 that zeroises the disk-encryption key and the user-entered passphrase from memory immediately before
3519 handing control to the operating system, while leaving the attestation quote in its designated register, satisfies
3520 the requirement.


3521  Fail: the requirement is not met if a sensitive item remains readable in memory at handoff without a
3522 documented attestation exception; if an authentication credential or confidential cryptographic material
3523 persists in storage across a power cycle outside the documented exceptions; or where the attestation carve-out
3524 is used to retain material beyond the measurements and attestation credentials the requirement permits.

3525 Assessment evidence: inventory of sensitive items; record of memory inspection at handoff; record of inspection after
3526 power cycling.

3527 6.8 Integrity protection

3528 6.8.0 Overview of requirements addressed in clause 6.8

3529 The present clause specifies assessment criteria for the requirements in clause 5.8.

3530 Table 6.8.0-1: Requirements addressed in clause 6.8

Requirement Profile applicability
REQ-BM-INT- 001 All
REQ-BM-INT- 002 MEDIUM, HIGH (LOW if implemented)
REQ-BM-INT- 003 MEDIUM, HIGH (LOW if implemented)
REQ-BM-INT- 004 All (if measured boot)
REQ-BM-INT- 005 MEDIUM, HIGH
REQ-BM-INT- 006 MEDIUM, HIGH (LOW if implemented)
REQ-BM-INT- 007 MEDIUM, HIGH (LOW if implemented)
REQ-BM-INT- 008 MEDIUM, HIGH (LOW if implemented)
REQ-BM-INT-009 All
REQ-BM-INT- 010 MEDIUM, HIGH (if HW supports)
REQ-BM-INT- 011 All (if configuration capability)
REQ-BM-INT- 012 All (if configuration capability)
REQ-BM-INT- 013 MEDIUM, HIGH (if network boot)
REQ-BM-INT- 014 MEDIUM, HIGH (if network boot)
REQ-BM-INT- 015 MEDIUM, HIGH (if network boot)
REQ-BM-INT- 016 MEDIUM, HIGH (if update or configuration capability)
REQ-BM-INT- 017 HIGH only
REQ-BM-INT- 018 MEDIUM, HIGH (LOW if implemented)
REQ-BM-INT- 019 MEDIUM, HIGH (LOW if implemented)
REQ-BM-INT- 020 All
REQ-BM-INT- 021 MEDIUM, HIGH
REQ-BM-INT- 022 MEDIUM, HIGH (LOW if implemented)
REQ-BM-INT- 023 MEDIUM, HIGH
REQ-BM-INT- 024 All (if code execution authority data is stored)
3531

3532 6.8.1 [ACC-BM-INT-001]

3533 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-INT-001.
