3534 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager enforces privilege boundaries between boot stages such that code
3535 in one stage cannot obtain privileges assigned to another stage or cross established trust boundaries.

3536 Assessment preparation:

3537  Test environment: the boot manager at a point where two or more boot stages execute with distinct privileges.

3538  Required information: the privilege boundaries between stages (memory regions, privileged instructions,
3539 security-sensitive hardware access) and the enforcement mechanism for each.

3540  Required tools: test payload executed within a stage attempting cross-stage privilege access.


3541 Assessment activities:

3542  For each privilege boundary, run a test payload in the lower-privileged stage that attempts to access the higher-
3543 privileged stage's memory, instructions, or hardware resources; confirm each attempt is rejected.

3544  Attempt an invocation across a trust boundary (for example calling a higher-trust routine with crafted
3545 arguments); confirm the enforcement mechanism prevents escalation.

3546 Assessment verdict:

3547  Pass: code in one boot stage cannot reach the privileges of another, and crossing a trust boundary does not
3548 escalate privilege. For example, a payload in a later, lower-privileged stage that tries to read an earlier stage's
3549 key material, execute an instruction reserved to a higher-privileged stage, or call a higher-trust routine with
3550 crafted arguments is faulted or denied, and every documented boundary holds.

3551  Fail: the requirement is not met if a payload in one stage reads or writes memory belonging to another stage; if
3552 it executes a privileged instruction or reaches a hardware resource reserved to another stage; or where a crafted
3553 call across a trust boundary escalates privilege instead of being rejected.

3554 Assessment evidence: the list of privilege boundaries; records of the cross-access tests per boundary.

3555 6.8.2 [ACC-BM-INT-002]

3556 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-INT-002.

3557 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager verifies integrity and authenticity of each boot stage using
3558 approved cryptographic mechanisms and establishes a chain of trust to a root trust anchor before transferring control.

3559 Assessment preparation:

3560  Test environment: the boot manager with verified boot active and representative boot-stage artefacts.

3561  Required information: the chain of trust (stages, credentials, verification algorithm per stage) and the identity
3562 of the root trust anchor.

3563  Required tools: signed boot-stage artefacts using trusted and untrusted credentials; a means to observe each
3564 verification step.

3565 Assessment activities:

3566  Where the boot manager does not perform on-boot verification, record the requirement as not applicable and
3567 close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

3568  Execute a full boot with all stages validly signed; confirm each stage is verified using an approved mechanism
3569 per Annex K and that the chain is traced to the root trust anchor before control transfer.

3570  Substitute one stage's credential with an untrusted credential; confirm the chain-of-trust check detects the
3571 break and halts before that stage's control transfer.

3572 Assessment verdict:

3573  Pass: every stage is verified with an approved mechanism and the chain of trust reaches the root trust anchor
3574 before control passes to the next stage, and a broken chain stops the boot. For example, a boot with all stages
3575 correctly signed proceeds with each stage validated back to the root anchor, while substituting an untrusted
3576 credential at one stage halts the boot before that stage runs.

3577  Fail: the requirement is not met if a stage executes without being verified; if the chain of trust does not reach
3578 the root trust anchor before control transfer; or where a broken chain goes undetected and the affected stage
3579 runs.

3580 Assessment evidence: chain-of-trust specification; observation of verification per stage; record of injection of broken
3581 chains.


3582 6.8.3 [ACC-BM-INT-003]

3583 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-INT-003.

3584 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager prevents boot continuation with components that fail integrity or
3585 authenticity verification.

3586 Assessment preparation:

3587  Test environment: the boot manager with verified boot active and the ability to substitute components with
3588 documented failure conditions.

3589  Required information: the verification failure classes (invalid credential, expired credential, revoked
3590 credential, tampered component, missing or untrusted verification data).

3591  Required tools: a component-substitution tool covering each failure class.

3592 Assessment activities:

3593  Where the boot manager does not perform on-boot verification, record the requirement as not applicable and
3594 close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

3595  For each failure class, substitute a component exhibiting that failure condition and initiate boot.

3596  Confirm the boot manager halts before executing the failed component, and that no subsequent boot stage
3597 executes while the failure condition persists.

3598 Assessment verdict:

3599  Pass: each failure class stops the boot before the failed component runs, and no later stage executes while the
3600 failure persists. For example, a component carrying a revoked credential, and separately one whose contents
3601 were tampered after signing, each cause the boot manager to halt before that component is given control.

3602  Fail: the requirement is not met if a component that fails verification is executed; if a later stage runs after a
3603 prior verification failure; or where a failure class produces no halt.

3604 Assessment evidence: the list of failure classes; records of substitution and halt per class.

3605 6.8.4 [ACC-BM-INT-004]

3606 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-INT-004.

3607 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager computes and records a cryptographic measurement of each boot
3608 stage into hardware-protected storage before transferring control, establishing a measurement chain rooted in a
3609 hardware-based trust anchor.

3610 Assessment preparation:

3611  Test environment: the boot manager with measured boot active on a platform with hardware-protected
3612 measurement storage (e.g. TPM).

3613  Required information: the measurement scheme (stages measured, hash algorithm, storage target, hardware
3614 root of trust).

3615  Required tools: a tool to read the hardware-protected measurement storage; an external verifier able to
3616 reproduce the expected measurement chain.

3617 Assessment activities:

3618  Where the boot manager does not implement measured boot, record the requirement as not applicable and
3619 close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

3620  Execute a boot and read the measurement storage at each transition between stages; confirm each stage's
3621 measurement is recorded before control is transferred.


3622  Reproduce the expected measurement chain with the external verifier from the documented initial values;
3623 confirm the recorded chain matches.

3624  Confirm the root of the measurement chain is the hardware trust anchor.

3625 Assessment verdict:

3626  Pass: each stage is measured into hardware-protected storage before control passes on, the recorded chain
3627 reproduces the expected computation, and it is rooted in the hardware trust anchor. For example, reading the
3628 TPM registers after boot shows a measurement recorded for every stage in order, and an external verifier
3629 rebuilds the same chain from the documented initial values back to the hardware root.

3630  Fail: the requirement is not met if a stage is not measured; if a measurement is recorded only after control has
3631 transferred; if the recorded chain deviates from the expected computation; or where the chain is not rooted in
3632 the hardware trust anchor.

3633 Assessment evidence: measurement-scheme specification; capture of measurements per stage; record of reproducing
3634 the expected chain.

3635 6.8.5 [ACC-BM-INT-005]

3636 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-INT-005.

3637 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager verifies authenticity and integrity of update packages before
3638 installation, and additionally after the content is received where updates are written to protected storage

3639 Assessment preparation:

3640  Test environment: the boot manager in its configuration for receiving and installing updates; where applicable,
3641 with protected intermediate storage for updates.

3642  Required information: the verification algorithm applied to update packages; whether protected intermediate
3643 storage is used; the verification points required by the requirement.

3644  Required tools: a tool to generate update packages with valid and with invalid authenticity or integrity; a
3645 means to capture and modify content in transit.

3646 Assessment activities:

3647  Where the boot manager does not perform on-update verification, record the requirement as not applicable and
3648 close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

3649  Submit a package with valid authenticity and integrity; confirm verification succeeds and installation proceeds.

3650  Submit a package altered after signing; confirm verification rejects it before installation.

3651  Where protected intermediate storage is used, confirm the additional verification after the content is received
3652 and before it is committed to that storage; modify the content between receipt and commit and confirm the
3653 modification is detected.

3654 Assessment verdict:

3655  Pass: a package with valid authenticity and integrity is installed, a package altered after signing is rejected
3656 before installation, and where protected intermediate storage is used the after-receipt verification catches
3657 content modified between receipt and commit. For example, a bit-flipped package is refused before any
3658 installation step, and a package modified while staged in protected storage is detected on the second
3659 verification rather than being committed.

3660  Fail: the requirement is not met if an altered package is installed; if verification occurs only after installation
3661 has begun; or where, with protected intermediate storage in use, a modification between receipt and commit
3662 goes undetected.

3663 Assessment evidence: the verification specification; test records per package; records of the modification tests after
3664 receipt.


3665 6.8.6 [ACC-BM-INT-006]

3666 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-INT-006.

3667 Assessment objective: verify that, where hardware security components are unavailable, the boot manager implements
3668 software-based cryptographic verification with keys loaded from protected storage.

3669 Assessment preparation:

3670  Test environment: the boot manager operating on a platform where hardware security components are absent
3671 or documented as unavailable.

3672  Required information: the software-based verification mechanism and the protected-storage location for the
3673 keys.

3674  Required tools: a storage inspection tool; a means to observe the software verification path.

3675 Assessment activities:

3676  Where the boot manager does not perform verified boot, or hardware security components are available, record
3677 the requirement as not applicable and close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

3678  Observe that the software-based verification path is used for verified boot and that the keys are retrieved from
3679 the documented protected storage.

3680  Attempt to modify the stored keys through any interface other than the documented authorised path; confirm
3681 rejection.

3682 Assessment verdict:

3683  Pass: with hardware security components unavailable, the boot manager verifies boot in software using keys
3684 held in the documented protected storage, and the keys cannot be modified outside the authorised path. For
3685 example, the verification routine loads its key from a write-protected region and an attempt to overwrite that
3686 key through another interface is refused.

3687  Fail: the requirement is not met if no software-based verification is performed where hardware components are
3688 unavailable; if the keys reside in storage that is not protected; or where the keys can be modified through an
3689 interface other than the authorised path.

3690 Assessment evidence: record of platform hardware-component availability; observation of the verification path;
3691 inspection of the key storage.

3692 6.8.7 [ACC-BM-INT-007]

3693 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-INT-007.

3694 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager supports combined verification using more than one approved
3695 signing algorithm, where the trust anchor is not immutable.

3696 Assessment preparation:

3697  Test environment: the boot manager with verified boot active, a mutable trust anchor, and the configuration
3698 interface exposed.

3699  Required information: the set of approved signing algorithms, the interface for configuring it, and the
3700 authorisation required to change it.

3701  Required tools: a configuration tool.

3702 Assessment activities:

3703  Where the boot manager does not perform verified boot, has no configuration capability, or has an immutable
3704 trust anchor, record the requirement as not applicable and close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.


3705  Inspect the configured set of signing algorithms and confirm each entry is an approved algorithm per
3706 Annex K.

3707  Substitute the configured algorithm through the configuration interface (for example replacing a deprecated
3708 algorithm with another approved one) and confirm the change takes effect in the boot manager's verification
3709 behaviour.

3710  Attempt to change the set without the documented authorisation; confirm rejection.

3711 Assessment verdict:

3712  Pass: the configured set of signing algorithms holds only approved algorithms, the boot manager allows an
3713 approved algorithm to be substituted for another through the authorised interface, and an unauthorised change
3714 is refused. A configured set of one algorithm is acceptable provided the substitution capability is present. For
3715 example, replacing a deprecated approved algorithm with a current approved one through the configuration
3716 interface changes which algorithm the boot manager accepts, while the same change attempted without
3717 authorisation is rejected.

3718  Fail: the requirement is not met if the configured set cannot be changed where the trust anchor is mutable; if it
3719 holds an algorithm that is not approved under Annex K; if an authorised substitution does not take effect; or
3720 where an unauthorised change is accepted.

3721 Assessment evidence: inspection of the configured set; test records of the substitution; records of the unauthorised-
3722 change attempts.

3723 6.8.8 [ACC-BM-INT-008]

3724 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-INT-008.

3725 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager supports combined verification using more than one approved
3726 signing algorithm, where the trust anchor is not immutable.

3727 Assessment preparation:

3728  Test environment: the boot manager with verified boot active and configured for combined verification with
3729 more than one approved algorithm.

3730  Required information: the algorithms used in combination and how a component carries the combined
3731 signatures; the rule by which the combination is judged to pass.

3732  Required tools: boot-stage artefacts carrying the combined signatures, able to render any one of the constituent
3733 signatures invalid or absent.

3734 Assessment activities:

3735  Where the boot manager does not perform verified boot, has no configuration capability, or has an immutable
3736 trust anchor, record the requirement as not applicable and close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

3737  Present a boot-stage artefact whose combined signatures are all valid; confirm verification succeeds.

3738  Present an artefact in which one of the combined signatures is invalid or absent while the others are valid;
3739 confirm verification fails.

3740 Assessment verdict:

3741  Pass: the boot manager verifies a component against more than one approved algorithm in combination,
3742 accepting it only when every constituent signature is valid. For example, a stage carrying both a classical and a
3743 post-quantum signature is accepted when both verify, and is rejected when either one is invalid or missing.

3744  Fail: the requirement is not met if the boot manager cannot verify against more than one algorithm in
3745 combination; or where it accepts a component when one of the combined signatures is invalid or absent,
3746 treating the combination as satisfied by a single algorithm.


3747 Assessment evidence: the combined-verification specification; verification records for the all-valid case and for each
3748 case with one constituent signature invalid or absent.

3749 6.8.9 [ACC-BM-INT-009]

3750 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-INT-009.

3751 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager prevents unauthorised modification of a component between its
3752 verification and its execution, for the TOCTOU threats within its documented threat model.

3753 Assessment preparation:

3754  Test environment: the boot manager with inspection access to the memory region holding a verified
3755 component between verification and execution.

3756  Required information: the memory-protection mechanism applied between verification and execution (for
3757 example locked page tables, or execute-in-place from write-protected storage); the TOCTOU threats in scope
3758 per the security analysis in Annex B. Physical-attack TOCTOU on the boot medium (T-PHYS-5, T-PHYS-6)
3759 is assessed under Annex D and is outside this assessment.

3760  Required tools: a means to attempt modification of the component's memory concurrently with the window
3761 between verification and execution.

3762 Assessment activities:

3763  Where the boot manager has no verified boot capability, record the requirement as not applicable and close
3764 this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

3765  During the window between a component's verification and its execution, attempt to modify the component's
3766 memory through each in-scope access path (for example DMA, other processor cores where applicable,
3767 peripheral-initiated access).

3768  Confirm the memory-protection mechanism prevents the modification, or detects it and halts execution, and
3769 that it stays in effect for the full window without early release.

3770 Assessment verdict:

3771  Pass: across the in-scope TOCTOU vectors, a modification attempted between a component's verification and
3772 its execution is prevented, or detected and the boot halted, and the protection holds for the whole window. For
3773 example, a DMA write into a verified stage's memory after it has been checked but before control passes to it
3774 is blocked, or detected and the boot stopped, rather than allowing the altered stage to run.

3775  Fail: the requirement is not met if a modification during the window succeeds undetected; if the protection
3776 mechanism releases before the component executes; or where an in-scope vector is left unprotected.

3777 Assessment evidence: the memory-protection specification; records of the concurrent-modification tests per in-scope
3778 vector.

3779 6.8.10 [ACC-BM-INT-010]

3780 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-INT-010.

3781 Assessment objective: verify that, where the hardware platform supports protected memory, the boot manager loads
3782 components into protected memory before verification.

3783 Assessment preparation:

3784  Test environment: the boot manager on a platform with documented protected-memory capability (for
3785 example locked memory regions or enclaves).

3786  Required information: the platform's protected-memory support and the mechanism used.

3787  Required tools: a tool to identify the protected memory regions.


3788 Assessment activities:

3789  Where the boot manager has no verified boot capability, or the hardware platform does not support protected
3790 memory, record the requirement as not applicable and close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

3791  Observe the component-loading sequence and confirm components are placed into the protected region before
3792 verification begins.

3793  Attempt to modify the component content during the verification window through an unprotected access path;
3794 confirm the attempt fails because of the protection.

3795 Assessment verdict:

3796  Pass: on a platform that supports protected memory, each component is placed into the protected region before
3797 it is verified, and an attempt to modify it through an unprotected path fails. For example, a stage is loaded into
3798 a locked memory region and then verified in place, and a write to that region from outside the protection
3799 during the verification window does not take effect.

3800  Fail: the requirement is not met if a component is verified before being placed into protected memory; or
3801 where a modification through an unprotected path succeeds during the verification window.

3802 Assessment evidence: record of the platform's protected-memory capability; observation of the loading sequence;
3803 records of the modification attempts.

3804 6.8.11 [ACC-BM-INT-011]

3805 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-INT-011.

3806 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager protects the integrity and authenticity of sensitive configuration
3807 settings.

3808 Assessment preparation:

3809  Test environment: the boot manager with configuration capability and sensitive configuration items populated.

3810  Required information: the sensitive configuration settings and the protection mechanism for each (hardware-
3811 protected storage, or authenticated encryption with freshness protection and non-deterministic encryption); the
3812 cryptographic parameters per Annex K.

3813  Required tools: a storage inspection tool; a means to tamper with a stored setting; a means to analyse
3814 ciphertext for determinism.

3815 Assessment activities:

3816  Where the boot manager has no configuration capability, record the requirement as not applicable and close
3817 this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

3818  For each sensitive configuration setting, identify the protection mechanism and confirm it matches the
3819 declared category.

3820  Tamper with a protected setting in its stored form and confirm the boot manager detects the alteration and does
3821 not act on the tampered value.

3822  Where hardware-protected storage is used, inspect the storage and confirm the setting is not accessible or
3823 modifiable outside the protected path.

3824  Where authenticated encryption is used, confirm the algorithm is listed in Annex K; confirm that encrypting
3825 equal values produces differing ciphertext across events (unique nonces); and confirm freshness by replaying a
3826 prior protected value and observing rejection.


3827 Assessment verdict:

3828  Pass: each sensitive setting is protected by its declared mechanism, a tampered setting is detected and not acted
3829 upon, and where authenticated encryption is used the algorithm is from Annex K, nonces are not reused, and a
3830 replayed value is rejected. For example, altering a stored verification policy is caught and the boot manager
3831 falls back to the protected value rather than the tampered one, and a captured earlier ciphertext for that setting
3832 is refused on replay.

3833  Fail: the requirement is not met if a sensitive setting lacks its declared protection; if a tampered setting is acted
3834 upon undetected; if an authenticated-encryption mechanism uses an algorithm outside Annex K, reuses
3835 nonces, or accepts a replayed value.

3836 Assessment evidence: mapping of settings to protection mechanisms; records of storage inspection; ciphertext non-
3837 determinism test; replay-rejection test.

3838 6.8.12 [ACC-BM-INT-012]

3839 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-INT-012.

3840 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager restores secure default configuration settings when configuration
3841 corruption is detected, where technically feasible.

3842 Assessment preparation:

3843  Test environment: the boot manager with configuration capability and the ability to inject configuration
3844 corruption.

3845  Required information: the corruption-detection mechanism; the secure default configuration; the documented
3846 technical-feasibility limitations (for example restrictions from immutable elements).

3847  Required tools: a means to inject configuration corruption.

3848 Assessment activities:

3849  Where the boot manager has no configuration capability, record the requirement as not applicable and close
3850 this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

3851  Inject corruption into each configurable category and confirm the boot manager detects it. Confirm that, where
3852 technically feasible, the boot manager restores the secure default for the affected category.

3853  For categories documented as outside technical feasibility (for example values held in immutable e-fuses or
3854 ROM), confirm the documented handling applies rather than a restoration.

3855 Assessment verdict:

3856  Pass: corruption is detected in every configurable category, the secure default is restored wherever restoration
3857 is technically feasible, and the documented limitation applies to the categories declared infeasible. For
3858 example, corrupting a mutable boot-policy setting is detected and the setting reverts to its secure default, while
3859 a value fixed in an e-fuse is handled as documented rather than restored.

3860  Fail: the requirement is not met if corruption goes undetected in a configurable category; if restoration fails in
3861 a category documented as feasible; or where a category claimed infeasible has no supporting documentation.

3862 Assessment evidence: records of corruption injection; records of restoration outcome; record of feasibility
3863 documentation.

3864 6.8.13 [ACC-BM-INT-013]

3865 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-INT-013.

3866 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager authenticates network boot servers using cryptographic certificates
3867 before accepting actions or configuration data from them.


3868 Assessment preparation:

3869  Test environment: the boot manager configured for network boot in a controlled environment with distinct
3870 authorised and unauthorised server identities.

3871  Required information: the server authentication mechanism (certificate format, trust roots, verification
3872 algorithm) and the actions and configuration data it governs.

3873  Required tools: a controlled network boot server able to present a valid certificate, an untrusted certificate, or
3874 none.

3875 Assessment activities:

3876  Where the boot manager has no network boot capability, record the requirement as not applicable and close
3877 this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

3878  Connect the boot manager to a server presenting a valid trusted certificate; confirm it accepts actions and
3879 configuration data from the server.

3880  Connect to a server presenting no certificate; confirm the boot manager rejects the session before any action is
3881 launched or data accepted.

3882  Connect to a server presenting a certificate from an untrusted root; confirm rejection.

3883 Assessment verdict:

3884  Pass: the boot manager accepts actions or configuration data only from a server that presents a
3885 cryptographically valid certificate chaining to a trusted root, and rejects a server that presents none or one from
3886 an untrusted root before anything is accepted. For example, a network boot proceeds from the server with a
3887 trusted certificate, while an attempt from a server with no certificate is dropped before any boot action.

3888  Fail: the requirement is not met if an action is launched or configuration data accepted from a server without a
3889 valid trusted certificate; or where authentication occurs only after data has been accepted.

3890 Assessment evidence: the server authentication specification; connection records per scenario.

3891 6.8.14 [ACC-BM-INT-014]

3892 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-INT-014.

3893 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager rejects network boot connections presenting invalid or revoked
3894 server certificates, and rejects expired certificates where a dependable source of time is available.

3895 Assessment preparation:

3896  Test environment: the boot manager configured for network boot with access to the certificate-validation
3897 reference data it uses (CRL, OCSP, or a documented equivalent).

3898  Required information: the certificate-validity checks applied; the revocation mechanism; whether a dependable
3899 source of time is available to the boot manager (see the assumption in Annex B, clause B.3.2).

3900  Required tools: a controlled server able to present certificates in each failure state (invalid signature, revoked,
3901 malformed, not-yet-valid, and expired).

3902 Assessment activities:

3903  Where the boot manager has no network boot capability, record the requirement as not applicable and close
3904 this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

3905  For each invalid and revoked certificate state, connect the boot manager to the server and confirm the session
3906 is rejected before any network boot action.

3907  Confirm revocation status is checked through the documented mechanism (for example CRL retrieval, OCSP
3908 query, or consultation of a local revocation store); where the boot manager operates offline, confirm the offline
3909 revocation mechanism is present.


3910  Where a dependable source of time is available, present an expired certificate and confirm rejection. Where no
3911 dependable source of time is available, confirm expiration is not relied upon and revocation checking still
3912 applies.

3913 Assessment verdict:

3914  Pass: invalid and revoked server certificates are rejected before any network boot action, revocation is checked
3915 through the documented mechanism, and an expired certificate is rejected wherever a dependable source of
3916 time is available. For example, a connection offering a revoked certificate is dropped after the revocation
3917 check, and on a platform with trusted time an expired certificate is likewise refused.

3918  Fail: the requirement is not met if an invalid or revoked certificate is accepted; if the revocation mechanism is
3919 absent or bypassable; or where, with a dependable source of time available, an expired certificate is accepted.

3920 Assessment evidence: the list of certificate failure states; connection records per state; record of exercising the
3921 revocation mechanism; record of the time-source condition under which expiration was assessed.

3922 6.8.15 [ACC-BM-INT-015]

3923 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-INT-015.

3924 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager validates that network configuration and boot-related responses
3925 originate from authorised infrastructure.

3926 Assessment preparation:

3927  Test environment: the boot manager configured for network boot in an environment that can present both
3928 authorised and rogue response sources.

3929  Required information: the response types (DHCP responses, PXE boot offers, network-provided boot
3930 configuration data, and similar) and the authorisation mechanism applied to each (for example signed
3931 responses, authenticated transport, or trusted source enforcement).

3932  Required tools: response injection tools representing authorised and rogue sources.

3933 Assessment activities:

3934  Where the boot manager has no network boot capability, record the requirement as not applicable and close
3935 this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

3936  For each response type, present a response from an authorised source and confirm it is accepted.

3937  Present a response of the same type from a rogue source and confirm it is rejected.

3938  Where a rogue response can race an authorised one, confirm the boot manager takes the authorised response.

3939 Assessment verdict:

3940  Pass: for every response type, the boot manager accepts responses from authorised infrastructure and rejects
3941 rogue responses, and where the two race it takes the authorised one. For example, a PXE boot offer from the
3942 authorised server is acted upon while a rogue PXE offer injected on the same segment is ignored, even when
3943 the rogue response arrives first.

3944  Fail: the requirement is not met if a rogue response is accepted for any response type; or where a race between
3945 an authorised and a rogue response results in the rogue one being used.

3946 Assessment evidence: the list of response types; records of authorised and rogue inputs per type; records of the race-
3947 condition tests.

3948 6.8.16 [ACC-BM-INT-016]

3949 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-INT-016.


3950 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager enforces rollback protection when verifying boot stages and
3951 configuration data.

3952 Assessment preparation:

3953  Test environment: the boot manager with update or configuration capability and representative artefacts at the
3954 current and at earlier versions.

3955  Required information: the rollback-protection mechanism (version counter, signed version metadata); where
3956 anti-rollback is configurable by the OEM, the documented policy bounding that configuration (see the note in
3957 clause 5.3).

3958  Required tools: a tool to generate artefacts at chosen versions.

3959 Assessment activities:

3960  Where the boot manager has neither update nor configuration capability, record the requirement as not
3961 applicable and close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

3962  Present a boot stage or configuration artefact correctly signed but at a version earlier than the current one;
3963 confirm the boot manager rejects it.

3964  Present the current or a newer authorised version; confirm acceptance.

3965  Where anti-rollback is configurable by the OEM, confirm the configurable path stays within the documented
3966 policy and does not disable rollback protection for stages where the policy requires it.

3967 Assessment verdict:

3968  Pass: an earlier-version artefact is rejected while the current or a newer authorised version is accepted, and any
3969 OEM-configurable relaxation stays within the documented policy. For example, a correctly signed boot stage
3970 carrying a version below the recorded one is refused, while the current version loads, and an OEM setting
3971 cannot switch off rollback protection where the policy mandates it.

3972  Fail: the requirement is not met if an earlier-version artefact is accepted; if a newer authorised version is
3973 rejected; or where OEM configuration disables rollback protection in a case the policy forbids.

3974 Assessment evidence: records of the version tests; record of the OEM policy inspection.

3975 6.8.17 [ACC-BM-INT-017]

3976 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-INT-017.

3977 Assessment objective: verify that, at HIGH security profile, the boot manager stores anti-rollback counters in
3978 hardware-backed or tamper-evident storage and verifies signed version metadata before accepting updates.

3979 Assessment preparation:

3980  Test environment: the boot manager at HIGH security profile with update capability and the anti-rollback
3981 counter storage inspectable.

3982  Required information: the counter storage mechanism (hardware-backed or tamper-evident) and the signed
3983 version metadata format.

3984  Required tools: a counter storage inspection tool; a tool to produce version metadata that is valid, altered, or
3985 unsigned.

3986 Assessment activities:

3987  Where the boot manager is not at HIGH security profile or has no update capability, record the requirement as
3988 not applicable and close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

3989  Inspect the counter storage and confirm it is hardware-backed or tamper-evident per the declared mechanism.


3990  Submit an update with correctly signed version metadata at a version at or above the counter; confirm
3991 acceptance.

3992  Submit an update whose version metadata is altered after signing, and separately one with unsigned metadata;
3993 confirm each is rejected before any update action.

3994  Attempt to decrement the counter through any interface; confirm rejection.

3995 Assessment verdict:

3996  Pass: the anti-rollback counter is held in hardware-backed or tamper-evident storage, signed version metadata
3997 is verified before an update is accepted, altered or unsigned metadata is rejected, and the counter cannot be
3998 decremented. For example, an update carrying validly signed metadata at or above the stored counter installs,
3999 while one whose metadata was changed after signing is refused and an attempt to roll the counter back through
4000 a maintenance interface fails.

4001  Fail: the requirement is not met if the counter storage is neither hardware-backed nor tamper-evident; if
4002 version metadata is not verified, or verified only after the update has begun; if altered or unsigned metadata is
4003 accepted; or where the counter can be decremented.

4004 Assessment evidence: inspection of the counter storage; submission records per metadata variant; records of the
4005 counter-decrement attempts.

4006 6.8.18 [ACC-BM-INT-018]

4007 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-INT-018.

4008 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager validates a certificate chain to a trusted root before using a
4009 certificate in a security-relevant operation.

4010 Assessment preparation:

4011  Test environment: the boot manager configured to use certificate chains for a security-relevant operation, with
4012 the trusted-root set in place.

4013  Required information: the trusted-root set; the chain-validation policy (chain from end-entity to root, validity-
4014 period checking, revocation, policy constraints); whether a dependable source of time is available (see the
4015 assumption in Annex B, clause B.3.2).

4016  Required tools: a certificate generation tool able to produce chains rooted in trusted and untrusted roots, with
4017 and without each validation property.

4018 Assessment activities:

4019  Where the boot manager does not use certificate chains for security-relevant operations, record the
4020 requirement as not applicable and close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

4021  Present a certificate with a valid chain to a trusted root, within validity, not revoked, and policy-compliant;
4022 confirm acceptance.

4023  Present certificates each failing one validation property: a chain ending at an untrusted root; a revoked
4024 intermediate; a policy violation at some level; confirm rejection in each case.

4025  Where a dependable source of time is available, present a chain with an expired certificate and confirm
4026 rejection; where no dependable source of time is available, confirm validity-period checking is not relied upon
4027 while the other checks still apply.

4028 Assessment verdict:

4029  Pass: only a certificate whose chain reaches a trusted root and meets the applicable validation criteria is
4030 accepted for a security-relevant operation, and each failure class is rejected.


4031  For example, a certificate chaining to a trusted root and passing revocation and policy checks is accepted,
4032 while one chaining to an untrusted root, and one whose intermediate is revoked, are each refused; on a
4033 platform with trusted time an expired chain is also refused.

4034  Fail: the requirement is not met if a chain that does not reach a trusted root is accepted; if a revoked or policy-
4035 violating chain is accepted; or where, with a dependable source of time available, an expired chain is accepted.

4036 Assessment evidence: the trusted-root set; test records for the valid chain and for each failure class; record of the time-
4037 source condition under which validity-period checking was assessed.

4038 6.8.19 [ACC-BM-INT-019]

4039 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-INT-019.

4040 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager supports revocation of mutable compromised keys and certificates.

4041 Assessment preparation:

4042  Test environment: the boot manager with verified boot and measured boot supporting remote attestation, and a
4043 mutable trust anchor or certificate store.

4044  Required information: the revocation mechanism (revocation database, CRL, OCSP, authenticated
4045 configuration update, or revocation metadata); the revocation-slot constraints.

4046  Required tools: a tool to generate revocation data.

4047 Assessment activities:

4048  Where the boot manager does not provide verified boot and measured boot with remote attestation, or its keys
4049 and certificates are immutable, record the requirement as not applicable and close this assessment per
4050 clause 5.1.3.

4051  Designate a previously valid key or certificate as compromised and apply revocation through the documented
4052 mechanism.

4053  Attempt to use the revoked key or certificate in a security-relevant operation; confirm it is accepted before
4054 revocation and rejected after.

4055  Confirm the revocation state survives a power cycle and cannot be bypassed by downgrading or replaying the
4056 pre-revocation state.

4057 Assessment verdict:

4058  Pass: applying revocation through the documented mechanism causes a previously valid key or certificate to
4059 be rejected, and the revocation state persists across power cycles and resists downgrade or replay, within the
4060 documented slot constraints. For example, a key that verified a stage before revocation no longer does so after
4061 a revocation entry is applied, and re-presenting the earlier pre-revocation state does not restore acceptance.

4062  Fail: the requirement is not met if a revoked key or certificate is still accepted after revocation; if the
4063 revocation state is lost on power cycle; or where the pre-revocation state can be downgraded or replayed to
4064 bypass it.

4065 Assessment evidence: the revocation-mechanism specification; usage records before and after revocation; records of
4066 the persistence and bypass attempts.

4067 6.8.20 [ACC-BM-INT-020]

4068 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-INT-020.

4069 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager uses cryptographic algorithms, key sizes, and parameters in
4070 accordance with Annex K.


4071 Assessment preparation:

4072  Test environment: the boot manager with its cryptographic operations observable.

4073  Required information: the inventory of cryptographic algorithms, key sizes, and parameters the boot manager
4074 uses, with reference to Annex K.

4075  Required tools: a means to inspect the algorithm, key size, and parameters of each cryptographic operation.

4076 Assessment activities:

4077  For each cryptographic operation the boot manager performs, observe and record the algorithm, key size, and
4078 parameters used.

4079  Compare each against Annex K and confirm the combination is listed and within the applicable deprecation
4080 schedule.

4081 Assessment verdict:

4082  Pass: every algorithm, key size, and parameter combination the boot manager uses is listed in Annex K and
4083 within its deprecation schedule. For example, the signature verification and hashing operations observed
4084 during boot all resolve to Annex K entries that have not passed their deprecation date.

4085  Fail: the requirement is not met if any combination the boot manager uses is absent from Annex K, or has
4086 passed its deprecation schedule.

4087 Assessment evidence: the inventory of cryptographic operations with their Annex K cross-reference.

4088 6.8.21 [ACC-BM-INT-021]

4089 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-INT-021.

4090 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager supports migration between approved cryptographic algorithms.

4091 Assessment preparation:

4092  Test environment: the boot manager configured to operate with at least one approved cryptographic algorithm
4093 and capable of operating with at least one alternative approved algorithm.

4094  Required information: the algorithm-migration mechanism (configuration metadata, multi-algorithm support,
4095 controlled algorithm selection, or boot manager replacement); the approved algorithms supported, with
4096 reference to Annex K.

4097  Required tools: tooling to invoke the migration mechanism as documented (for example a metadata update
4098 tool, an algorithm selection interface, or the update mechanism where migration is achieved through boot
4099 manager replacement).

4100 Assessment activities:

4101  Where the boot manager has no update capability or its trust anchor is immutable, record the requirement as
4102 not applicable and close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

4103  Confirm at least one approved algorithm is in active use as the verification algorithm.

4104  Through the documented migration mechanism, transition the boot manager from the current approved
4105 algorithm to a different approved algorithm from Annex K.

4106  Confirm that after migration the boot manager verifies under the new algorithm, that artefacts signed under the
4107 new algorithm are accepted, and that artefacts signed under the previous algorithm are handled per the
4108 documented policy (for example a grace period, immediate rejection, or a documented transition).

4109  Where concurrent multi-algorithm support is documented, confirm artefacts signed under any active algorithm
4110 are verified.


4111 Assessment verdict:

4112  Pass: the documented migration mechanism moves the boot manager from one approved algorithm to another,
4113 verification afterwards operates under the new algorithm, and artefacts under the previous algorithm are
4114 handled per the documented transition policy. For example, migrating from one Annex K signature algorithm
4115 to another through the documented mechanism causes newly signed artefacts to verify under the new
4116 algorithm, while artefacts under the old algorithm follow the documented grace-period or rejection policy.

4117  Fail: the requirement is not met if no functional migration mechanism exists; if verification does not operate
4118 under the new algorithm after migration; or where the handling of artefacts signed under the previous
4119 algorithm diverges from the documented policy.

4120 Assessment evidence: specification of the algorithm-migration mechanism; records of verification before and after
4121 migration; record of the migration policy; records of multi-algorithm verification where applicable.

4122 6.8.22 [ACC-BM-INT-022]

4123 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-INT-022.

4124 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager uses collision-resistant and preimage-resistant one-way functions
4125 for origin authentication and verification of boot code provenance.

4126 Assessment preparation:

4127  Test environment: the boot manager with verified boot or measured boot active.

4128  Required information: the one-way functions used for origin authentication and provenance verification, with
4129 reference to Annex K for collision- and preimage-resistance; any function used only for integrity protection in
4130 combination with device-specific keys.

4131  Required tools: a means to inspect the one-way functions invoked during boot.

4132 Assessment activities:

4133  Where the boot manager has neither verified nor measured boot capability, record the requirement as not
4134 applicable and close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

4135  Observe the one-way functions invoked for origin authentication and provenance verification; confirm each is
4136 listed in Annex K and is collision-resistant and preimage-resistant.

4137  Confirm no such function has an Annex K deprecation applying at the assessment date.

4138  Where a non-collision-resistant function is used, confirm it is used only for integrity protection in combination
4139 with a device-specific key, and not for origin authentication or provenance verification.

4140 Assessment verdict:

4141  Pass: every one-way function used for origin authentication and provenance verification is collision-resistant,
4142 preimage-resistant, Annex K approved, and within its deprecation schedule, and any non-collision-resistant
4143 function is confined to integrity protection with a device-specific key. For example, boot-stage provenance is
4144 established with a SHA-2 or SHA-3 function from Annex K, while a non-collision-resistant construction such
4145 as GHASH appears only in an integrity check bound to a device-specific key.

4146  Fail: the requirement is not met if a function used for origin authentication or provenance verification is not
4147 collision- and preimage-resistant, is absent from Annex K, or has passed its deprecation schedule; or where a
4148 non-collision-resistant function is used for origin authentication or provenance verification.

4149 Assessment evidence: the inventory of invoked functions with their Annex K cross-reference and their purpose (origin
4150 authentication or provenance verification, or integrity protection with a device-specific key).


4151 6.8.23 [ACC-BM-INT-023]

4152 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-INT-023.

4153 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager supports replacement of trust anchors used for boot verification.

4154 Assessment preparation:

4155  Test environment: the boot manager with update capability and a mutable trust anchor store.

4156  Required information: the trust-anchor replacement mechanism (for example an authenticated update path, a
4157 key provisioning interface, or a recovery procedure); the trust anchors and the procedure for replacing each;
4158 the authority required to authorise a replacement.

4159  Required tools: the trust-anchor replacement tool or interface as documented; signing material under both the
4160 existing and the replacement trust anchor.

4161 Assessment activities:

4162  Where the boot manager has no update capability or its trust anchor is immutable, record the requirement as
4163 not applicable and close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

4164  Confirm the trust anchor is mutable and can be replaced through the documented authorised path.

4165  Replace the trust anchor with a new anchor and confirm the boot manager then verifies artefacts signed under
4166 the new anchor.

4167  Confirm artefacts signed under the prior anchor are handled per the documented policy after replacement (for
4168 example immediate rejection, a documented transition, or a configurable grace period).

4169  Attempt a trust-anchor replacement through an unauthorised path; confirm rejection.

4170 Assessment verdict:

4171  Pass: the trust anchor can be replaced through the documented authorised path, verification afterwards
4172 operates under the new anchor, artefacts under the prior anchor follow the documented policy, and an
4173 unauthorised replacement is refused. For example, replacing the anchor through the authenticated update path
4174 causes artefacts signed under the new anchor to verify, while artefacts under the old anchor follow the
4175 documented grace-period or rejection policy and an unauthorised replacement attempt is rejected.

4176  Fail: the requirement is not met if the trust anchor cannot be replaced through the authorised path; if
4177 verification does not operate under the new anchor after replacement; if handling of artefacts under the prior
4178 anchor diverges from the documented policy; or where an unauthorised replacement is accepted.

4179 Assessment evidence: record of the trust-anchor replacement; verification records before and after replacement; record
4180 of the rejection of the unauthorised attempt; documentation of the replacement authority.

4181 6.8.24 [ACC-BM-INT-024]

4182 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-INT-024.

4183 Assessment objective: verify that the storage holding trust anchors, key enrolment records, and policy database
4184 contents used by the code execution authority is protected against modification by entities not authorised by the
4185 documented authority model.

4186 Assessment preparation:

4187  Test environment: the boot manager with the code execution authority active, the storage holding authority
4188 data open to inspection, and at least one unauthorised entity available to attempt modification.

4189  Required information:

4190 a) the storage location for trust anchors, key enrolment records, and policy database contents;


4191 b) the protection mechanism applied to that storage (for example a hardware-protected region, signed
4192 configuration, or authenticated update); and

4193 c) the authority model identifying which entities may modify each data category.

4194  Required tools: a storage-inspection tool appropriate to the storage technology (for example a flash-region
4195 reader or a secure-element command interface); a means to attempt modification through each documented
4196 and undocumented interface to the storage.

4197 Assessment activities:

4198  Where the boot manager implements no code execution authority mechanism requiring stored authority data,
4199 record the requirement as not applicable and close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

4200  Inspect the documented storage and confirm trust anchors, key enrolment records, and policy database
4201 contents are held there as described. The protection of any trusted certificate store falling within this storage is
4202 assessed under ACC-BM-AC-007 (clause 6.6.7); the present assessment covers the authority data storage more
4203 broadly.

4204  For each unauthorised entity in the authority model, attempt to modify each data category through the
4205 documented interfaces; confirm rejection.

4206  Attempt to modify each data category through undocumented interfaces (direct storage write, debug interfaces
4207 where exposed, alternative configuration paths); confirm rejection or detection.

4208  Where the protection relies on cryptographic verification, confirm a modification with an invalid signature is
4209 rejected, and a modification with a valid signature from an unauthorised signer is rejected.

4210 Assessment verdict:

4211  Pass: the authority data is held only in the documented protected storage, and every attempt to modify it by an
4212 entity outside the authority model is rejected or detected, through documented and undocumented interfaces
4213 alike. For example, a write to the policy database from an entity the authority model does not permit is refused
4214 over the configuration interface and over an exposed debug interface, and a signed change from an
4215 unauthorised signer is likewise rejected.

4216  Fail: the requirement is not met if an unauthorised entity modifies any authority data category through any
4217 interface; or where authority data is found held outside the documented protection mechanism.

4218 Assessment evidence: the specification of the authority-data storage and its protection mechanism; the record of
4219 authority-model entities; records of the modification attempts per entity per data category, with the outcome of each.

4220 6.9 Data minimisation

4221 6.9.0 Overview of requirements addressed in clause 6.9

4222 The present clause specifies assessment criteria for the requirements in clause 5.9.

4223 Table 6.9.0-1: Requirements addressed in clause 6.9

Requirement Profile applicability
REQ-BM-DM- 001 MEDIUM, HIGH (if implemented)
REQ-BM-DM- 002 MEDIUM, HIGH (if network boot)
4224

4225 6.9.1 [ACC-BM-DM-001]

4226 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-DM-001.

4227 Assessment objective: verify that information disclosed by the boot manager to network infrastructure during boot is
4228 limited to what is necessary for boot operations.


4229 Assessment preparation:

4230  Test environment: the boot manager configured for network boot in a controlled network environment
4231 permitting passive traffic capture.

4232  Required information: documentation of network boot protocols used, the list of fields populated by the boot
4233 manager in each protocol exchange, and the justification for each field.

4234  Required tools: network traffic analyser; protocol-aware decoder for the network boot protocols in use (e.g.
4235 DHCP, PXE, TFTP, HTTP(S)).

4236 Assessment activities:

4237  Where the boot manager does not perform network boot, record the requirement as not applicable and close
4238 this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

4239  Capture the complete network traffic generated by the boot manager during a successful network boot, from
4240 first transmission to successful handoff.

4241  Parse each outbound message and enumerate the information fields populated by the boot manager.

4242  Verify that each populated field is justified by a documented boot operation and that no sensitive or
4243 unnecessary information is included (cross-check with ACC-BM-DM-002 for the sensitive-information
4244 categories).

4245  Repeat the capture under documented failure modes (e.g. no response from server, invalid response) and
4246 confirm that the information disclosed does not expand under those conditions.

4247 Assessment verdict:

4248  Pass: every information field the boot manager transmits to network infrastructure is justified by a documented
4249 boot operation, and no sensitive or unnecessary information is disclosed under nominal or failure conditions.
4250 For example, a network boot that requests only the files required, negotiates only the protocol parameters
4251 needed to establish the session, and exposes only identifiers such as the MAC address and device class
4252 discloses nothing further when the server fails to respond or returns an invalid response.

4253  Fail: the requirement is not met if the boot manager transmits a field not justified by a documented boot
4254 operation; if it discloses sensitive or unnecessary information; or where the information disclosed expands
4255 under a documented failure mode.

4256 Assessment evidence: captured network traces; field-by-field justification table; records of failure-mode capture.

4257 6.9.2 [ACC-BM-DM-002]

4258 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-DM-002.

4259 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager does not disclose sensitive device information on the network and
4260 that temporary network credentials are not retained beyond their required use.

4261 Assessment preparation:

4262  Test environment: the boot manager in a controlled network environment supporting traffic capture and post-
4263 boot inspection of the handoff state.

4264  Required information: the enumeration of sensitive device information (at minimum: hardware serial numbers,
4265 internal configuration, diagnostic data); a statement of which temporary credentials (if any) are used during
4266 network boot and their intended lifetime.

4267  Required tools: network traffic analyser; inspection tool for the boot manager's handoff state (memory,
4268 registers, passed structures as applicable to the platform).

4269 Assessment activities:

4270  Where the boot manager does not perform network boot, record the requirement as not applicable and close
4271 this assessment per clause 5.1.3.


4272  Capture the network traffic generated by the boot manager during a complete network boot.

4273  Search the captured traffic for instances of the documented sensitive-information categories; confirm none are
4274 disclosed.

4275  Where temporary network credentials (e.g. session tokens, ephemeral keys, bearer tokens) are used, inspect the
4276 handoff state after boot completion and confirm that those credentials are neither retained in memory nor
4277 passed to the operating system.

4278  Where network boot is executed under failure modes, confirm that sensitive information is not disclosed as
4279 part of error or diagnostic responses.

4280 Assessment verdict:

4281  Pass: none of the documented sensitive-information categories appears in the captured network traffic under
4282 nominal or failure conditions, and any temporary network credentials used during boot are not retained beyond
4283 their required use. For example, a complete network boot exposes no hardware serial number, internal
4284 configuration, or diagnostic data, and a session token used to fetch the boot image is absent from the handoff
4285 state and is not passed to the operating system.

4286  Fail: the requirement is not met if a documented sensitive-information category appears in network traffic
4287 under nominal or failure conditions; if a temporary network credential persists in the handoff state after boot
4288 completion; or where such a credential is retained beyond its intended lifetime.

4289 Assessment evidence: list of sensitive-information categories; network trace records with search results; records of
4290 state inspection at handoff for temporary credential retention.

4291 6.10 Availability protection

4292 6.10.0 Overview of requirements addressed in clause 6.10

4293 The present clause specifies assessment criteria for the requirements in clause 5.10.

4294 Table 6.10.0-1: Requirements addressed in clause 6.10

Requirement Profile applicability
REQ-BM-AP- 001 All (if configuration capability)
REQ-BM-AP-002 HIGH
REQ-BM-AP- 003 All
REQ-BM-AP-004 MEDIUM, HIGH (if verified or network boot)
REQ-BM-AP- 005 All
REQ-BM-AP-006 MEDIUM, HIGH
REQ-BM-AP- 007 MEDIUM, HIGH (not in immutable memory)
REQ-BM-AP- 008 All (if recovery capability)
REQ-BM-AP- 009 MEDIUM, HIGH (if network boot)
REQ-BM-AP-010 MEDIUM, HIGH (if verified or measured boot with logging)
REQ-BM-AP- 011 All
REQ-BM-AP-012 All (if recovery capability)
REQ-BM-AP- 013 MEDIUM, HIGH (if verified boot)
REQ-BM-AP-014 All
REQ-BM-AP- 015 All (if recovery capability)
REQ-BM-AP- 016 MEDIUM, HIGH (if update and recovery capability)
4295

4296 6.10.1 [ACC-BM-AP-001]

4297 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AP-001.

4298 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager supports fallback to a previous known-good configuration.


4299 Assessment preparation:

4300  Test environment: the boot manager with a current configuration and a documented known-good configuration
4301 stored.

4302  Required information: the specification of the known-good configuration mechanism, the fallback trigger
4303 conditions, and the fallback procedure.

4304  Required tools: configuration-corruption or configuration-replacement tool; fallback-trigger tool.

4305 Assessment activities:

4306  Where the boot manager has no configuration capability, record the requirement as not applicable and close
4307 this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

4308  Corrupt or replace the current configuration in a manner documented as triggering fallback.

4309  Invoke the fallback trigger and confirm the boot manager boots using the known-good configuration.

4310  Confirm the known-good configuration is not corrupted by the trigger or fallback itself.

4311 Assessment verdict:

4312  Pass: the boot manager returns to the documented known-good configuration when the documented fallback
4313 trigger occurs, and the known-good configuration remains intact after fallback. For example, a boot manager
4314 that detects a corrupted active configuration, boots from the stored known-good configuration, and leaves that
4315 known-good copy unmodified satisfies the requirement.

4316  Fail: the requirement is not met if fallback does not occur on the documented trigger; if the boot manager
4317 boots from a configuration other than the known-good one; or where the known-good configuration is lost or
4318 corrupted by the trigger or the fallback itself.

4319 Assessment evidence: record of the known-good configuration; test records of corruption and fallback.

4320 6.10.2 [ACC-BM-AP-002]

4321 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AP-002.

4322 Assessment objective: verify that, at HIGH security profile, the boot manager automatically recovers from
4323 interruptions during the update process.

4324 Assessment preparation:

4325  Test environment: the boot manager at HIGH security profile, configured to perform updates.

4326  Required information: the enumeration of interruption classes during update (power loss, transport
4327 interruption, intermediate-stage failure); the documented recovery mechanism for each.

4328  Required tools: interruption-injection tools for each documented class (e.g. power cut at arbitrary update
4329 stages).

4330 Assessment activities:

4331  Where the boot manager is not at HIGH security profile, record the requirement as not applicable and close
4332 this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

4333  For each interruption class, induce the interruption at representative points during an update and confirm the
4334 boot manager automatically recovers to either the pre-update or post-update state without manual intervention.

4335  Confirm the resulting state is consistent (no split state with part of the update applied).

4336  Confirm recovery does not require operations outside the boot manager's control.


4337 Assessment verdict:

4338  Pass: the boot manager automatically recovers to a consistent pre-update or post-update state, without manual
4339 intervention, for every documented interruption class. For example, a boot manager interrupted by power loss
4340 midway through an update that resumes on the next boot to a fully pre-update or fully post-update state, with
4341 no operator action, satisfies the requirement.

4342  Fail: the requirement is not met if an interruption leaves the boot manager in an inconsistent or split state; if
4343 recovery requires manual intervention; or where recovery depends on operations outside the boot manager's
4344 control.

4345 Assessment evidence: enumeration of interruption classes; injection records per class; records of state inspection after
4346 interruption.

4347 6.10.3 [ACC-BM-AP-003]

4348 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AP-003.

4349 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager enforces timeouts to prevent indefinite blocking during boot-
4350 related operations.

4351 Assessment preparation:

4352  Test environment: the boot manager with control over the response latency of its inputs (network peers,
4353 peripherals, storage).

4354  Required information: the enumeration of boot-related operations subject to timeout; each timeout value.

4355  Required tools: response-latency control tool (e.g. slow-responding emulator); time measurement.

4356 Assessment activities:

4357  For each enumerated operation, delay the input source beyond the documented timeout and measure the boot
4358 manager's response.

4359  Confirm the boot manager terminates the operation at or near the documented timeout and does not block
4360 indefinitely.

4361  Confirm the boot manager's subsequent behaviour is as documented (e.g. fallback, halt, error state).

4362 Assessment verdict:

4363  Pass: every enumerated boot-related operation is terminated at or near its documented timeout, the boot
4364 manager does not block indefinitely on any documented input, and it proceeds afterwards to its documented
4365 behaviour. For example, a boot manager awaiting a network response that halts the attempt at the documented
4366 timeout and falls back to local boot rather than waiting indefinitely satisfies the requirement.

4367  Fail: the requirement is not met if an enumerated operation blocks beyond its documented timeout; if any
4368 documented input can cause the boot manager to block indefinitely; or where the post-timeout behaviour is
4369 inconsistent with the documentation.

4370 Assessment evidence: enumeration of operation timeouts; records of delay and response measurements per operation.

4371 6.10.4 [ACC-BM-AP-004]

4372 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AP-004.

4373 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager limits retry attempts and resource consumption for signature
4374 verification and network operations.

4375 Assessment preparation:

4376  Test environment: the boot manager in states exercising signature verification and network operations.


4377  Required information: the specification of retry-attempt limits and resource-consumption bounds for each
4378 operation class.

4379  Required tools: attempt-stimulation tool (e.g. repeated invalid-signature submissions, repeated network
4380 attempts); resource-monitoring tool.

4381 Assessment activities:

4382  Where the boot manager performs neither verified boot nor network boot, record the requirement as not
4383 applicable and close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

4384  Repeatedly submit inputs to signature verification and network-operation paths beyond the documented retry
4385 limit; confirm the boot manager halts retries at the documented limit.

4386  Measure resource consumption during sustained retry stimulus; confirm it remains within the documented
4387 bounds.

4388  Confirm that exceeding the retry limit produces the documented terminal behaviour rather than unbounded
4389 retrying.

4390 Assessment verdict:

4391  Pass: the boot manager observes its documented retry limits and resource-consumption bounds under sustained
4392 stimulus, and exceeding a retry limit produces the documented terminal behaviour. For example, a boot
4393 manager that stops re-attempting signature verification after the documented number of failed attempts, holds
4394 memory and time within the documented bounds throughout, and then halts to a documented error state
4395 satisfies the requirement.

4396  Fail: the requirement is not met if retries continue beyond the documented limit; if resource consumption
4397 exceeds the documented bounds under sustained stimulus; or where exceeding the limit produces
4398 undocumented behaviour instead of the documented terminal state.

4399 Assessment evidence: specification of retry and resource policy; test records with measurements under sustained
4400 stimulus.

4401 6.10.5 [ACC-BM-AP-005]

4402 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AP-005.

4403 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager prevents unauthorised bypass of security verification steps during
4404 normal operation.

4405 Assessment preparation:

4406  Test environment: the boot manager in normal operational mode; documented debug or in-field modes
4407 disabled or appropriately gated.

4408  Required information: the enumeration of security verification steps; the documented authorisation mechanism
4409 for any permitted bypass (e.g. in-field debug mode).

4410  Required tools: tools to attempt bypass via input manipulation, state manipulation, or invocation of
4411 documented bypass paths without authorisation.

4412 Assessment activities:

4413  For each security verification step, attempt to bypass it through input manipulation and via any documented
4414 bypass path without providing the documented authorisation; confirm the step is executed and the bypass is
4415 rejected.

4416  Where a documented bypass path exists (e.g. in-field debug mode), attempt invocation without authentication
4417 and confirm rejection.

4418  Confirm that in normal operational mode no mechanism permits unauthorised bypass.


4419 Assessment verdict:

4420  Pass: every security verification step executes in normal operation; documented bypass paths require
4421 authentication; unauthorised bypass attempts are rejected.

4422  Fail: a security verification step can be bypassed without authentication, or normal operational mode permits
4423 unauthorised bypass.

4424 Assessment evidence: enumeration of verification steps; records of bypass attempts per step; test records of bypass-
4425 path authorisation.

4426 6.10.6 [ACC-BM-AP-006]

4427 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AP-006.

4428 Assessment objective: verify that, at MEDIUM or HIGH security profile, the boot manager detects and corrects errors
4429 in critical data using mechanisms supported by the underlying platform.

4430 Assessment preparation:

4431  Test environment: the boot manager at MEDIUM or HIGH security profile with access to error-inducing
4432 channels on the critical-data storage.

4433  Required information: enumeration of critical data items; the error-detection and correction mechanism used
4434 for each (e.g. ECC, FEC, cross-copy comparison); the platform features relied upon.

4435  Required tools: bit-flip injection tool or equivalent for the platform; correction-observation tool.

4436 Assessment activities:

4437  Where the boot manager is not at MEDIUM or HIGH security profile, record the requirement as not applicable
4438 and close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

4439  For each critical-data item, inject a documented-recoverable error into the stored value.

4440  Confirm the boot manager detects the error during its next access.

4441  Confirm the error is corrected and the data is readable at its expected value.

4442  Inject a documented non-recoverable error and confirm detection plus documented failure handling.

4443 Assessment verdict:

4444  Pass: recoverable errors in critical data are detected and corrected, and non-recoverable errors are detected and
4445 produce documented failure handling. For example, a boot manager that detects a single-bit error in a stored
4446 key, corrects it using the platform error-correction mechanism, and refuses to boot when presented with an
4447 uncorrectable error in that key satisfies the requirement.

4448  Fail: the requirement is not met if an injected recoverable error is not detected or not corrected; if a non-
4449 recoverable error is not detected; or where a detected non-recoverable error does not lead to the documented
4450 failure handling.

4451 Assessment evidence: enumeration of critical data; records of error injection and correction per item.

4452 6.10.7 [ACC-BM-AP-007]

4453 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AP-007.

4454 Assessment objective: verify that, at MEDIUM or HIGH security profile where the boot manager is not stored in
4455 immutable memory, essential boot code remains available in the presence of storage corruption or failure.


4456 Assessment preparation:

4457  Test environment: the boot manager at MEDIUM or HIGH security profile on a platform whose boot-code
4458 storage is mutable and accessible for corruption injection.

4459  Required information: identification of essential boot code; the availability mechanism (e.g. redundant storage,
4460 fallback partition); the corruption scenarios the mechanism is expected to withstand.

4461  Required tools: storage-corruption injection tool; boot-execution observation tool.

4462 Assessment activities:

4463  Where the boot manager is stored in immutable memory, record the requirement as not applicable and close
4464 this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

4465  Corrupt the primary copy of the essential boot code within the documented withstand-scenario; confirm the
4466 boot manager continues boot using the redundant copy or fallback partition.

4467  Corrupt at the boundary of the documented withstand-scenario (e.g. both copies) and confirm the boot
4468 manager produces the documented failure indication rather than silently continuing.

4469  Confirm the availability mechanism itself is protected from unauthorised corruption.

4470 Assessment verdict:

4471  Pass: essential boot code remains available under the documented withstand-scenarios, the boot manager
4472 produces documented failure handling beyond those scenarios, and the availability mechanism is itself
4473 protected from unauthorised corruption. For example, a boot manager that boots from a redundant copy when
4474 its primary essential-boot-code copy is corrupted, signals a documented failure when both copies are
4475 corrupted, and prevents unauthorised modification of the redundant copy satisfies the requirement.

4476  Fail: the requirement is not met if essential boot code becomes unavailable within a documented withstand-
4477 scenario; if corruption beyond that scenario does not produce the documented failure handling; or where the
4478 availability mechanism can itself be bypassed or corrupted by an unauthorised entity.

4479 Assessment evidence: identification of essential boot code; test records of corruption injection; record of inspection of
4480 the availability mechanism.

4481 6.10.8 [ACC-BM-AP-008]

4482 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AP-008.

4483 Assessment objective: verify that sensitive actions performed in recovery mode require authentication or physical
4484 presence.

4485 Assessment preparation:

4486  Test environment: the boot manager with recovery capability and recovery mode entry controllable.

4487  Required information: enumeration of recovery-mode actions classified as sensitive; the authentication or
4488 physical-presence requirement for each.

4489  Required tools: recovery-mode entry tool; authentication and physical-presence stimulation tools.

4490 Assessment activities:

4491  Where the boot manager has no recovery capability, record the requirement as not applicable and close this
4492 assessment per clause 5.1.3.

4493  Enter recovery mode by each documented trigger (including automatic triggers on boot failure).

4494  Attempt each sensitive action without authentication or physical presence; confirm rejection.

4495  Attempt each sensitive action with the documented authentication or physical-presence assertion; confirm
4496 acceptance.


4497 Assessment verdict:

4498  Pass: every recovery-mode action classified as sensitive requires the documented authentication or physical
4499 presence, and attempts to perform such an action without either are rejected. For example, a boot manager that
4500 enters recovery mode automatically after repeated boot failures but refuses to erase keys or change the trust
4501 anchor until an authenticated operator acts satisfies the requirement.

4502  Fail: the requirement is not met if a sensitive recovery-mode action can be performed without the documented
4503 authentication or physical presence; or where a documented recovery trigger reaches a sensitive action without
4504 enforcing the authorisation requirement.

4505 Assessment evidence: enumeration of sensitive actions; authorisation test records per action.

4506 6.10.9 [ACC-BM-AP-009]

4507 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AP-009.

4508 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager, where network boot is supported, handles network boot failures in
4509 a manner that maintains boot availability.

4510 Assessment preparation:

4511  Test environment: the boot manager configured for network boot in a controlled environment permitting
4512 network-level failure injection.

4513  Required information: enumeration of network-boot failure classes; the documented handling mechanism for
4514 each (e.g. timeout, fallback to local boot, backoff retries, alternative servers).

4515  Required tools: network failure-injection tool (server unavailable, partial response, malformed response); boot-
4516 outcome observation.

4517 Assessment activities:

4518  Where the boot manager has no network boot capability, record the requirement as not applicable and close
4519 this assessment per clause 5.1.3.
