4520  For each documented failure class, induce the failure and observe the boot manager's handling.

4521  Confirm the documented handling mechanism is applied (timeout fires, fallback is entered, backoff retries
4522 proceed, or alternative servers are attempted as documented).

4523  Confirm the boot manager reaches a documented terminal state (successful boot via alternative path,
4524 documented failure indication) rather than hanging indefinitely.

4525 Assessment verdict:

4526  Pass: each documented network-boot failure class invokes the documented handling mechanism and the boot
4527 manager reaches a documented terminal state rather than hanging. For example, a boot manager that, on an
4528 unreachable boot server, applies its documented timeout, performs backoff retries, then falls back to local boot
4529 satisfies the requirement.

4530  Fail: the requirement is not met if a documented failure class causes the boot manager to hang or behave in an
4531 undocumented way; if the documented handling mechanism is not invoked; or where no documented terminal
4532 state is reached.

4533 Assessment evidence: enumeration of failure classes; injection and outcome records per class.

4534 6.10.10 [ACC-BM-AP-010]

4535 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AP-010.

4536 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager generates logs for security-relevant failure conditions.


4537 Assessment preparation:

4538  Test environment: the boot manager with verified or measured boot and logging capability active.

4539  Required information: the manufacturer's enumeration of security-relevant failure conditions (e.g. verification
4540 failures, integrity violations, authentication failures, unexpected modification of boot components); the
4541 documented log-entry content for each.

4542  Required tools: fault-injection tool for each condition; log capture tool.

4543 Assessment activities:

4544  Where the boot manager has no logging capability, or performs neither verified nor measured boot, record the
4545 requirement as not applicable and close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

4546  Induce each enumerated security-relevant failure condition.

4547  Capture the log output and confirm that a log entry consistent with the documented content is generated for
4548 each.

4549  Confirm the entry identifies the condition type and the affected component or step.

4550 Assessment verdict:

4551  Pass: every enumerated security-relevant failure condition produces a log entry consistent with the
4552 documented content, identifying the condition type and the affected component or step. For example, a boot
4553 manager that records a distinct, parseable log entry naming the failed component each time signature
4554 verification fails satisfies the requirement.

4555  Fail: the requirement is not met if an enumerated condition produces no log entry; if an entry does not match
4556 the documented content; or where an entry fails to identify the condition type or the affected component.

4557 NOTE: Logging of security-relevant failure conditions is also addressed by REQ-BM-MON-003, assessed under
4558 clause 6.14. Where both requirements apply, one body of log evidence may serve both this assessment
4559 and the assessment of ACC-BM-MON-003.

4560 Assessment evidence: enumeration of failure conditions; records of injection and log capture per condition.

4561 6.10.11 [ACC-BM-AP-011]

4562 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AP-011.

4563 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager uses time representations valid beyond the year 2038 for all
4564 security-relevant uses of time.

4565 Assessment preparation:

4566  Test environment: the boot manager with the ability to set internal time or to process inputs containing time
4567 values beyond 2038-01-19 03:14:07 UTC.

4568  Required information: enumeration of security-relevant uses of time (certificate validity, internal system time
4569 for boot decisions, timestamps in logs); the representation used for each.

4570  Required tools: time-manipulation tool to set inputs beyond the 2038 boundary; inspection tool for each time
4571 representation.

4572 Assessment activities:

4573  For each enumerated use, inspect the representation width and confirm it accommodates values beyond the
4574 2038 boundary (e.g. 64-bit timestamp).

4575  Process inputs containing a time value beyond the 2038 boundary (e.g. a certificate with a post-2038 expiry)
4576 and confirm correct handling.


4577  Set the boot manager's internal time beyond the 2038 boundary where supported and confirm subsequent
4578 operations behave correctly.

4579 Assessment verdict:

4580  Pass: every enumerated security-relevant use of time uses a representation that accommodates values beyond
4581 the 2038 boundary, and the boot manager handles post-2038 inputs and internal time correctly. For example, a
4582 boot manager that holds certificate validity and log timestamps in a 64-bit representation and correctly accepts
4583 a certificate with a post-2038 expiry satisfies the requirement.

4584  Fail: the requirement is not met if an enumerated representation wraps or truncates at or after the 2038
4585 boundary; if a post-2038 input is processed incorrectly; or where internal time set beyond the boundary
4586 produces incorrect behaviour.

4587 Assessment evidence: enumeration of time uses with inspection of representation; records of input processing after
4588 2038.

4589 6.10.12 [ACC-BM-AP-012]

4590 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AP-012.

4591 Assessment objective: verify that recovery mechanisms are protected from unauthorised modification or disablement.

4592 Assessment preparation:

4593  Test environment: the boot manager with recovery capability and the recovery-mechanism storage and
4594 configuration accessible.

4595  Required information: specification of the recovery mechanism and the protection applied to its code, data,
4596 and enablement state.

4597  Required tools: modification and disablement attempt tools for each interface exposing the recovery
4598 mechanism.

4599 Assessment activities:

4600  Where the boot manager has no recovery capability, record the requirement as not applicable and close this
4601 assessment per clause 5.1.3.

4602  Attempt modification of the recovery mechanism's code and data through each documented interface without
4603 the authorised path; confirm rejection.

4604  Attempt disablement of the recovery mechanism through each interface without authorised path; confirm
4605 rejection.

4606  Attempt modification via undocumented or residual interfaces; confirm rejection.

4607 Assessment verdict:

4608  Pass: the recovery mechanism's code, data, and enablement state are protected from modification and
4609 disablement through every interface lacking the authorised path. For example, a boot manager that rejects
4610 attempts to overwrite its recovery partition or clear its recovery-enabled flag through any interface other than
4611 the authenticated update path satisfies the requirement.

4612  Fail: the requirement is not met if the recovery mechanism's code or data can be modified without the
4613 authorised path; if the mechanism can be disabled without the authorised path; or where an undocumented or
4614 residual interface permits either.

4615 Assessment evidence: specification of the recovery mechanism; records of modification and disablement attempts per
4616 interface.

4617 6.10.13 [ACC-BM-AP-013]

4618 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AP-013.


4619 Assessment objective: verify that partial execution of boot components is prevented when verification has not
4620 completed successfully.

4621 Assessment preparation:

4622  Test environment: the boot manager with verified boot and the ability to interrupt or fail verification mid-
4623 process.

4624  Required information: specification of the execution-gate mechanism between verification and execution.

4625  Required tools: verification-fault injection tool; execution observation tool.

4626 Assessment activities:

4627  Where the boot manager does not perform verified boot, record the requirement as not applicable and close
4628 this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

4629  Induce verification failure at various stages (before completion, at a boundary, immediately prior to execution)
4630 and confirm no portion of the component is executed.

4631  Induce a verification process that does not complete (e.g. crashed verifier) and confirm the boot manager does
4632 not proceed to execution.

4633  Inspect the transition between verification and execution for any race or shortcut path.

4634 Assessment verdict:

4635  Pass: no portion of a boot component is executed when its verification fails or has not completed, and no race
4636 or shortcut path bypasses the gate between verification and execution. For example, a boot manager that holds
4637 a component inert until its signature check completes successfully, and that halts rather than executing when
4638 the verifier crashes mid-check, satisfies the requirement.

4639  Fail: the requirement is not met if any portion of a component executes while its verification is incomplete or
4640 has failed; or where a race condition or shortcut path allows execution to begin before the verification gate
4641 completes.

4642 NOTE: Continuation of boot with components that fail verification is addressed by REQ-BM-INT-003, assessed
4643 under clause 6.8; the present requirement addresses partial execution of a component while verification is
4644 incomplete.

4645 Assessment evidence: records of verification-failure injection; records of execution observation; record of inspection of
4646 the transition path.

4647 6.10.14 [ACC-BM-AP-014]

4648 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AP-014.

4649 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager does not perform security-sensitive operations when required
4650 cryptographic components or services are unavailable.

4651 Assessment preparation:

4652  Test environment: the boot manager with the ability to induce unavailability of required cryptographic
4653 components or services (e.g. TPM unavailable, cryptographic provider faulted).

4654  Required information: numeration of security-sensitive operations and the cryptographic components or
4655 services each depends upon.

4656  Required tools: cryptographic-component unavailability injection tool.

4657 Assessment activities:

4658  For each security-sensitive operation, make the required cryptographic component or service unavailable and
4659 attempt the operation.


4660  Confirm the operation is not performed under the unavailability condition and the boot manager produces
4661 documented handling.

4662  Confirm that no fallback uses a weaker substitute that would circumvent the security intent.

4663 Assessment verdict:

4664  Pass: no security-sensitive operation is performed while a cryptographic component or service it requires is
4665 unavailable, and no weaker substitute is used in place of the required one. For example, a boot manager that
4666 declines to verify a signature and halts to a documented error state when the TPM it relies on is unavailable,
4667 rather than skipping verification or using an unapproved fallback, satisfies the requirement.

4668  Fail: the requirement is not met if a security-sensitive operation is performed while its required cryptographic
4669 component or service is unavailable; or where a weaker substitute is used that circumvents the security intent.

4670 Assessment evidence: mapping of operations to components; unavailability test records per operation; record of
4671 fallback inspection.

4672 6.10.15 [ACC-BM-AP-015]

4673 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AP-015.

4674 Assessment objective: verify that, where recovery capability exists, the boot manager does not bypass security controls
4675 when handling security violations or verification failures.

4676 Assessment preparation:

4677  Test environment: the boot manager with recovery capability and the ability to induce security violations and
4678 verification failures.

4679  Required information: the manufacturer's enumeration of violation and failure classes; the handling path for
4680 each, including the security controls retained.

4681  Required tools: violation and failure injection tools; inspection tool for the security-control state during and
4682 after handling.

4683 Assessment activities:

4684  Where the boot manager has no recovery capability, record the requirement as not applicable and close this
4685 assessment per clause 5.1.3.

4686  Induce each enumerated violation or failure class and observe the handling path.

4687  Confirm that the security controls documented as retained are active during and after handling (e.g.
4688 verification is still required before execution; authentication is still required for sensitive actions).

4689  Confirm that the handling path does not reach a state where security controls are weakened or bypassed.

4690 Assessment verdict:

4691  Pass: every documented handling path for a security violation or verification failure retains the security
4692 controls documented as retained, and no path weakens or bypasses them. For example, a boot manager that, on
4693 detecting an integrity violation, enters its handling path while still requiring signature verification before any
4694 subsequent execution and authentication before any sensitive action satisfies the requirement.

4695  Fail: the requirement is not met if a handling path weakens or bypasses a security control documented as
4696 retained; or where handling a violation or failure reaches a state in which verification or authentication is no
4697 longer enforced.

4698 Assessment evidence: enumeration of violation classes with mapping of retained control; injection records per class
4699 with records of control state.


4700 6.10.16 [ACC-BM-AP-016]

4701 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AP-016.

4702 Assessment objective: verify that recovery capability is preserved across firmware and configuration updates.

4703 Assessment preparation:

4704  Test environment: the boot manager with recovery and update capabilities in an environment supporting
4705 applying representative updates.

4706  Required information: the manufacturer's specification of the recovery-preservation mechanism across
4707 updates; the update scenarios required to preserve recovery capability.

4708  Required tools: update-application tool; recovery-mechanism exercise tool.

4709 Assessment activities:

4710  Where the boot manager has no update capability or no recovery capability, record the requirement as not
4711 applicable and close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

4712  Apply firmware and configuration updates through the documented update paths.

4713  After each update, exercise the recovery mechanism and confirm it is functional.

4714  Include in the test sample a firmware update that alters boot-manager components and a configuration update
4715 that alters recovery-related configuration.

4716 Assessment verdict:

4717  Pass: recovery capability remains functional after every documented class of firmware and configuration
4718 update. For example, a boot manager whose recovery mechanism still operates after a firmware update that
4719 replaces boot-manager components and after a configuration update that alters recovery-related settings
4720 satisfies the requirement.

4721  Fail: the requirement is not met if recovery capability is broken, disabled, or degraded by any documented
4722 update class; or where a documented update scenario leaves the recovery mechanism non-functional.

4723 Assessment evidence: enumeration of update classes; records of recovery exercises per update.

4724 6.11 Non-interference

4725 6.11.0 Overview of requirements addressed in clause 6.11

4726 The present clause specifies assessment criteria for the requirements in clause 5.11.

4727 Table 6.11.0-1: Requirements addressed in clause 6.11

Requirement Profile applicability
REQ-BM-IM- 001 MEDIUM, HIGH (if network boot)
4728

4729 6.11.1 [ACC-BM-IM-001]

4730 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-IM-001.

4731 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager does not generate harmful or disruptive network behaviour.

4732 Assessment preparation:

4733  Test environment: the boot manager configured for network boot in a controlled network environment with
4734 other hosts and network segments present, permitting passive observation of all traffic originating from the
4735 boot manager.


4736  Required information: the manufacturer's enumeration of network behaviours produced by the boot manager
4737 (broadcast scope, multicast participation, repeated retries, peer-discovery patterns) and the documented bounds
4738 on each.

4739  Required tools: network traffic analyser capable of identifying broadcast storms, loop formation, and abnormal
4740 traffic rates; topology probe able to detect loop conditions.

4741 Assessment activities:

4742  Capture the complete network traffic generated by the boot manager across a successful network boot and
4743 across each documented failure-mode scenario.

4744  Analyse the captured traffic for behaviour patterns that would be harmful or disruptive to other hosts or
4745 network segments, at minimum: broadcast rate relative to documented bounds; presence of loop-inducing
4746 frame forwarding; sustained retry patterns beyond documented bounds; traffic targeted at unintended
4747 destinations.

4748  Exercise the boot manager in a network topology where loops could form if frame-forwarding behaviour were
4749 incorrect; confirm no loop is induced.

4750 Assessment verdict:

4751  Pass: observed network behaviour stays within the documented bounds; no broadcast storm, loop, or sustained
4752 disruptive pattern is produced under nominal or failure-mode operation.

4753  Fail: the boot manager produces a broadcast storm, induces a network loop, or generates sustained traffic
4754 beyond documented bounds.

4755 Assessment evidence: documented bounds on network behaviour; traffic captures under nominal conditions and under
4756 failure modes; record of loop-topology exercises.

4757 6.12 Attack surface minimisation

4758 6.12.0 Overview of requirements addressed in clause 6.12

4759 The present clause specifies assessment criteria for the requirements in clause 5.12.

4760 Table 6.12.0-1: Requirements addressed in clause 6.12

Requirement Profile applicability
REQ-BM-AMS- 001 All
REQ-BM-AMS- 002 All
REQ-BM-AMS-003 All
REQ-BM-AMS- 004 All
REQ-BM-AMS-005 All
REQ-BM-AMS- 006 All
REQ-BM-AMS-007 All (if configuration capability)
4761

4762 6.12.1 [ACC-BM-AMS-001]

4763 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AMS-001.

4764 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager, before handing off control to the boot target, ensures that only the
4765 resources necessary for the boot target remain enabled.

4766 Assessment preparation:

4767  Test environment: the boot manager executed to the handoff point with inspection capability over the platform
4768 resource state at that point (peripherals, memory regions, DMA controllers, interrupt sources, CPU modes).


4769  Required information: the enumeration of resources enabled during boot; for each, whether it is required by
4770 the boot target at handoff and the rationale.

4771  Required tools: platform-state inspection tool capable of enumerating enabled resources at the handoff
4772 moment.

4773 Assessment activities:

4774  Capture the resource state at the handoff point (e.g. by halting immediately prior to handoff, or by
4775 instrumenting the handoff transition).

4776  For each resource enumerated as enabled, confirm it is documented as required by the boot target; investigate
4777 any undocumented enabled resource.

4778  For each resource documented as not required at handoff but enabled during earlier boot stages, confirm it has
4779 been disabled, quiesced, or revoked before handoff.

4780 Assessment verdict:

4781  Pass: only the resources necessary for the boot target remain enabled at the handoff point, and every resource
4782 used during earlier boot stages but not required at handoff has been disabled, quiesced, or released. For
4783 example, a boot manager that disables its DMA-capable diagnostic interface and releases its network and
4784 communication buffers before transferring control, leaving enabled only the memory regions and devices the
4785 boot target requires, satisfies the requirement.

4786  Fail: the requirement is not met if a resource not required by the boot target remains enabled at handoff; if a
4787 resource enabled during an earlier boot stage is not disabled, quiesced, or released before handoff; or where an
4788 enabled resource at the handoff point has no documented justification.

4789 Assessment evidence: record of resource enumeration with required/not-required classification; record of state capture
4790 at handoff.

4791 6.12.2 [ACC-BM-AMS-002]

4792 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AMS-002.

4793 Assessment objective: verify that non-essential code is excluded from production builds of the boot manager.

4794 Assessment preparation:

4795  Test environment: the production build of the boot manager as placed on the market.

4796  Required information: build configuration and documented differences between development, test, and
4797 production builds; the list of code paths, modules, or features categorised as non-essential for production (e.g.
4798 debug output, test harnesses, development shortcuts, example configurations).

4799  Required tools: binary analysis tools capable of identifying string constants, code paths, and linked modules;
4800 where source access is available, build-manifest inspection.

4801 Assessment activities:

4802  Inspect the build configuration and confirm that non-essential modules and flags are not enabled for the
4803 production build.

4804  Inspect the binary for indicators of non-essential code (e.g. debug strings, test symbols, unreached branches
4805 linked only by non-production flags) and investigate any finding.

4806  Where source access is available, confirm that guards around non-essential code exclude it under the
4807 production build configuration.


4808 Assessment verdict:

4809  Pass: the production build excludes code documented as non-essential, and no indicator of non-essential code
4810 is found in the production binary beyond those documented. For example, a production build whose debug-
4811 output module and test harness are excluded by the production build flags, and whose binary shows no debug
4812 strings or test symbols beyond the documented set, satisfies the requirement.

4813  Fail: the requirement is not met if the production build contains modules or code paths documented as non-
4814 essential; or where binary analysis surfaces non-essential code not present in the documentation.

4815 Assessment evidence: record of build configuration; findings of binary analysis; review of source guards where
4816 applicable.

4817 6.12.3 [ACC-BM-AMS-003]

4818 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AMS-003.

4819 Assessment objective: verify that interfaces and functions not intended for operational use are disabled or protected.

4820 Assessment preparation:

4821  Test environment: the boot manager in its operational configuration on a representative platform.

4822  Required information: enumeration of interfaces and functions exposed by the boot manager, each classified as
4823 operational or non-operational; for non-operational items, the applied mechanism (disabled, physically
4824 protected, authentication-gated, fuse-locked).

4825  Required tools: interface enumeration tools for the platform; interaction tools for each interface category (e.g.
4826 serial debug, JTAG, USB debug, memory-mapped registers).

4827 Assessment activities:

4828  Enumerate the interfaces accessible on the operational product and compare against the documented list.

4829  For each interface classified as non-operational, confirm the documented protection is in effect; test the
4830 protection by attempting to exercise the interface without the documented unlock path.

4831  For each interface classified as operational, confirm it matches the manufacturer's intended purpose and
4832 exposes only documented functions.

4833 Assessment verdict:

4834  Pass: every non-operational interface or function is protected by its documented mechanism and cannot be
4835 exercised without the documented unlock path, and operational interfaces expose only documented functions.
4836 For example, a boot manager whose serial debug console is fuse-locked in production and unreachable without
4837 the documented unlock path, and whose operational update interface exposes no functions beyond those
4838 documented, satisfies the requirement.

4839  Fail: the requirement is not met if a non-operational interface is reachable without its documented protection;
4840 or where an operational interface exposes undocumented functions.

4841 Assessment evidence: enumeration of interfaces with record of operational classification; record of protection tests per
4842 interface.

4843 6.12.4 [ACC-BM-AMS-004]

4844 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AMS-004.

4845 Assessment objective: verify that unused or non-essential interfaces and protocols have been removed from the boot
4846 manager.


4847 Assessment preparation:

4848  Test environment: the production build of the boot manager.

4849  Required information: enumeration of interfaces and protocols supported by the boot manager; for each, the
4850 operational purpose that justifies its inclusion.

4851  Required tools: interface and protocol enumeration tools; binary analysis tools capable of identifying linked
4852 protocol stacks or interface handlers.

4853 Assessment activities:

4854  Enumerate the interfaces and protocols exposed at runtime and, via binary analysis, those compiled into the
4855 boot manager.

4856  For each interface or protocol, confirm an operational-purpose justification exists and the protocol is actively
4857 used in documented boot scenarios.

4858  Identify any interface or protocol present in the binary or at runtime without a documented operational purpose
4859 and record it as an unused or non-essential item not removed.

4860 Assessment verdict:

4861  Pass: every interface and protocol present at runtime or in the binary maps to a documented operational
4862 purpose. For example, a boot manager that links only the network protocol stack required for its documented
4863 network-boot scenario, with no unused discovery service compiled in, satisfies the requirement.

4864  Fail: the requirement is not met if an interface or protocol is present at runtime or in the binary without a
4865 documented operational purpose.

4866 Assessment evidence: runtime and binary interface/protocol enumeration; justification mapping record.

4867 6.12.5 [ACC-BM-AMS-005]

4868 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AMS-005.

4869 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager validates all inputs for conformance with expected formats.

4870 Assessment preparation:

4871  Test environment: the boot manager accessible through each documented input channel (e.g. configuration
4872 files, signed artefacts, network inputs, user interfaces, inter-component messages).

4873  Required information: the manufacturer's enumeration of input channels; for each, the expected input format
4874 and the validation mechanism applied.

4875  Required tools: input fuzzing tools appropriate to each channel; controlled-input generation tools.

4876 Assessment activities:

4877  For each input channel, submit well-formed inputs and confirm acceptance.

4878  Submit inputs violating the expected format in documented ways (e.g. truncated, oversized, malformed
4879 encoding, out-of-range values); confirm rejection before any security-relevant processing.

4880  Submit a sample of non-targeted fuzz inputs on each channel and confirm that the boot manager handles them
4881 without entering an undefined state.

4882 Assessment verdict:

4883  Pass: well-formed inputs are accepted, documented malformed inputs are rejected before any security-relevant
4884 processing, and fuzz inputs do not drive the boot manager into an undefined state. For example, a boot
4885 manager that accepts a well-formed configuration file, rejects a truncated or oversized one before parsing
4886 security-relevant fields, and remains in a defined state under fuzzed input on every documented channel
4887 satisfies the requirement.


4888  Fail: the requirement is not met if a documented malformed input is processed without rejection; or where a
4889 fuzz input drives the boot manager into an undefined state.

4890 Assessment evidence: enumeration of input channels; well-formed and malformed test records per channel; fuzz test
4891 summary.

4892 6.12.6 [ACC-BM-AMS-006]

4893 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AMS-006.

4894 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager detects errors in critical operations, rejects non-compliant inputs,
4895 and transitions to error handling on fault.

4896 Assessment preparation:

4897  Test environment: the boot manager configured for network boot in a controlled environment where inputs can
4898 be manipulated and faults can be induced.

4899  Required information: enumeration of critical operations; for each, the error conditions, the compliance criteria
4900 for inputs, and the documented error-handling transition.

4901  Required tools: controllable input source; fault-injection tools; state inspection tool for the boot manager's
4902 error-handling path.

4903 Assessment activities:

4904  For each enumerated critical operation, induce the documented error condition (e.g. truncated response, invalid
4905 signature in a signed resource, protocol-level fault); confirm detection.

4906  Submit non-compliant inputs (e.g. violating protocol structure, outside value ranges); confirm rejection before
4907 the operation completes.

4908  Confirm that on detection or rejection the boot manager transitions to the documented error-handling state
4909 rather than continuing into a potentially compromised path.

4910 Assessment verdict:

4911  Pass: each enumerated error condition is detected, non-compliant inputs are rejected, and the documented
4912 error-handling transition is taken on every fault. For example, a boot manager that detects an invalid signature
4913 on a fetched resource, rejects a structurally non-compliant input before the operation completes, and transitions
4914 to its documented error-handling state rather than continuing satisfies the requirement.

4915  Fail: the requirement is not met if an enumerated error condition is not detected; if a non-compliant input is
4916 processed; or where the boot manager continues past a detected fault without taking the documented error-
4917 handling transition.

4918 Assessment evidence: enumeration of critical operations; fault-injection and non-compliant input test records, per
4919 operation; records of error-handling transitions.

4920 6.12.7 [ACC-BM-AMS-007]

4921 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-AMS-007.

4922 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager provides a mechanism to disable configuration options that are not
4923 required by the deployment integrator.

4924 Assessment preparation:

4925  Test environment: the boot manager accessible through its configuration interface.

4926  Required information: enumeration of configuration options; for each, the mechanism provided for the
4927 deployment integrator to disable or suppress the option; the documentation directed at deployment integrators
4928 explaining the disable mechanism.


4929  Required tools: configuration tool; inspection tool for the boot manager's effective configuration state.

4930 Assessment activities:

4931  Where the boot manager has no configuration capability, record the requirement as not applicable and close
4932 this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

4933  For each configuration option that may be disabled per manufacturer documentation, invoke the disable
4934 mechanism and confirm that the option is no longer exposed or active in the boot manager's effective state.

4935  Confirm that the disable mechanism is documented for the deployment integrator and does not require
4936 manufacturer-restricted access.

4937  Confirm that re-enabling a previously disabled option, where documented, requires the same mechanism
4938 accessible to the deployment integrator.

4939 Assessment verdict:

4940  Pass: each documented configuration option can be disabled through the deployment-integrator-accessible
4941 mechanism, disablement takes effect in the boot manager's effective state, and re-enablement where
4942 documented uses the same mechanism. For example, a boot manager that lets the deployment integrator
4943 disable an optional network-boot path through documented configuration, with the option absent from the
4944 effective state afterwards and re-enabled only through the same integrator-accessible mechanism, satisfies the
4945 requirement.

4946  Fail: the requirement is not met if a documented configuration option cannot be disabled by the deployment
4947 integrator; if disablement does not take effect; or where re-enablement requires manufacturer-restricted or
4948 otherwise undocumented access.

4949 Assessment evidence: enumeration of configuration options with mapping of disable mechanisms; test records of
4950 disable and re-enable per option.

4951 6.13 Exploit mitigation

4952 6.13.0 Overview of requirements addressed in clause 6.13

4953 The present clause specifies assessment criteria for the requirement in clause 5.13.

4954 Requirements relevant to exploitation mitigation are also specified in other clauses of the present document and are
4955 assessed under the corresponding clauses of clause 6:

4956  Privilege separation and trust-boundary enforcement: REQ-BM-INT-001, assessed under clause 6.8.

4957  Resource minimisation and DMA restriction at handoff: REQ-BM-AMS-001, assessed under clause 6.12.

4958  Access control on cryptographic key material: REQ-BM-CP-001, assessed under clause 6.7.

4959  Attack-surface reduction: REQ-BM-AMS-002, REQ-BM-AMS-003, REQ-BM-AMS-004,
4960 REQ-BM-AMS-007, assessed under clause 6.12.

4961  Input validation and error handling: REQ-BM-AMS-005, REQ-BM-AMS-006, assessed under clause 6.12.

4962  Prevention of partial execution on verification failure and of boot continuation with failed components:
4963 REQ-BM-AP-013, assessed under 6.10, and REQ-BM-INT-003, assessed under clause 6.8.

4964 Table 6.13.0-1: Requirements addressed in clause 6.13

Requirement Profile applicability
REQ-BM-EM-001 MEDIUM, HIGH (runtime code-execution or privilege-escalation threats)
4965


4966 6.13.1 [ACC-BM-EM-001]

4967 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-EM-001.

4968 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager implements exploitation mitigation mechanisms aligned with the
4969 documented threat model, addressing unauthorised code execution, privilege escalation between boot stages, and
4970 uncontrolled propagation of compromise in the pre-OS execution environment.

4971 Assessment preparation:

4972  Test environment: the boot manager with exploitation mitigation mechanisms enabled in the documented
4973 default configuration, executable in a controlled environment in which targeted exploitation attempts can be
4974 applied.

4975  Required information: documentation of:

4976 a) the threat model including the threat categories the exploitation mitigation mechanisms are intended to
4977 address;

4978 b) the exploitation mitigation mechanisms implemented in the boot manager (for example compiler-level
4979 protections such as stack protection, ASLR, control-flow integrity, position-independent code; runtime
4980 integrity protections; isolation between boot stages; memory protection at handoff);

4981 c) the toolchain and platform features on which those mechanisms depend;

4982 d) the boot-manager components covered by each mechanism; and

4983 e) the documented limitations of each mechanism in the pre-OS context.

4984  Required tools: binary inspection tool appropriate to the boot manager binary format to confirm presence of
4985 compiler-level and platform-level mitigations; targeted exploitation framework appropriate to the
4986 boot-manager execution environment for attempted bypass; isolation-violation probes for the trust-boundary
4987 enforcement covered by REQ-BM-INT-001 and the resource and DMA restrictions covered by
4988 REQ-BM-AMS-001.

4989 Assessment activities:

4990  Where the documented threat model does not include runtime code-execution attacks or stage-to-stage
4991 privilege escalation, record the requirement as not applicable and close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

4992  Threat-model alignment: confirm that the documented set of exploitation mitigation mechanisms addresses the
4993 threat categories identified in the threat model and at minimum covers unauthorised code execution, privilege
4994 escalation between boot stages, and uncontrolled propagation of compromise where these are within the scope
4995 of the threat model.

4996  Functional verification: by binary inspection or equivalent technique appropriate to the platform, confirm
4997 presence of each documented compiler-level or platform-level mitigation in the boot-manager binary as
4998 shipped in the default configuration. Where a mitigation depends on a toolchain or platform feature, confirm
4999 the feature is enabled.

5000  Targeted exploitation attempts: for each documented mitigation, apply at least one targeted exploitation
5001 attempt designed to be blocked by that mitigation; confirm the attempt is rejected, contained, or detected.
5002 Attempts include, where applicable: code-injection attempts against writable-and-executable regions; control-
5003 flow hijack attempts against indirect calls; privilege-escalation attempts crossing documented trust boundaries
5004 between boot stages; propagation attempts from a deliberately-faulted boot-manager component to subsequent
5005 boot stages.

5006  Limitation acknowledgement: confirm that documented limitations of each mitigation in the pre-OS context
5007 (for example mitigations not available because the underlying hardware does not provide them) are recorded in
5008 the product documentation.


5009 Assessment verdict:

5010  Pass: the documented mitigations address the threat categories in the threat model that fall within the scope of
5011 the requirement; each documented mitigation is present in the boot-manager binary and toolchain
5012 configuration; targeted exploitation attempts within the scope of those mitigations are rejected, contained, or
5013 detected; and the documented limitations are recorded. For example, a binary built with stack protection,
5014 control-flow integrity, and position-independent code shows those features present on inspection, a code-
5015 injection attempt against a writable region and a control-flow hijack against an indirect call are both blocked,
5016 and the hardware features each mitigation depends on are confirmed enabled.

5017  Fail: the requirement is not met if the documented mitigations leave a threat category within the scope of the
5018 requirement unaddressed; if a documented mitigation is absent from the boot-manager binary or toolchain
5019 configuration; if a targeted exploitation attempt within the scope of a documented mitigation succeeds; or
5020 where a documented limitation is not recorded.

5021 Assessment evidence: The documented threat model relevant to exploitation mitigation; description of documented
5022 mitigations; record of binary / toolchain inspection per mitigation; record of targeted exploitation attempts and
5023 outcomes; record of documented limitations.

5024 NOTE 1: The mechanisms available to boot managers for exploitation mitigation are constrained by the pre-OS
5025 execution environment. Where hardware-side controls would mitigate physical-attack threats (T-PHYS-5,
5026 T-PHYS-6, T-PHYS-9, T-PHYS-11), those are addressed under Annex D and are not within the scope of
5027 this assessment.

5028 NOTE 2: Informative guidance on exploitation mitigation techniques is provided in Annex D. The techniques listed
5029 there are non-exhaustive; the assessment focuses on the mitigations documented by the manufacturer
5030 rather than on a fixed checklist of techniques.

5031 6.14 Monitoring

5032 6.14.0 Overview of requirements addressed in clause 6.14

5033 The present clause specifies assessment criteria for the requirements in clause 5.14.

5034 Table 6.14.0-1: Requirements addressed in clause 6.14

Requirement Profile applicability
REQ-BM-MON-001 MEDIUM, HIGH (if measured boot and logging implemented)
REQ-BM-MON- 002 MEDIUM, HIGH (if measured boot and logging implemented)
REQ-BM-MON-003 MEDIUM, HIGH (if logging implemented)
REQ-BM-MON- 004 All
REQ-BM-MON-005 MEDIUM, HIGH (if logging and authority transfer implemented)
5035

5036 6.14.1 [ACC-BM-MON-001]

5037 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-MON-001.

5038 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager records measurements of boot components and security-critical
5039 configuration in a tamper-evident way before handoff.

5040 Assessment preparation:

5041  Test environment: the boot manager executed to completion with access to the retention mechanism used for
5042 measurements (e.g. platform configuration registers, tamper-proof storage).

5043  Required information: the manufacturer's documentation of the measurement retention mechanism, the set of
5044 components and configuration items measured, and the tamper-evidence properties claimed for the
5045 mechanism.

5046  Required tools: inspection tool for the retention mechanism appropriate to the platform (e.g. TPM command
5047 interface for PCR read, secure-storage inspection utility).


5048 Assessment activities:

5049  Where the boot manager does not implement measured boot with logging capability, record the requirement as
5050 not applicable and close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

5051  Execute a complete boot and, immediately before handoff, read the retention mechanism to obtain the
5052 measurement set actually recorded.

5053  Compare the recorded measurements against the documented set of components and configuration items;
5054 confirm the set is complete.

5055  Verify the tamper-evidence property of the retention mechanism by attempting to alter a recorded
5056 measurement via documented and undocumented interfaces; confirm that alteration is either prevented or
5057 produces a detectable indication.

5058  Where retention is volatile (e.g. PCR), confirm that retention across the boot manager's execution to handoff is
5059 sufficient for the assessment objective.

5060 Assessment verdict:

5061  Pass: measurements of all documented components and security-critical configuration items are recorded
5062 before handoff, and the retention mechanism is tamper-evident both by inspection and under attempted
5063 alteration. For example, a complete boot populates a platform configuration register with the documented
5064 measurement set before control is handed off, and an attempt to overwrite a recorded measurement through
5065 documented and undocumented interfaces is either prevented or leaves a detectable indication.

5066  Fail: the requirement is not met if a documented measurement is missing or incomplete; if measurements are
5067 recorded only after handoff; or where the retention mechanism permits a recorded measurement to be altered
5068 without detection.

5069 Assessment evidence: record of retention mechanism inspection; record of measurement-set completeness; record of
5070 tamper-alteration tests.

5071 6.14.2 [ACC-BM-MON-002]

5072 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-MON-002.

5073 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager provides measurement records in a format that supports remote
5074 attestation and includes mechanisms to ensure freshness against replay.

5075 Assessment preparation:

5076  Test environment: the boot manager configured to emit measurement records to an external attestation verifier.

5077  Required information: the specification of the measurement record format, the supported freshness mechanism
5078 (e.g. nonces, monotonic counters, timestamps, challenge-response), and the attestation protocol or format the
5079 records conform to.

5080  Required tools: attestation verifier or parser capable of consuming the specified record format; tool for
5081 generating attestation challenges where the freshness mechanism is challenge-based.

5082 Assessment activities:

5083  Where the boot manager does not implement measured boot with logging capability, record the requirement as
5084 not applicable and close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

5085  Capture a measurement record produced by the boot manager and parse it using an attestation verifier
5086 implementing the specified format.

5087  Confirm that the parsed record contains at least the fields required for remote attestation: component
5088 identifiers, measurement digests, and the freshness element.

5089  Issue a challenge (or consume a nonce) as supported by the freshness mechanism; verify that the boot
5090 manager's response binds to the challenge or nonce.


5091  Replay a previously valid measurement record to the verifier and confirm that the replay is detected by the
5092 freshness mechanism.

5093 Assessment verdict:

5094  Pass: the measurement records parse against the specified attestation format and contain the fields required for
5095 remote attestation, and the freshness mechanism binds each record to a fresh element and rejects replayed
5096 records. For example, an attestation verifier parses a captured record, finds the component identifiers,
5097 measurement digests, and a nonce bound to the verifier's challenge, and rejects a previously valid record
5098 replayed against the same challenge.

5099  Fail: the requirement is not met if a measurement record fails to parse against the specified format; if a field
5100 required for remote attestation is missing; if the freshness mechanism is absent; or where a replayed record is
5101 not detected.

5102 Assessment evidence: sample of parsed measurement records; record of challenge-response exchange; record of replay
5103 rejection.

5104 6.14.3 [ACC-BM-MON-003]

5105 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-MON-003.

5106 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager produces log indications for security-relevant failures and state
5107 changes.

5108 Assessment preparation:

5109  Test environment: the boot manager executed under conditions that can be induced to produce each class of
5110 security-relevant event.

5111  Required information: the enumeration of security-relevant failures and state changes recorded by the boot
5112 manager (at minimum: verification failures, authentication failures, security policy violations, recovery mode
5113 activation, execution of unsigned code), the log output mechanism, and the log record format.

5114  Required tools: fault-injection or stimulation tools for each event class (e.g. corrupted boot image for
5115 verification failure, invalid credentials for authentication failure); log capture tool appropriate to the log output
5116 mechanism.

5117 Assessment activities:

5118  Where the boot manager does not implement logging capability, record the requirement as not applicable and
5119 close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

5120  For each enumerated event class, induce the event (e.g. present a boot image with an invalid signature to
5121 trigger a verification failure) and capture the boot manager's log output.

5122  Confirm that an identifiable log entry is produced for each induced event, that the entry identifies the event
5123 class, and that the entry is consistent with the documented log record format.

5124  Confirm that log entries are produced at the time the event occurs and are not suppressed under ongoing failure
5125 conditions.

5126 Assessment verdict:

5127  Pass: each enumerated class of security-relevant failure or state change produces an identifiable log entry that
5128 names the event class and matches the documented record format, at the time the event occurs. For example,
5129 presenting a boot image with an invalid signature produces a verification-failure entry distinguishable from an
5130 authentication-failure entry, each in the documented format, and the entries are not suppressed when failures
5131 continue.

5132  Fail: the requirement is not met if an enumerated event class produces no log entry; if the entry cannot be
5133 distinguished by event class; if it is inconsistent with the documented format; or where entries are suppressed
5134 under ongoing failure conditions.


5135 NOTE: Logging of security-relevant failure conditions is also required by REQ-BM-AP-010 (assessed under
5136 clause 6.10). Where both apply, the log capture performed here also serves that assessment and need not
5137 be repeated.

5138 Assessment evidence: enumeration of event classes; records of fault-injection tests; captured log entries for each
5139 induced event.

5140 6.14.4 [ACC-BM-MON-004]

5141 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-MON-004.

5142 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager provides version information accessible to the operating system,
5143 management systems, or authorised entity.

5144 Assessment preparation:

5145  Test environment: the boot manager executed to completion with the interfaces accessible to operating system,
5146 management system or authorised entity consumers.

5147  Required information: the documentation of the version information exposed (content and format), the access
5148 mechanism (e.g. ACPI table, UEFI variable, runtime service, platform-specific register), and the identity of the
5149 consumer role accessing the information.

5150  Required tools: consumer-role tool for the access mechanism (e.g. operating-system utility reading the
5151 exposed structure).

5152 Assessment activities:

5153  Query the boot manager's version information through each documented access mechanism.

5154  Confirm that the returned information contains the documented version fields (e.g. boot manager version,
5155 build identifier, relevant component versions).

5156  Confirm that the access is available to the documented consumers (operating system, management system,
5157 authorised entity) and that no authorisation step beyond those documented is required.

5158 Assessment verdict:

5159  Pass: the version information is accessible through each documented access mechanism, to each documented
5160 consumer role, and contains the documented version fields, with no authorisation step beyond those
5161 documented. For example, an operating-system utility reads the exposed structure and obtains the boot
5162 manager version and build identifier without any undocumented authorisation, and a management system
5163 reaches the same information through its documented interface.

5164  Fail: the requirement is not met if a documented access mechanism fails to return the version information; if
5165 the returned information is missing a documented field; or where access requires an authorisation step beyond
5166 those documented.

5167 Assessment evidence: sample query and response through each documented access mechanism; record of field
5168 completeness.

5169 6.14.5 [ACC-BM-MON-005]

5170 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-MON-005.

5171 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager records each authority transfer as a security-relevant event in the
5172 security log, with the prescribed event fields.

5173 Assessment preparation:

5174  Test environment: the boot manager with logging capability active and at least one authority transfer
5175 mechanism exposed.


5176  Required information: the manufacturer's enumeration of authority transfer mechanisms supported by the boot
5177 manager (e.g. trust anchor enrolment, ownership transfer, policy update), the log record format, the log output
5178 mechanism, and the field-by-field specification of the authority transfer event (mechanism invoked, initiating
5179 entity, approving entity, components affected).

5180  Required tools: invocation tool for each authority transfer mechanism; log capture tool appropriate to the log
5181 output mechanism; record-format parser.

5182 Assessment activities:

5183  Where the boot manager does not implement logging capability or provides no authority transfer mechanism,
5184 record the requirement as not applicable and close this assessment per clause 5.1.3

5185  For each documented authority transfer mechanism, invoke a transfer under documented conditions; capture
5186 the boot manager's log output.

5187  Confirm that the log captures an authority transfer event corresponding to each invocation, identifiable by
5188 event class.

5189  Parse the captured event against the documented format; confirm presence of each prescribed field
5190 (mechanism invoked, initiating entity, approving entity, components affected) and that the recorded values
5191 match the invocation.

5192  Invoke a transfer that fails authorisation; confirm that the failure is also recorded with the prescribed fields,
5193 identifying the attempted-but-rejected nature of the event.

5194 Assessment verdict:

5195  Pass: every documented authority transfer mechanism produces a security-relevant log event recording the
5196 mechanism invoked, the initiating entity, the approving entity, and the components affected, with values
5197 consistent with the invocation, and a transfer that fails authorisation is recorded with the same fields. For
5198 example, invoking trust-anchor enrolment produces a log event naming the enrolment mechanism, the entity
5199 that initiated it, the entity that approved it, and the affected trust store, and an enrolment attempt that fails
5200 authorisation is recorded as a rejected event with those same fields.

5201  Fail: the requirement is not met if a documented authority transfer mechanism produces no log event; if a
5202 recorded event omits any prescribed field; if a recorded value is inconsistent with the invocation; or where a
5203 rejected transfer is not recorded.

5204 Assessment evidence: enumeration of authority transfer mechanisms; per-mechanism log capture; field-by-field
5205 verification record; record of rejected-transfer logging.

5206 6.15 Factory reset and data portability

5207 6.15.0 Overview of requirements addressed in clause 6.15

5208 The present clause specifies assessment criteria for the requirements in clause 5.15.

5209 Table 6.15.0-1: Requirements addressed in clause 6.15

Requirement Profile applicability
REQ-BM-FRDP- 001 MEDIUM, HIGH (if user-modifiable data stored)
5210

5211 6.15.1 [ACC-BM-FRDP-001]

5212 Assessment reference: REQ-BM-FRDP-001.

5213 Assessment objective: verify that the boot manager provides a mechanism that, when invoked by an authorised entity,
5214 securely and permanently removes all user-modifiable data and settings stored by the boot manager and restores the
5215 boot manager to its default state as placed on the market.


5216 Assessment preparation:

5217  Test environment: the boot manager configured with non-default user-modifiable data and settings populated
5218 (boot configuration deltas, user-added trust anchors, audit log entries, any other persistent state outside the as-
5219 shipped default).

5220  Required information: the inventory of user-modifiable data categories stored by the boot manager; the
5221 specification of the default state as placed on the market; the documented invocation interface for the factory
5222 reset mechanism; the authority model for "authorised entity" in the context of factory reset; the description of
5223 the secure removal technique used per data category.

5224  Required tools: invocation tool for the factory reset mechanism; storage-inspection tool appropriate to each
5225 storage technology used (flash region reader, secure-element command interface, etc.); recovery-attempt tool
5226 capable of attempting to read previously-stored values from the underlying storage media after reset.

5227 Assessment activities:

5228  Where the boot manager stores no user-modifiable data or settings, record the requirement as not applicable
5229 and close this assessment per clause 5.1.3.

5230  Populate each user-modifiable data category enumerated in the inventory with non-default values; confirm the
5231 populated values via inspection.

5232  Attempt invocation of the factory reset mechanism by an entity not in the documented authorised-entity scope;
5233 confirm rejection.

5234  Invoke the factory reset mechanism by a documented authorised entity; confirm successful completion as
5235 documented.

5236  Inspect each storage location after reset and confirm: (a) the values populated in step 1 are no longer present
5237 and (b) the documented default state is restored.

5238  For each storage technology used, perform a recoverability check appropriate to the technology (e.g. raw flash
5239 read for flash storage, secure-element residue check for SE-held data); confirm that the populated values are
5240 not recoverable.

5241  Confirm that the default state as placed on the market is itself not removed by the mechanism (the as-shipped
5242 trust anchors, default configuration, and any non-user-modifiable state remain present after reset).

5243 Assessment verdict:

5244  Pass: the factory reset mechanism rejects invocation by an entity outside the documented authorised scope, and
5245 under authorised invocation it removes every enumerated user-modifiable data category from the documented
5246 storage with no recoverable residue, restores the documented default state, and leaves that default state itself
5247 intact. For example, an unauthorised caller is refused, an authorised reset clears the populated boot
5248 configuration, user-added trust anchors, and audit log so that a raw read of the underlying storage recovers
5249 none of them, and the as-shipped trust anchors and default configuration remain present afterwards.

5250  Fail: the requirement is not met if an unauthorised invocation succeeds; if any populated user-modifiable data
5251 category remains present or is recoverable from the underlying storage after reset; if the documented default
5252 state is not restored; or where the default state is itself removed by the mechanism.

5253 Assessment evidence: Inventory of user-modifiable data categories; record of populated values; record of unauthorised
5254 invocation rejection; record of authorised invocation; per-storage post-reset inspection; per-storage recoverability
5255 record; record of default-state preservation.

5256 NOTE: Secure disposal of cryptographic key material is also required by REQ-BM-CP-008 (assessed under
5257 clause 6.7). Where key material falls within the user-modifiable data removed here, its disposal is
5258 assessed under clause 6.7 and need not be repeated.

5288


5289 Annex B (informative):

5290 Security analysis

5291 B.0 Introduction

5292 This annex applies state of the art methodology to identify assets, threats, identify and evaluate risk factors, and define
5293 security profiles applicable to the different use cases identified in the product context. It identifies assets (clause B.1),
5294 risk factors (clause B.2), assumptions (clause B.3), threats (clause B.4), and maps risk factors to use cases (clause B.5)
5295 and security profiles (clause B.6).

5296 Boot managers face unique challenges: pre-OS execution, establishment of platform trust, and extreme product
5297 diversity from 256-byte ROM code to full UEFI systems. This diversity makes requirements based on deployment
5298 scenarios impractical since manufacturers often cannot predict final deployment context.

5299 The standard uses a capability-based model where objective technical features determine which threats are relevant and
5300 which requirements apply. Each product capability has a dual security impact: it introduces an attack surface requiring
5301 protective measures and enables security mechanisms that mitigate specific threats. For example, update capability
5302 enables vulnerability remediation while requiring protection against malicious update injection. Requirements address
5303 both aspects.

5304 B.1 Assets

5305 B.1.1 A-CRYPT: Cryptographic keys and certificates

5306 Keys and certificates establishing trust in the boot chain. Compromise enables signing malicious code as legitimate or
5307 decrypting protected data.

5308  Root verification keys (platform keys, root certificates).

5309  Signature database.

5310  Device attestation keys.

5311  Symmetric encryption keys.

5312  Revocation data.

5313 NOTE: Platform keys require special attention due to supply chain risks including default keys and key leakage.
5314 See T-SUPPLY-6.

5315 B.1.2 A-ROLLBACK: Rollback protection data

5316 Counters and version information that prevent downgrade to vulnerable versions. Compromise enables rollback attacks
5317 where attackers exploit known patched vulnerabilities.

5318  Version counters (monotonic, non-decreasing).

5319  Minimum version numbers.

5320  Anti-rollback enforcement data.


5321 B.1.3 A-CONFIG: Configuration data

5322 Settings that control boot manager security behaviour. Compromise allows attackers to weaken security policies or
5323 enable unauthorised boot paths.

5324  Security policy settings.

5325  Trust anchor configuration.

5326  Boot device selection and priority.

5327  Network boot credentials (when present).

5328  Recovery mode settings.

5329  Debug interface lockdown state.

5330  Parsed input data (e.g. boot images, logo images, UEFI variables, configuration files).

5331 NOTE: Parsed input is attack surface for parser vulnerabilities. See T-INTEGRITY-14.

5332 B.1.4 A-AUTH: Authentication credentials

5333 Credentials controlling access to boot manager configuration and recovery functions. Compromise enables unauthorised
5334 configuration changes and security policy modifications.

5335  Setup/BIOS passwords (hashed).

5336  Administrator passwords (hashed).

5337  Physical presence authentication.

5338  Recovery authentication data.

5339 B.1.5 A-MEASURE: Measurement and attestation data

5340 Records of boot components and configuration for remote verification. Compromise allows attackers to hide malicious
5341 modifications and appear trustworthy during attestation.

5342  Event log.

5343  Measurement metadata (component identities, versions, algorithms used).

5344 B.1.6 A-AUDIT: Audit logs

5345 Records of security-relevant events during boot. Compromise allows attackers to hide evidence of attacks and prevent
5346 detection or forensic investigation.

5347  Verification success/failure events.

5348  Authentication attempts.

5349  Configuration change records.

5350  Security policy violation attempts.

5351  Recovery mode activation events.


5352 B.1.7 A-RUNTIME: Runtime state data

5353 Security state during boot execution. Compromise enables attackers to bypass security checks, manipulate boot
5354 decisions, or enable unlimited authentication attempts.

5355  Security mode state (setup mode, user mode, deployed mode).

5356  Verification completion flags.

5357  Boot attempt counters.

5358  Memory protection configuration.

5359  Boot phase state machine.

5360 NOTE: State transitions are attack surface for privilege escalation. See T-INTEGRITY-15.

5361 B.1.8 A-CODE: Boot manager executable code

5362 The boot manager code itself while executing or staged for update. Compromise provides persistent privileged access
5363 and complete control over boot process.

5364  Boot manager code in writable memory during execution.

5365  Runtime services code (if persisting after boot target handoff).

5366  Update staging area contents.

5367 B.1.9 A-UPDATE: Update packages and delivery mechanisms

5368 Update packages during delivery, staging, and installation, plus update tooling.

5369  Update packages in transit.

5370  Staged updates awaiting installation.

5371  Update signature metadata.

5372  Update verification tools.

5373  Update delivery infrastructure trust anchors.

5374 NOTE: Update tools themselves are attack targets (BIOS Disconnect). See T-INTEGRITY-16, T-SUPPLY-7.

5375 B.2 Risk Factors

5376 B.2.1 General

5377 Risk factors characterise the security-relevant aspects of boot manager deployment. They provide the analytical basis
5378 for mapping of the use cases to the security profiles (clauses B.5 and B.6). Four risk factors are defined. RF-SURFACE
5379 is determined by the product's implemented capabilities. RF-NET, RF-AVAIL, and RF-IMPACT are determined by the
5380 deployment context described in clause 4.3.

5381 B.2.2 RF-SURFACE: Capability-driven attack surface

5382 The set of capabilities implemented in the boot manager determines the attack surface exposed during boot. Each
5383 additional capability introduces interfaces, protocols, or state that an attacker may target.


5384 Table B.2.2-1: Capability-driven attack surface levels

```
Level Description Examples
Minimal Immutable code, no configuration or
update interfaces
```
```
ROM-only, fixed boot path
```
```
Standard Verified boot, update capability,
configuration management, logging
```
```
Updateable boot manager with local interfaces
```
```
Extended Standard plus network boot, remote
configuration, debug interfaces, or
measured boot
```
```
Full-featured boot manager with network and remote
management
```
5385

5386 B.2.3 RF-NET: Network reachability

5387 Network reachability of the boot manager during boot, update, or configuration operations. Elevated network exposure
5388 increases remote attack surface before operating system security mechanisms are active. See clause 4.3.3 for
5389 deployment context.

5390 Table B.2.3-1: Network reachability levels

```

Isolated No network connectivity during boot Air-gapped, internal storage only

perimeter
```
```

```
```

exposure
```
```
Edge devices
```
5391

5392 B.2.4 RF-AVAIL: Operational continuity

5393 The operational continuity expectations for the system in which the boot manager is deployed. Higher continuity
5394 expectations increase the impact of boot failures and constrain acceptable recovery strategies. See clauses 4.4.5 and
5395 4.4.8 for deployment context.

5396 Table B.2.4-1: Operational continuity levels

```

Flexible Downtime acceptable for maintenance
and recovery
```
```
Development boards, consumer devices
```
```
Standard Normal business availability
expectations
```
```
Office equipment, personal computing
```
```
Critical Continuous operation required; boot
failure causes safety impact or critical
service disruption
```
```
Medical devices, industrial control,
telecommunications infrastructure
```
5397

5398 B.2.5 RF-IMPACT: Compromise severity

5399 The severity of consequences if the boot manager is compromised, considering data sensitivity, safety implications, and
5400 downstream effects on other system components. See clauses 4.4.5 and 4.4.8 for deployment context.

5401 Table B.2.5-1: Compromise severity levels

```

operational disruption

data, or critical infrastructure
```
Medical devices, financial infrastructure, government
systems
5402


5403 B.3 Assumptions

5404 B.3.1 General

5405 The security analysis in this annex assumes the following conditions hold. These assumptions describe properties that
5406 the boot manager depends on but cannot itself verify or enforce. Where an assumption does not hold, the corresponding
5407 threats identified in clause B.4 are not mitigated by the present document.

5408 B.3.2 Hardware platform assumptions

5409 AS-HW-1: The hardware root of trust (initial boot code, e-fuses, or equivalent) is correctly implemented and has not
5410 been modified without authorisation after manufacture. [T-PHYS-5, T-PHYS-6, T-PHYS-9]

5411 AS-HW-2: Hardware memory protection and privilege separation mechanisms function as specified by the platform.
5412 [T-PHYS-2]

5413 AS-HW-3: Hardware security components (TPM, secure element, HSM) correctly isolate key material and resist
5414 physical probing at the level claimed by the component. [T-PHYS-3, T-PHYS-4]

5415 AS-HW-4: Hardware debug interfaces (JTAG, SWD) are disabled or protected by the platform when claimed.
5416 [T-PHYS-11]

5417 AS-HW-5: The platform provides sufficient entropy for cryptographic key generation. [T-INTEGRITY-12]

5418 AS-HW-6: The platform provides hardware mechanisms to resist fault injection (voltage glitching, EM interference)
5419 when claimed. [T-PHYS-2]

5420 B.3.3 Process assumptions

5421 AS-PROC-1: The manufacturing environment provisions correct initial key material and firmware. [T-SUPPLY-1]

5422 AS-PROC-2: Development toolchains have not been compromised. [T-SUPPLY-3]

5423 AS-PROC-3: Update distribution infrastructure is operated securely by the manufacturer. [T-SUPPLY-4, T-SUPPLY-
5424 5]

5425 AS-PROC-4: Update tooling is authentic and has not been tampered with. [T-SUPPLY-7]

5426 B.3.4 Boot target assumptions

5427 AS-TARGET-1: The post-handoff stage (operating system, hypervisor, or next-stage loader) implements security
5428 properties consistent with the declared use case, or another verification mechanism takes over at handoff. Applies to all
5429 use cases.

5430 AS-TARGET-2: For UC-IMM, the post-handoff stage maintains equivalent immutability, or the boot target itself is
5431 immutable. Where this assumption does not hold, the absence of post-deployment remediation that defines UC-IMM's
5432 risk posture extends only to the boot manager and not to the running system.


5433 B.4 Threats

5434 B.4.1 Security property impacts

5435 B.4.1.1 General

5436 Boot managers present unique risks due to their privileged position, persistence, invisibility, and role as trust
5437 foundation:

5438  Privileged position: Operates at highest privilege level with direct hardware access.

5439  Persistence: Survives OS reinstall and traditional security remediation.

5440  Invisibility: Executes below OS visibility and security tools.

5441  Trust establishment: Forms the foundation for all subsequent security decisions

5442 These characteristics mean boot manager compromises have disproportionate impact compared to application or
5443 OS-level compromises. Different capabilities introduce different threat exposures.

5444 B.4.1.2 Confidentiality

5445 The confidential information that the bootloader may have access to include the storage encryption keys, network
5446 access keys, and the user or device identity. This information may be stored in non-volatile storage, in a trusted
5447 hardware element, or retrieved from another system as part of a remote attestation.

5448 If this data is stored in clear text in non-volatile storage, a local attacker may be able to gain access to the confidential
5449 information. This sort of storage is only suggested for use cases where physical access is protected by other means.

5450 Even if the confidential data is stored in a trusted hardware component, the local bus that connects the bootloader to the
5451 external hardware may be compromised by a local attacker. In some cases, the secrets are returned to the bootloader in
5452 plain text on the bus, putting them at risk of disclosure.

5453 If the secrets are encrypted on the bus, but the measurements from the bootloader to the trusted hardware component are
5454 not, the device may be susceptible to a replay attack leading to disclosure of the secrets.

5455 If the devices on the local bus are not authenticated in some way, a local attacker might be able to install an interposer
5456 to intercept the measurements and modify them, similar to the replay attack, to reveal the secrets.

5457 If the attacker can downgrade from verified to measured boot, they should not be able to unseal confidential data since
5458 the configuration measurements will not match, but they might be able to present an authentic looking authentication
5459 screen to the user and trick them into revealing recovery or other secrets.

5460 During a remote attestation, an attacker may be able to force a protocol downgrade that could lead to a disclosure of
5461 user identity or the returned secrets.

5462 A loss of confidentiality of disk encryption keys could lead to a larger loss of confidentiality of the disk contents, as
5463 well as could be leveraged to a persistent loss of integrity in the operating system.

5464 B.4.1.3 Integrity

5465 Integrity for the bootloader means that the OS that it hands control to is the one that the system's owner intends, that the
5466 system is configured as intended, and any hardware measurements correctly reflect this configuration. Any attack that
5467 compromises integrity can also compromise availability and confidentiality, and potentially compromise the
5468 availability, confidentiality and integrity of the operating system that it loads.

5469 An attacker that can modify the bootloader configuration can lead to a loss of integrity, such as by changing the
5470 verification keys to load an attacker signed operating system or enabling a debug mode that does not perform validation.

5471 An attacker that can force the bootloader to execute untrusted code, through misconfiguration or other means such as
5472 TOCTOU, can lead to a loss of integrity.


5473 An attacker might be able to modify measurements when they are being sent to the trusted hardware element, leading to
5474 a failure of integrity of the measurements, which could lead to faked attestations.

5475 An attacker might rollback the system configuration to an older, vulnerable but still signed version that could be
5476 exploited to compromise integrity unless there are rollback protections.

5477 Additionally, some attacks on bootloader integrity can lead to persistence in flash, disk, or other storage, allowing the
5478 attacker to compromise the integrity of not only the current boot, but all future boots as well.

5479 Attacks on bootloader runtime services from the operating system or from a hypervisor guest are also a potential attack
5480 on overall system integrity since they often have elevated privilege levels above the hypervisor itself. This is another
5481 means that an attacker on the bootloader could gain persistence on the system after the bootloader has passed control to
5482 the operating system.

5483 Audit and security event logs may be targeted by attackers to hide evidence of boot compromise. Loss of audit log
5484 integrity prevents forensic investigation and attack detection.

5485 B.4.1.4 Availability

5486 If an attacker changes any of the boot configuration in a verified boot system, the device may no longer boot and might
5487 not be accessible by the user. Depending on when during the boot process the configuration verification fails,
5488 communicating the nature of the failure to the user may be challenging. System designers should consider recovery
5489 flows for re-establishing trust in the device if the bootloader verification fails.

5490 Corruption of rollback protection, measurement data, or runtime state can cause boot failures. Critical asset
5491 unavailability can render the system unbootable, creating support and recovery challenges.

5492 B.4.1.5 Impact of other devices

5493 Integrity failures during the bootloader process can leave the attacker in a position to interfere with other devices on the
5494 network or future components in the boot chain.

5495 Availability failures could lead to a boot loop where the bootloader continuously tries to authenticate with a remote
5496 server.

5497 B.4.2 Threat identification methodology

5498 B.4.2.0 Introduction

5499 This risk analysis uses three interconnected elements:

5500 Assets (clause B.1) Nine categories requiring protection: code, configuration, runtime state, cryptographic material,
5501 measurements, audit logs, authentication credentials, update packages and rollback counters.

5502 Threats (clause B.4.3): Six threat categories: T-INTEGRITY, T-PERSIST, T-PHYS, T-SUPPLY, T-NET, T-AVAIL.

5503 Product capabilities (clause 4.2): Technical features determining which threats are relevant and which security
5504 mechanisms are available.

5505 The analysis maps product characteristics to threat exposure:

5506  Which threats become relevant based on technical features.

5507  Which assets are impacted.

5508  Risk implications for each characteristic.

5509 Each product characteristic clause provides:

5510  Relevant threats for each characteristic variant.

5511  Assets affected.


5512  Threat exposure analysis.

5513  Risk implications for manufacturers.

5514 B.4.2.1 Development approach

5515 The threat taxonomy in clause B.4.3 was developed through analysis of documented attacks, security frameworks,
5516 regulatory requirements, and expert review.

5517 B.4.2.2 Threat sources

5518  NIST SP 800-193 [i.10] Platform Firmware Resiliency Guidelines, Appendix A attack scenarios.

5519  Threat frameworks: MITRE EMB3D [i.12], CAPEC [i.11], CWE firmware patterns [i.13].

5520  Documented attacks, for example BlackLotus (CVE-2022-21894), BootHole (CVE-2020-10713), LogoFAIL
5521 (CVE-2023-40238), BootBandit (CVE-2022-34301).

5522  CRA Annex I: Essential cybersecurity requirements for supply chain, updates, vulnerability handling.

5523 B.4.2.3 Categorisation rationale

5524 Six threat categories separate attacks by vector and persistence mechanism. Categories reflect attack mechanisms while
5525 acknowledging sophisticated attacks combine multiple vectors.

5526 B.4.2.4 Limitations

5527 Taxonomy represents threats known at standard development.

5528 B.4.3 Threat catalogue

5529 B.4.3.1 Introduction

5530 This clause provides the threat catalogue referenced by requirements in clause 5. Each threat is identified by a unique
5531 identifier. Threat relevance is determined by capability presence. Threat exposure level is determined by risk factor
5532 analysis per clause B.2.

5533 NOTE: The "Mitigated by" column uses the following markers: REQ-BM-ESR-NNN: Requirement(s) that
5534 mitigate this threat.

5535 Threats marked [HW] or [PROC] are not addressable by boot manager software alone.

5536 B.4.3.2 T-INTEGRITY: Boot integrity attacks

5537 B.4.3.2.0 Introduction

5538 Boot integrity attacks target the authenticity and trustworthiness of boot components, attempting to execute
5539 unauthorised code, weaken security policies, bypass verification mechanisms, or exploit parsing and input validation
5540 weaknesses. Threat exposure increases with RF-SURFACE (additional capabilities introduce verification and parsing
5541 attack surface).

5587 B.4.3.7 T-AVAIL: Availability and resilience threats

5588 Availability and resilience threats prevent successful boot completion, cause denial of service, or undermine recovery
5589 mechanisms that ensure operational continuity. Threat exposure increases with RF-AVAIL (higher continuity
5590 expectations amplify the impact of boot failures) and RF-SURFACE (additional capabilities introduce failure modes).
