5593 NOTE 1: Availability threats often interact with integrity threats (T-INTEGRITY) and persistence threats
5594 (T-PERSIST).

5595 NOTE 2: Many availability protections are reliability features (timeouts, retries, fallbacks) rather than direct
5596 security countermeasures. These requirements support recovery from attacks but are not mitigations in
5597 themselves.

5598 B.5 Mapping of risk factors to use cases

5599 Table B.5-1 maps the risk factors defined in clause B.2 to the use cases defined in clause 4.6. Values reflect typical
5600 deployments. Actual values for a specific product may vary within the use case.

5601 NOTE: The mappings in this clause are informative. They support the rationale for the use case definitions in
5602 clause 4.6 and the security profiles in clause B.6, but do not in themselves impose requirements on the
5603 boot manager.

5604 Table B.5-1: Risk factor mapping to use cases

Risk factor UC-IMM UC-VER UC-HW
RF-SURFACE Minimal Standard Standard
RF-NET Isolated varies varies
RF-AVAIL Flexible varies varies
RF-IMPACT Limited varies Critical
NOTE 1: "varies" indicates that the risk factor is determined by the deployment context of the
device in which the boot manager is integrated, not by the boot manager product
itself.
NOTE 2: For UC-HW, RF-AVAIL is marked "varies" to reflect that the use case with
hardware-rooted trust can apply to devices that are critical in compromise impact
(RF-IMPACT) without requiring the highest availability expectations. Examples
include high-assurance personal computing devices and certain medical devices
where compromise impact is severe but continuous operation is not required.
5605


5606 B.6 Mapping of risk factors to security profiles

5607 B.6.1 General

5608 The security profiles are derived from the risk factor analysis in B.5. This clause documents the rationale for associating
5609 each use case with its security profile.

5610 B.6.2 UC-IMM: LOW

5611 UC-IMM products have minimal attack surface (RF-SURFACE: Minimal).

5612 The absence of update, network boot, and configuration capabilities eliminates entire threat categories (T-NET, T-
5613 AVAIL-1, T-INTEGRITY-3, T-INTEGRITY-20/21/22).

5614 The residual risk is vulnerability accumulation without remediation capability, accepted because the minimal attack
5615 surface limits exploitability. Security profile LOW is appropriate.

5616 B.6.3 UC-VER: MEDIUM

5617 UC-VER products have standard attack surface (RF-SURFACE: Standard).

5618 Verified boot detects and refuses execution of bootkit-installed components covered by T-INTEGRITY-1/2 and
5619 T-PERSIST-1/2.

5620 Update capability mitigates long-term vulnerability accumulation but introduces T-INTEGRITY-3 and
5621 T-SUPPLY-4/5/7. Logging enables post-incident analysis.

5622 Key provisioning supports trust anchor lifecycle management. The balance of mitigation and introduced risk places
5623 UC-VER above LOW.

5624 Environmental factors (RF-NET, RF-AVAIL, RF-IMPACT) vary by deployment but do not change the security profile.
5625 They are addressed through functional capability requirements triggered when the corresponding capability is present.
5626 Security profile MEDIUM is appropriate.

5627 B.6.4 UC-HW: HIGH

5628 UC-HW products add hardware-backed key protection to UC-VER capabilities. This addresses T-INTEGRITY-10
5629 (software key extraction) which UC-VER cannot mitigate.

5630 Hardware security reduces software-only attack surface against the root of trust to physical attacks requiring specialist
5631 equipment.

5632 Typical deployments have critical impact expectations (RF-IMPACT: Critical), while availability expectations vary by
5633 deployment context. The combination of elevated impact and the hardware assurance described above justifies the
5634 highest assessment depth, independent of the availability expectation. Security profile HIGH is appropriate.

5641

5642 NOTE: Security testing evidence applies to all profiles (LOW, MEDIUM, HIGH) and is addressed through the
5643 conformity assessment regime in clause 6. Testing evidence requirements are described in C.7.

5644 C.2 Security design documentation

5645 Threat modelling: Documented threat modelling covering all threats in Annex B applicable to the product's
5646 capabilities.

5647 Boot flow and trust boundaries: Documentation of the complete boot flow from power-on to handoff, identifying trust
5648 boundaries between stages and the defence-in-depth approach.

5649 Cryptographic architecture: Documentation of the cryptographic key hierarchy, storage locations, and trust model.
5650 This includes key provisioning, lifecycle management, and identification of trust anchors.

5651 Memory and interface architecture: Documentation of memory layout, protection mechanisms, and interfaces
5652 exposed at each boot stage.

5653 Recovery mechanisms: Documentation of recovery and failsafe mechanisms, including recovery triggers, failsafe boot
5654 paths, and user notification.

5655 Isolation boundaries: Documentation of isolation boundaries between boot components, including the mechanisms
5656 employed and failure isolation properties.

5657 Software Bill of Materials (SBOM): Software bill of materials aligned with the requirements of prEN 40000-1-3 [i.4],
5658 listing all third-party components with version information.


5659 C.3 Physical security documentation

5660 Documentation of physical security requirements when updates are not supported. This covers physical access control
5661 requirements, tamper detection expectations, and compensating controls for lack of update capability.

5662 C.4 Integrity mechanism documentation

5663 Measurement process: Documentation of the measurement process for validation, including measurement algorithm,
5664 sequence, storage, and validation method.

5665 Environmental assumptions without hardware security: Documentation of environmental assumptions for physical
5666 security when hardware security components are not available, including threat model limitations and deployment
5667 restrictions.

5668 C.5 Configuration security documentation

5669 Documentation of security impact for each configuration option, including recommended secure values and warnings
5670 for insecure configurations. Applies to boot managers with configuration capability (all profiles).

5671 C.6 Vulnerability handling documentation

5672 Update procedures: Documentation of update procedures, or explicit statement that updates are not supported with
5673 rationale.

5674 Compensating controls for non-updateable implementations: Documentation of compensating controls and
5675 hardware replacement as the update mechanism when updates are not supported.

5676 End-of-life guidance: End-of-life guidance when vulnerabilities cannot be mitigated for non-updateable
5677 implementations, including decommissioning procedures.

5678 Vulnerability mitigation scope: Documentation of which vulnerabilities can be addressed via configuration versus
5679 code updates.

5680 C.7 Security testing evidence

5681 Evidence demonstrating the boot manager has undergone appropriate security validation.

5682 Signature verification testing: Evidence of testing valid signatures, invalid signatures, expired signatures, and revoked
5683 signatures.

5684 Authentication mechanism testing: Evidence of authentication bypass and privilege escalation testing.

5685 Rollback protection testing: Evidence of rollback attempt testing with older valid images and version counter
5686 manipulation.

5687 Secure failure mode testing: Evidence of testing behaviour under verification failure, resource exhaustion, and
5688 corrupted input.

5689 Input fuzz testing: Evidence of fuzz testing covering parsers for configuration, images, and certificates.

5690 Memory safety testing: Evidence of buffer overflow and integer overflow testing, including static and dynamic
5691 analysis.

5692 Code review: Evidence of security-focused code review.

5693 Architecture review: Evidence of architecture review against the documented threat model.


5694 Binary analysis: Evidence of binary analysis of production builds, including verification that debug symbols and test
5695 code are removed.

5696 Supply chain security review: Evidence of supply chain security review covering third-party components and build
5697 process.

5698 Test coverage metrics: Documentation of test coverage metrics for code, requirements, and threats.

5699 Vulnerability remediation: Evidence of remediation of vulnerabilities identified during testing.


5700 Annex D (informative):

5701 Relation to physical attack resistance standards

5702 D.1 Purpose

5703 D.1.0 Introduction

5704 This annex identifies external standards that address physical-attack-related threats to products with digital elements.
5705 The physical-attack threats applicable to boot managers are catalogued in clause B.4.3.4 (T-PHYS). The present
5706 document does not specify requirements for physical-attack resistance of boot managers.

5707 D.1.1 Component standards: prEN 50765 and prEN 50766

5708 prEN 50765 [i.7] (CLC TC 47X WG 1) and prEN 50766 [i.8] (CLC TC 47X WG 2) specify security requirements for
5709 secure microcontrollers and tamper-resistant security processors, respectively. Clause 8.3.15 (TR_RES) of
5710 prEN 50765 [i.7] specifies tamper- and attack-resistance requirements at the component level.

5711 A boot manager whose security relies on a secure microcontroller or a tamper-resistant security processor inherits the
5712 physical-attack resistance properties of the underlying hardware. The assumption that hardware platform components
5713 meet their applicable component standards is recorded in clause B.3.2 (AS-HW-*).

5714 NOTE: Where no such hardware component is present, the physical-attack resistance of the boot manager is
5715 determined by the protections offered by the platform on which it executes.

5716 D.1.2 Assessment standards

5717 EN 17927 [i.6] (SESIP), clause 7.7 (Vulnerability Assessment), and ISO/IEC 15408 [i.9] Common Criteria,
5718 vulnerability analysis assurance family (AVA_VAN), specify methodology used in the evaluation of physical-attack
5719 countermeasures.

5720 D.2 Threat coverage in the wider landscape

5721 For the threats catalogued in clause B.4.3.4 (T-PHYS), the following external standards address corresponding subject
5722 matter.

5723 Table D.2-1: Threat coverage

```
Threat (B.4.3.4) External standards
Fault injection prEN 50765 [i. 7 ], Section 8.3.15
Hardware tampering and component
modification
```
prEN 50765 [i.7], Section 8.3.15
prEN 50766 [i. 8 ]
Flash / ROM extraction prEN 50765 [i.7] and prEN 50766 [i.8]
Debug interface exploitation prEN 50765 [i. 7 ] and prEN 50766 [i. 8 ]
5724

5725 NOTE: This table is descriptive of the standards landscape at the date of publication of the present document.

5726 D.3 Exploitation mitigation guidance

5727 The present clause provides non-exhaustive informative guidance on exploitation mitigation techniques that may
5728 contribute to fulfilling the requirement in clause 5.13 (REQ-BM-EM-001). Exploitation mitigation aims to ensure that,
5729 where a vulnerability is successfully exploited, the consequences remain limited and controlled.


5730 The objective is to prevent an attacker from extending their control, escalating privileges, or accessing components,
5731 interfaces, or data beyond those directly affected by the original vulnerability. This can be achieved by designing the
5732 boot manager so that:

5733  containment and isolation are applied, for example through isolation or sandboxing of critical components or
5734 processes;

5735  least privilege and resource minimisation are enforced, by reducing the privileges, accessible memory regions,
5736 and data available to each function;

5737  functionality restriction is in place, by limiting the functionality available to compromised components;

5738  runtime protection and integrity enforcement are implemented, such as Control Flow Integrity (CFI), pointer
5739 authentication, or memory tagging, where supported by the target toolchain and platform;

5740  memory protection mechanisms are applied, such as stack protection mechanisms or Address Space Layout
5741 Randomisation (ASLR), where supported by the target toolchain and platform;

5742  side-channel mitigation measures are applied, such as differential power analysis (DPA) countermeasures,
5743 electromagnetic (EM) shielding, tamper detection, and constant-time implementation of cryptographic
5744 operations, where the deployment context warrants and the underlying hardware supports them.

5745 The applicability of each measure to a specific boot manager depends on the toolchain, the underlying platform, and the
5746 operational environment. The product-facing requirement in clause 5.13 (REQ-BM-EM-001) does not mandate a
5747 specific subset of the above techniques but requires the boot manager to implement exploitation mitigation mechanisms
5748 appropriate to the boot-manager execution environment and to the documented threat profile.

5749 NOTE: The exploitation-mitigation guidance in this clause corresponds to control GEC-11 of the generic security
5750 framework in prEN 40000-1-2 [i.5] (clause 5.2.2(k)). As prEN 40000-1-2 [i.5] is not a normative
5751 reference of the present document, the substantive intent of that control is reproduced here as informative
5752 guidance and instantiated as the normative requirement REQ-BM-EM-001 in clause 5.13.

5753


5754 Annex E (informative):

5755 Relation to NIST SP 800-193

5756 E.1 Purpose

5758 Platform Firmware Resiliency Guidelines.

5759 NOTE 1: NIST SP 800-193 [i.10] defines Roots of Trust (RTU, RTD, RTRec) anchored in immutable hardware.
5760 These are out of scope, boot managers consume these roots but do not provide them.

5761 NOTE 2: "Section" references throughout this annex refer to sections within NIST SP 800-193 [i.10], not clauses
5762 within the present document.

5801 Annexes F to J:

5803


5804 Annex K (normative):

5805 Generic cryptographic requirements and assessment

5806 K.1 Cryptography

5807 K.1.1 Requirement

5808 The product's default configuration shall only use cryptographic mechanisms that meet at least one of the following
5809 criteria:

5810 1) ACM-listed: the cryptographic mechanism is listed in the ECCG Agreed Cryptographic Mechanisms (ACM)
5811 catalogue [1];

5812 2) ACM-extended: the cryptographic mechanism is not listed in the ECCG Agreed Cryptographic Mechanisms
5813 (ACM) catalogue [reference] and meets at least one of the following conditions:

5814 a) the cryptographic mechanism is listed in clause K.3.2 as an ACM-extended cryptographic mechanism for
5815 the specific product function(s), following consideration of the criteria specified in item 2.b);

5816 b) where the cryptographic mechanism is not listed in clause K.3.2, the cryptographic mechanism meets all
5817 the following criteria:

5818 i) the cryptographic mechanism, or where applicable the ACM-listed cryptographic mechanism on
5819 which it is based, is not deprecated per the ECCG Agreed Cryptographic Mechanisms (ACM)
5820 catalogue [1];

5821 ii) the cryptographic mechanism has been specified, developed or maintained through a transparent
5822 process by a recognised European, international or sector-specific standards development
5823 organisation, or by an industry specification organisation accountable for the relevant specification,
5824 including ISO, IEC, IETF, IEEE, ETSI, CEN and CENELEC; or the cryptographic mechanism is
5825 listed as suitable in a publicly available cryptographic catalogue maintained by a recognised
5826 national or governmental cybersecurity authority, where the catalogue is maintained under a
5827 documented revision and retirement process, including NIST FIPS and Special Publications, NIST
5828 CAVP/ACVP validation programmes, BSI TR-02102 series [i.18], ANSSI RGS Annex B [i.19],
5829 CCCS ITSP.40.111 [i.20] and ETSI TS 119 312 [i.21].

5830 iii) the cryptographic mechanism is described in a valid, publicly available and uniquely referenceable
5831 specification;

5832 iv) the cryptographic properties of the cryptographic mechanism are known;

5833 v) no known weakness affects the cryptographic mechanism in a way that affects its cryptographic
5834 properties;

5835 vi) the cryptographic mechanism is required for a specific set of product functions;

5836 3) Interoperability-based: the cryptographic mechanism is listed in clause K.4.2 as an interoperability-based
5837 cryptographic mechanism for specific product function(s) and external specification(s) or external
5838 requirement(s).

5839 NOTE 1: The reference to the product's default configuration is intended to define a clear and assessable baseline,
5840 corresponding to the configuration in which the product is placed on the market. The product can provide
5841 several configurations that fulfil the requirement.

5842 NOTE 2: For products supplied as hardware platforms or components to be configured by an integrator, references
5843 in this annex to the product's default configuration refer to the configuration specified for the intended
5844 operational use of the product after integration, including the relevant integration assumptions and
5845 configuration constraints.


5846 NOTE 3: The applicable ACM catalogue version is identified in the normative references of the present document.
5847 The lifecycle treatment of mechanisms affected by ACM deprecation dates, expiry dates, migration
5848 conditions or usage limitations is addressed in clause K.2.

5849 NOTE 4: In this clause, an external specification or external requirement means a specification or requirement that
5850 is imposed on the product, and which requires the use of a specific cryptographic mechanism for the
5851 product to interoperate with an identified system, platform or operational context. An external
5852 requirement can be a regulatory requirement, operational constraint, technical interoperability constraint,
5853 or platform compatibility requirement.

5854 NOTE 5: Inclusion of a cryptographic mechanism under the interoperability-based criterion does not classify that
5855 mechanism as state-of-the-art cryptography.

5856 EXAMPLE: Examples of product functions include secure communication based on TLS 1.3; authenticated
5857 encryption of communicated data based on AES-GCM; storage confidentiality based on AES-
5858 XTS; firmware signature verification based on Ed25519; and key derivation based on HKDF.

5859 K.1.2 Assessment of product cryptographic configuration

5860 K.1.2.0 General

5861 The assessment in clause K.1.2 verifies the cryptographic mechanisms used in the product's default configuration
5862 against clause K.1.1.

5863 For ACM-extended cryptographic mechanisms, the assessment verifies that the cryptographic mechanism is either
5864 listed in clause K.3.2 or fulfils the criteria specified in clause K.1.1 item 2.b. For interoperability-based cryptographic
5865 mechanisms, the assessment verifies that the cryptographic mechanism is listed in clause K.4.2. The assessment also
5866 verifies that the product uses the cryptographic mechanism in accordance with the relevant characteristics, product
5867 functions, use cases where applicable, external specifications or external requirements, and conditions specified in the
5868 present document.

5869 K.1.2.1 Assessment of ACM-listed cryptographic mechanisms

5870 K.1.2.1.1 Assessment objective

5871 The purpose of this assessment case is to verify that cryptographic mechanisms claimed to comply with clause K.1.1
5872 item 1) and used in the product's default configuration are listed in the ECCG Agreed Cryptographic Mechanisms
5873 (ACM) catalogue [1].

5874 K.1.2.1.2 Assessment preparation

5875  Preconditions for the assessment: The product's default configuration shall be used for the assessment.

5876  The documentation shall provide a list of cryptographic mechanisms used in the product's default
5877 configuration and claimed under clause K.1.1 item 1), including the related product function, relevant
5878 parameters where applicable, and the relevant ACM entry.

5879 K.1.2.1.3 Assessment activities

5880 The assessment shall include verification that:

5881 a) each cryptographic mechanism claimed under clause K.1.1 item 1) is identified by reference to a relevant
5882 ACM entry;

5883 b) the ACM entry corresponds to the cryptographic mechanism used in the product's default configuration,
5884 including relevant parameters where applicable;

5885 c) where the ACM entry includes lifecycle information, such as expiry date, deprecation date, migration
5886 condition or usage limitation, this information is reflected in the documentation.


5887 K.1.2.1.4 Assessment evidence

5888 The assessment evidence shall include, as applicable:

5889 a) description of the product's default configuration;

5890 b) list of cryptographic mechanisms claimed under clause K.1.1 item 1);

5891 c) references to the relevant ACM entries;

5892 d) relevant parameters, profiles, cipher suites or configuration constraints, where applicable;

5893 e) relevant lifecycle information from the ACM catalogue, where applicable.

5894 K.1.2.1.5 Assessment verdict

5895  The verdict PASS shall be assigned if the required evidence has been provided, is complete, is applicable to
5896 the assessed configuration, and demonstrates compliance with clause K.1.1 item 1).

5897  The verdict FAIL shall be assigned otherwise.

5898 K.1.2.2 Assessment of ACM-extended cryptographic mechanisms

5899 K.1.2.2.1 Assessment objective

5900 The purpose of this assessment case is to verify that cryptographic mechanisms claimed to comply with clause K.1.1
5901 item 2) and used in the product's default configuration are either listed as ACM-extended cryptographic mechanisms in
5902 clause K.3.2 or fulfil the criteria specified in clause K.1.1 item 2.b, and are used for the claimed product function(s).

5903 K.1.2.2.2 Assessment preparation

5904  Preconditions for the assessment: The product's default configuration shall be used for the assessment.

5905  The documentation shall provide a list of cryptographic mechanisms used in the product's default
5906 configuration and claimed under clause K.1.1 item 2), including the related product function, use case where
5907 applicable, relevant parameters where applicable, and at least one of the following:

5908 a) the relevant entry in clause K.3.2; or

5909 b) evidence that the cryptographic mechanism fulfils all applicable criteria in clause K.1.1 item 2.b.

5910 K.1.2.2.3 Assessment activities

5911 The assessment shall include verification that:

5912 a) each cryptographic mechanism claimed under clause K.1.1 item 2) is either listed in clause K.3.2 as an ACM-
5913 extended cryptographic mechanism or supported by evidence demonstrating fulfilment of the applicable
5914 criteria in clause K.1.1 item 2.b;

5915 b) the cryptographic mechanism used by the product corresponds to the mechanism listed in clause K.3.2 or
5916 described in the evidence provided under clause K.1.1 item 2.b;

5917 c) the product function using the cryptographic mechanism, and the use case where applicable, correspond to the
5918 related product function and use case specified in clause K.3.2 or justified under clause K.1.1 item 2.b;

5919 d) the relevant characteristics, parameters, profiles, cipher suites or configuration constraints of the cryptographic
5920 mechanism correspond to those specified in clause K.3.2 or justified under clause K.1.1 item 2.b, where
5921 applicable;

5922 e) where clause K.3.2 or the justification under clause K.1.1 item 2.b defines conditions or limitations for the use
5923 of the cryptographic mechanism, these conditions or limitations are reflected in the product's default
5924 configuration;


5925 f) where technically feasible, the cryptographic mechanism, parameters and configuration identified in the
5926 documentation correspond to the assessed product configuration.

5927 K.1.2.2.4 Assessment evidence

5928 The assessment evidence shall include, as applicable:

5929 a) description of the product's default configuration;

5930 b) list of cryptographic mechanisms claimed under clause K.1.1 item 2);

5931 c) reference to the relevant entry in clause K.3.2, where the mechanism is listed in clause K.3.2;

5932 d) evidence that the cryptographic mechanism fulfils the criteria in clause K.1.1 item 2.b, where compliance with
5933 clause K.1.1 item 2 is claimed on the basis of those criteria;

5934 e) identification of the related product function using the cryptographic mechanism and the use case where
5935 applicable;

5936 f) relevant characteristics, parameters, profiles, cipher suites or configuration constraints, where applicable;

5937 g) evidence that the cryptographic mechanism is used in accordance with the conditions or limitations specified
5938 in clause K.3.2 or in the justification under clause K.1.1 item 2.b, where applicable.

5939 K.1.2.2.5 Assessment verdict

5940  The verdict PASS shall be assigned if the required evidence has been provided, is complete, is applicable to
5941 the assessed configuration, and demonstrates compliance with clause K.1.1 item 2).

5942  The verdict FAIL shall be assigned otherwise.

5943 K.1.2.3 Assessment of interoperability-based cryptographic mechanisms

5944 K.1.2.3.1 Assessment objective

5945 The purpose of this assessment case is to verify that cryptographic mechanisms claimed to comply with clause K.1.1
5946 item 3) and used in the product's default configuration are listed as interoperability-based cryptographic mechanisms in
5947 clause K.4.2 and are used in accordance with the characteristics, product functions, use cases where applicable, external
5948 specifications or external requirements, and conditions specified in clause K.4.2.

5949 K.1.2.3.2 Assessment preparation

5950  Preconditions for the assessment: The product's default configuration shall be used for the assessment.

5951  The documentation shall provide a list of cryptographic mechanisms used in the product's default
5952 configuration and claimed under clause K.1.1 item 3), including the related product function, use case where
5953 applicable, relevant parameters where applicable, the external specification or external requirement requiring
5954 its use, and the relevant entry in clause K.4.2.

5955 K.1.2.3.3 Assessment activities

5956 The assessment shall include verification that:

5957 a) each cryptographic mechanism claimed under clause K.1.1 item 3) is listed in clause K.4.2 as an
5958 interoperability-based cryptographic mechanism;

5959 b) the cryptographic mechanism used by the product corresponds to the cryptographic mechanism listed in
5960 clause K.4.2;

5961 c) the product function using the cryptographic mechanism, and the use case where applicable, correspond to the
5962 related product function and use case specified in clause K.4.2;


5963 d) the external specification or external requirement requiring the use of the cryptographic mechanism
5964 corresponds to the external specification or external requirement specified in clause K.4.2;

5965 e) the relevant characteristics, parameters, profiles, cipher suites or configuration constraints of the cryptographic
5966 mechanism correspond to those specified in clause K.4.2, where applicable;

5967 f) the conditions or limitations specified in clause K.4.2 for the use of the cryptographic mechanism are reflected
5968 in the product's default configuration;

5969 g) where technically feasible, the cryptographic mechanism, parameters and configuration identified in the
5970 documentation correspond to the assessed product configuration.

5971 K.1.2.3.4 Assessment evidence

5972 The assessment evidence shall include, as applicable:

5973 a) description of the product's default configuration;

5974 b) list of cryptographic mechanisms claimed under clause K.1.1 item 3);

5975 c) reference to the relevant entry in clause K.4.2;

5976 d) identification of the related product function using the cryptographic mechanism and the use case where
5977 applicable;

5978 e) identification of the external specification or external requirement requiring use of the cryptographic
5979 mechanism;

5980 f) relevant characteristics, parameters, profiles, cipher suites or configuration constraints, where applicable;

5981 g) evidence that the cryptographic mechanism is used in accordance with the conditions or limitations specified
5982 in clause K.4.2.

5983 K.1.2.3.5 Assessment verdict

5984  The verdict PASS shall be assigned if the required evidence has been provided, is complete, is applicable to
5985 the assessed configuration, and demonstrates compliance with clause K.1.1 item 3).

5986  The verdict FAIL shall be assigned otherwise.

5987 NOTE 1: The assessment of the external specification or external requirement itself is outside the scope of this
5988 assessment case. The assessment verifies that the external specification or external requirement is
5989 identified in clause K.4.2 and that the cryptographic mechanism is used by the product for the related
5990 product function.

5991 NOTE 2: Documentation review is a minimum assessment activity under the present annex. Functional and/or
5992 resistance testing activities can be added by vertical standards where relevant for the product category,
5993 product function or cryptographic mechanism.

5994 K.2 Crypto agility

5995 K.2.1 Requirement

5996 Where the product's default configuration uses a cryptographic mechanism for which the ACM catalogue, or the present
5997 document, specifies a deprecation date, expiry date, migration condition or usage limitation falling within the intended
5998 lifetime of the product, the product shall provide means for addressing the affected cryptographic mechanism by one or
5999 more of the following:

6000 a) updating the cryptographic mechanism;


6001 b) using another cryptographic mechanism that complies with clause K.1.1 and is not subject to the relevant
6002 deprecation date, expiry date, migration condition or usage limitation;

6003 c) disabling the use of the affected cryptographic mechanism; or

6004 d) limiting the use of the affected product functions accordingly.

6005 EXAMPLE: Where a security mechanism uses a hybrid cryptographic construction, for example a hybrid key-
6006 encapsulation mechanism combining a classical and a post-quantum primitive, the lifecycle status
6007 of each constituent primitive is relevant to the lifecycle status of the construction. Hybridisation
6008 can be used as part of a planned migration strategy where permitted by the ACM catalogue or by
6009 the present document. However, hybridisation does not, by itself, extend the recommended usage
6010 lifetime of a constituent primitive that has been deprecated.

6011 NOTE 1: Where a hybrid cryptographic construction includes multiple cryptographic primitives, the lifecycle status
6012 of each constituent primitive is relevant to the lifecycle status of the construction. Hybridisation is not
6013 assumed to mitigate the deprecation of a constituent primitive unless the ACM catalogue or the present
6014 document classifies the hybrid construction as suitable for the corresponding product function.

6015 NOTE 2: Crypto agility supports maintaining appropriate cryptographic protection within the intended lifetime of
6016 the product, in addition to the capability of updating cryptographic mechanisms on the product in
6017 accordance with secure update and secure communication mechanisms.

6018 NOTE 3: Deprecation information from sources other than the ACM catalogue or the present document can be
6019 considered as input to vulnerability management or security risk assessment but does not by itself trigger
6020 the requirement in clause K.2.1.

6021 NOTE 4: Where the product provides cryptographic capabilities for use by other products, components or layers,
6022 the mechanism required by clause K.2.1 can consist of update, configuration, disabling, deprecation or
6023 limitation capabilities usable by the integrating product, system operator or user, where applicable.

6024 NOTE 5: The applicability condition of this requirement can express exceptions based on product characteristics,
6025 e.g. cryptographic implementation based on immutable hardware co-processor(s) or hardware-based root
6026 of trust, or long-lived silicon used in a long-lived non-updateable environment.

6027 K.2.2 Assessment of crypto-agility

6028 K.2.2.1 Assessment objective

6029 The purpose of this assessment case is to verify whether, where the product's default configuration uses a cryptographic
6030 mechanism for which the ACM catalogue, or the present document, specifies a deprecation date, expiry date, migration
6031 condition or usage limitation falling within the intended lifetime of the product, the product provides means to address
6032 the affected cryptographic mechanism in accordance with clause K.2.1.

6033 K.2.2.2 Assessment preparation

6034  Preconditions for the assessment: The product's default configuration shall be used for the assessment.

6035  The documentation shall identify:

6036 a) the intended lifetime of the product;

6037 b) the cryptographic mechanisms used in the product's default configuration;

6038 c) the related product function(s) for each cryptographic mechanism;

6039 d) the lifecycle information applicable to each cryptographic mechanism, where specified by the ACM
6040 catalogue or the present document, including any deprecation date, expiry date, migration condition or
6041 usage limitation.


6042 K.2.2.3 Assessment activities

6043 The assessment shall include verification that:

6044 a) for each cryptographic mechanism used in the product's default configuration, the lifecycle information
6045 specified by the ACM catalogue or the present document has been identified, where such information is
6046 specified;

6047 b) where the ACM catalogue or the present document specifies a deprecation date, expiry date, migration
6048 condition or usage limitation for a cryptographic mechanism, this information is reflected in the
6049 documentation;

6050 c) where a deprecation date, expiry date, migration condition or usage limitation falls within the intended lifetime
6051 of the product, the product provides an applicable mechanism for updating the cryptographic mechanism,
6052 using another cryptographic mechanism that complies with clause K.1.1 and is not subject to the relevant
6053 deprecation date, expiry date, migration condition or usage limitation, disabling the use of the affected
6054 cryptographic mechanism, or limiting the use of the affected product functions accordingly;

6055 d) where another cryptographic mechanism is used, that cryptographic mechanism complies with clause K.1.1
6056 and is not subject to the relevant deprecation date, expiry date, migration condition or usage limitation.

6057 K.2.2.4 Assessment evidence

6058 The assessment evidence shall include, as applicable:

6059 a) documentation of the intended lifetime of the product;

6060 b) list of cryptographic mechanisms used in the product's default configuration;

6061 c) identification of the related product function(s) for each cryptographic mechanism;

6062 d) references to the ACM catalogue entry or to the provision of the present document used to determine lifecycle
6063 information, where applicable;

6064 e) identification of any deprecation date, expiry date, migration condition or usage limitation falling within the
6065 intended lifetime of the product;

6066 f) description of the means provided by the product, such as update of the cryptographic mechanism, use of
6067 another cryptographic mechanism that complies with clause K.1.1 and is not subject to the relevant lifecycle
6068 constraint, disabling the use of the affected cryptographic mechanism, or limitation of the use of the affected
6069 product functions.

6070 K.2.2.5 Assessment verdict

6071  The verdict PASS shall be assigned if the required evidence has been provided, is complete, is applicable to
6072 the assessed configuration, and demonstrates compliance with clause K.2.1.

6073  The verdict FAIL shall be assigned otherwise.

6074 K.3 ACM-extended cryptographic mechanisms

6075 K.3.1 Requirement

6076 Where the product's default configuration uses ACM-extended cryptographic mechanisms, these mechanisms shall
6077 comply with the ACM-extended criterion in clause K.1.1 item 2.

6078 K.3.2 List of ACM-extended cryptographic mechanisms

6079 No ACM-extended cryptographic mechanisms are specified.


6080 K.4 Interoperability-based cryptographic mechanisms

6081 K.4.1 Requirement

6082 Where the product's default configuration uses interoperability-based cryptographic mechanisms, these mechanisms
6083 shall be selected from the interoperability-based cryptographic mechanisms listed in clause K.4.2 for the specified
6084 product functions and external specifications or external requirements and shall be used in accordance with the
6085 conditions or limitations specified in clause K.4.2.

6086 K.4.2 List of interoperability-based cryptographic mechanisms

6087 No interoperability-based cryptographic mechanisms are specified.

6088
